The VCG structure of M10-J itself reveals four distinct registers: VCG-01 (God-directed), VCG-02 (interpersonal), VCG-03 (deterred/restrained — the conscience-and-will register), VCG-04 (requiring ritual remedy — the cultic-legal register). Within each register the inner-being structure differs: in VCG-01, the act involves the will turning against God's covenant claim; in VCG-02, the act involves a relational harm directed at a person; in VCG-03, the act is averted or protested (conscience-active resistance); in VCG-04, the act has occurred and the cultic machinery responds. Even at this early encounter, wilful sinning is not a simple undivided act but a constellation of related inner events sharing the core of a deliberate will engaging wrongdoing.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — At first encounter the characteristic has two constituent elements visible in the VCG structure: (1) the *moral-unintentional act* (VCG-01: Lev 4:2; Num 15:27/28; Num 22:34; 1Sa 14:33/34) — a person commits a real sin without deliberate knowledge, then conscience engages upon realisation; and (2) the *cultic-purification act* (VCG-02: Exo 29:36; Lev 8:15; Eze 43:20/22/45:18) — cha.ta used for the ritual cleansing of sacred objects, where no personal moral act by the sinner is in view. These two registers share vocabulary but differ in inner-being content. The characteristic's structure is two-register: personal moral (with conscience-engagement post-act) and ritual-cultic (with minimal personal inner-being content).

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The VCG structure reveals three constituent elements at first encounter. (1) *Individual first-person confession* (VCG-01, 23V): the personal conscience naming personal sin — from the single-sentence formula ("I have sinned," Exo 9:27) to the extended multi-dimensional Daniel confession (Dan 9:5/8/11/15). (2) *Corporate confession* (VCG-02, 10V): the community naming shared sin — "We have sinned" (Judg 10:10; 1Sa 7:6; Psa 106:6). (3) *Hollow acknowledgment* (VCG-03, 1V): the verbal form present without inner transformation (Deu 1:41). The three VCGs reveal that confession is not a simple uniform act but a spectrum: from heart-generated genuine individual naming (VCG-01 ideal: 2Sa 24:10), through communal corporate ownership (VCG-02), to the degenerate form where the words are spoken but the will does not follow (VCG-03).

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The VCG-01 corpus (8 verses, single VCG) has distinct constituent elements. (1) *Active false innocence claim*: Jer 2:35 — the person verbally asserts "I have not sinned" / "I am innocent" — the most active and self-aware mode of suppression. (2) *Genuine self-blindness*: Jer 16:10 — the people do not know what sin they committed — a perceptual blindness rather than a deliberate denial. (3) *Habitual sinning without recognition*: Ecc 8:12 — sin repeated a hundred times without the fear of God — conscience-absent by habit. (4) *Knowledge-absence enabling ongoing sinning*: 1Cor 15:34 — "some have no knowledge of God" — cognitive/spiritual ignorance as the conscience-suppression mechanism. (5) *Implicit self-condemnation not consciously held*: Tit 3:11 — "self-condemned" — the conscience operates but its verdict is not consciously received. (6) *Literal non-moral use*: Judg 20:16 — physical missing of target — no inner-being content. These elements represent a spectrum from active denial to passive absence.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The corpus reveals two constituent elements. (1) *Passive non-departure*: the majority of the Kings corpus — "did not depart," "did not turn aside" — presents the characteristic as a failure to move, a remaining-in-place. The will does not actively turn toward sin but fails to turn away from it. (2) *Active clinging and hardening*: 2Ki 3:3 — "he *clung* to the sin of Jeroboam" — the will actively adheres to the sinful course; Neh 9:29 — "stubborn shoulder... stiffened their neck... *would not* obey" — active wilful resistance to turning. The two constituent elements (passive non-departure vs active clinging/resistance) represent different intensities of the same refusal: from staying put (passive) to gripping and resisting (active).

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The corpus reveals three constituent elements. (1) *Hardened will driving repetition*: Exo 9:34 — "he sinned yet again and hardened his heart" — the repeated sinning is linked to heart-hardening, showing that the mechanism of habituation is the will's increasing rigidity in the sinning direction. (2) *Self-reinforcing institutionalisation*: Hos 8:11 — "altars multiplied for sinning, they have become altars for sinning" — the sinful pattern builds structures that produce more sinning; the habitual defection institutionalises itself. (3) *Universal underlying condition*: 1Ki 8:46; Ecc 7:20 — "no one who does not sin" — the universal baseline from which habitual defection grows; all persons have the sinning susceptibility; habitual defection is when that susceptibility has become the settled orientation rather than the occasional exception.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The corpus reveals three constituent elements. (1) *The leader's personal sinning as the source*: 1Ki 14:16 — "the sins of Jeroboam, which he sinned" — the personal Qal sinning is always present alongside the Hiphil causative; the leader is themselves sinning. (2) *The causative transmission through authority*: "and made Israel to sin" — the Hiphil causative is the transmission mechanism; the leader's authority is the channel. (3) *The structural embedding*: 2Ki 23:15 — Jeroboam's altar at Bethel — contagious sin builds physical-institutional structures (altars, high places) that outlast the individual leader and continue to transmit the sinning orientation to subsequent generations. These three elements (personal source + authority transmission + structural deposit) constitute the characteristic's complete form.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — The corpus reveals two constituent elements. (1) *The decisive act of breaking submission*: the pa.sha revolt itself — "rebelled against" (2Ki 1:1; 3:5), "revolted from the rule of" (2Ki 8:20; 2Ch 21:8/10), "in rebellion against" (1Ki 12:19; 2Ch 10:19). (2) *The constructive assertion of independent authority*: 2Ki 8:20 / 2Ch 21:8 — "and set up a king of their own" — the revolt is not merely negative (breaking from) but positive (establishing alternative authority). The two elements together constitute the full act: breaking submission + asserting independence. The 2Ch 21:10 verse adds a third element: *the inner spiritual ground* — "because he had forsaken the Lord" — the political revolt is grounded in the revolter-instigator's own inner abandonment of God.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The VCG structure reveals three distinct constituent elements. (1) *VCG-01 (slander/abusive speech from inner corruption)*: person-directed sinful speech originating in the heart's moral corruption — Mat 15:19; Mar 7:22; Eph 4:31; Col 3:8; 1Ti 6:4; 2Ti 3:2. (2) *VCG-02 (blasphemy as divine-authority claim)*: God-directed sinful speech that usurps divine prerogatives — Mat 12:31; Mat 26:65; Mar 2:7; Mar 3:28; Mar 14:64; Luk 5:21; Joh 10:33. (3) *VCG-03 (blasphemy as constitutive defiance)*: blasphemy as the defining character of the creature entirely given over to anti-God defiance — Rev 13:1/5/6; Rev 17:3; 2Pe 2:11; Rev 2:9. Additionally, Jude 9 and 2Pe 2:11 name the angelic constraint against blasphemous speech, establishing the creaturely boundary.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — The characteristic is constitutively composite — three analytically distinct mechanisms assembled under one characteristic because they share the property of being specific named inner pathways to sin. (1) *Enticement mechanism*: desire-faculty → bait presented → luring → capture (Jam 1:14; 2Pe 2:14/18). (2) *Hypocrisy mechanism*: social pressure → identity-performance adopted alongside others → authentic identity falsified → community corrupted (Gal 2:13). (3) *Apostasy mechanism*: covenantal identity held → departure decision → standing-away-from the covenantal framework (Act 21:21). The composite structure is acknowledged in the definition's triple formulation and in the three cross-cluster flags (M14/M08/M31).

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The corpus reveals a multi-dimensional condition with at least four constituent elements. (1) *Universal scope*: every person without exception is under the condition — Rom 3:9/23; Rom 2:12 — Jew and Gentile alike; Heb 5:3 — even the priest. (2) *Death-consequence*: the condition produces death — Rom 5:12 ("death through sin"); Rom 6:23 ("wages of sin is death"); Eph 2:1 ("dead in trespasses and sins"). (3) *Enslavement*: the condition functions as a master relationship — Rom 7:14 ("sold under sin"); Rom 6:16-20 (slavery to sin); Gen 4:7 ("its desire is for you"). (4) *Deficiency from intended glory*: Rom 3:23 — "fall short of the glory of God" — the condition is not neutral but a falling below what human existence was designed to be.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — The corpus reveals two constituent elements. (1) *The practice-to-slavery mechanism*: Joh 8:34 — the mechanism is the practice of sinning producing the enslaved state; repeated sinning generates the structural captivity. (2) *The universal imprisonment dimension*: Gal 3:22 — the Scripture's imprisoning of everything under sin is a distinct element — not individual practice-to-slavery but a universal structural confinement that applies to all regardless of individual sinning patterns. These two elements address different aspects: the individual's practice producing their personal enslavement, and the cosmic/universal imprisonment that confines all under sin as the presupposition of the gospel.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — The corpus reveals four constituent elements. (1) *Individual liability*: chet (VCG-01) — "each one shall be put to death for his own sin" (Deu 24:16) — personal accountable record; (2) *Collective/cumulative dimension*: 1Sa 12:19 — "we have added to all our sins this evil" — the record accumulates across acts and across the community; (3) *Named institutional pattern*: the Jeroboam-sin legacy (VCG-04) — 46 verses of a named recorded sin-pattern transmitted across generations; (4) *Divine-surveillance register*: VCG-03 — Job's testimony of God actively searching and watching for sin (Job 10:6; 14:16) — the record is under active divine monitoring.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — The corpus reveals four constituent elements. (1) *The inner recognition*: Lev 4:14 — "when the sin which they have committed becomes known" — the sin must be recognised before it can be sought-for; (2) *The seeking act*: Exo 32:30 — Moses going up; Act 2:38 — repenting; Act 10:43 — believing; (3) *The mediatorial mechanism*: VCG-01/03 — the priestly/sacrificial system; VCG-02 — Christ's blood and name; (4) *The divine declaration or grant*: Lev 16:30 — "you shall be clean before the Lord"; Luk 7:48 — "your sins are forgiven"; Col 2:13 — God "having forgiven us all our trespasses."

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — The corpus reveals two constituent elements. (1) *The originating ancestral sinning act*: Isa 43:27 — "your first father sinned" — there is a founding sinful act from which the generational condition begins; (2) *The sustained corporate sinning pattern*: Psa 78:17/32; Isa 64:5 — successive generations continue in the sinning-pattern, deepening and extending the condition. The two elements are distinct: the origin (first father's act) and the continuation (each generation's own sinning within the inherited pattern) together constitute the full characteristic.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — The corpus reveals three constituent elements corresponding to the three VCGs. (1) *The inner moral disposition* (VCG-03): the extreme sinner's total moral character is oriented toward sin — Gen 13:13's "great sinners against the Lord" names an inner orientation of persistent rebellion; (2) *The social-relational status* (VCG-01): the sinner-identity is publicly recognised and carries social exclusion — Psa 1:5; Mat 9:10/11; Luk 7:37; (3) *The constituted/imputed standing* (VCG-02): Rom 5:19 — "made sinners" — the status is formally constituted through Adam's representative act, operating independently of individual moral character formation.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — The corpus reveals five constituent elements corresponding to the five VCGs. (1) *Conscience-recognition moment* (VCG-01): the specific inner event of guilt-realisation after violation; (2) *Accumulation dynamic* (VCG-02): guilt mounting as more violations add to the weight; (3) *Transferability* (VCG-03): guilt as a burden that can be assumed by or redirected to another; (4) *Punitive-consequence dimension* (VCG-04): the specific weight of the penalty-dimension of guilt; (5) *Indelibility and divine perspective* (VCG-05): Jer 2:22 — guilt visible to God despite self-cleansing attempts; Isa 6:7 — the removal of guilt through divine action.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — The corpus reveals eight constituent elements corresponding to the eight VCGs. (1) *Priestly cultic bearing* (VCG-01 — 17V): the institutional mechanism for iniquity's ritual address; (2) *Generational transmission* (VCG-02 — 18V): iniquity crossing family lines; (3) *Divine memory* (VCG-03 — 28V): iniquity held in God's sight and record; (4) *Personal individual ownership* (VCG-04 — 29V): each person's own crime; (5) *Overwhelming accumulated weight* (VCG-05 — 30V): the mounting pressure that exceeds capacity; (6) *Pardon and removal* (VCG-06 — 21V): divine forgiveness resolving the moral debt; (7) *Self-destructive force* (VCG-07 — 15V): iniquity ruining from within; (8) *Heart-seated origin* (VCG-08 — 4V): iniquity originating in the will.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — The corpus reveals nine constituent elements corresponding to the nine VCGs. (1) *Against God in the covenant relationship* (VCG-01 — 27V): rebellion as relational betrayal; (2) *Personal moral breach — Job/Psalms/wisdom* (VCG-09 — 34V): inward-facing honest assessment; (3) *Interpersonal breach between persons* (VCG-08 — 19V): horizontal wrongdoing; (4) *Revolt — inner defiance speaking and acting* (VCG-02 — 7V): sa.rah's vocal and active inner rebellion; (5) *Oppressive weight crushing and enslaving* (VCG-07 — 14V): transgression as a burden-force; (6) *Pardoned and erased by God* (VCG-06 — 13V): divine forgiveness of rebellion; (7) *Accumulated crossing of divine tolerance threshold* (VCG-03 — 13V): the Amos count-formula; (8) *Law-violation — NT parabasis* (VCG-04 — 15V): the knowing-law-crossing register; (9) *Adam-paradigm foundational crossing* (VCG-05 — 5V): the paraptōma first-trespass.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Three constituent elements corresponding to the three VCGs. (1) *Unfaithfulness toward God* (VCG-01 — 57V): the primary covenant-betrayal directed upward; ma.al dominant; (2) *Relational treachery between persons* (VCG-02 — 34V): the horizontal faithlessness between persons within the covenant community; ba.gad dominant; (3) *Constitutional character of treachery* (VCG-03 — 10V): the settled inner character that IS faithlessness — the person who has become a traitor as a defining identity.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — The corpus reveals five constituent elements corresponding to the five VCGs. (1) *Perversity of speech* (VCG-01 — 10V): tah.pu.khah — the tongue/lips as perversity's primary expressive medium; (2) *Perversion of judgment* (VCG-02 — 6V): sa.laph — bribery corrupting the cognitive-discernment faculty; (3) *Perversion of mind, will, and way* (VCG-03 — 19V): a.vah/tah.pu.khah — the twisted inner person whose mind and life-direction are bent; (4) *Sexual perversion and moral degeneracy* (VCG-04 — 4V): te.vel/sur — violation of created/family order; (5) *Moral corruption, decay, and lewdness* (VCG-05 — 25V): cha.val/nav.lut/ftheirō — comprehensive inner decay.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Three constituent elements corresponding to the three VCGs. (1) *Judicial and commercial injustice* (VCG-01 — 20V): the corruption of right process — partial judging, fraudulent weighing, commercial deceit; (2) *Injustice as oppression and harm to persons* (VCG-02 — 33V): the doing of wrong against vulnerable persons — violence, deceit, verbal wrongdoing; (3) *Character of the unjust person* (VCG-03 — 19V): the person-type constituted by injustice — adikos, av.val, a.vil — whose character is the inner condition from which the acts proceed.

---

### T1.2.3

**Question:** What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily engages, and its impact on the person?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Working description: *Wilful sinning is a volitional act of the inner person — primarily located in the will — in which the person knowingly commits a wrong directed against God, another person, or the self. It engages the will as the primary faculty, the conscience as the witness (whether active in restraint, as in VCG-03, or present as the moral register that recognises the act as wrong), and moral evaluation as the standard against which the act is measured. Its impact is rupture: it damages the vertical relationship with God (producing guilt, divine anger, and the need for atonement), horizontal relationships with persons (producing harm and requiring forgiveness), and the person's own moral integrity (self-damage, Psa 51:4; Pro 8:36; 1Cor 6:18). The act creates a debt — moral, relational, and (in the cultic corpus) ritual — that requires resolution.* Evidence: Gen 39:9 (will knowingly refuses); Psa 51:4 (vertical rupture named); Mat 18:15 (horizontal harm requiring confrontation); Lev 4:28/35 (cultic debt and remedy); 1Jo 2:1 (advocate for the sinning believer).

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Working description: *Unintentional sinning is a real moral act committed by a person in the absence of deliberate defiance of a known command — the will acts but not against a consciously registered moral prohibition. The act creates objective moral liability before God (Lev 4:2; Num 15:27/28) regardless of intent. When the sin surfaces to awareness — through realisation, disclosure, or confrontation — conscience engages (Lev 5:5: "when he realizes his guilt... and confesses"; Num 22:34: "I have sinned, for I did not know"). The prescribed remedy (sin offering, priestly atonement, forgiveness declared) addresses the objective moral liability and restores the person's standing. The cultic-purification register (VCG-02) uses the same vocabulary for the cleansing of sacred spaces from cultic defilement, which carries minimal personal inner-being content.* Primary evidence: Lev 4:2; Num 15:27/28; Lev 5:5; Num 22:34.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Working description: *Confession is the conscience-to-speech event in which the inner person names a committed sin as sin — directed toward God, persons, or community, and expressing a genuine or partial inner recognition of moral wrong. It is constitutively a speech-act rooted in conscience: conscience identifies the wrong (2Sa 24:10 — "David's heart struck him"), the will agrees to name it (1Ch 21:17 — "It is I who have sinned"), and the mouth speaks it (Luk 15:21 — "I have sinned against heaven and before you"). Genuine confession is followed by a plea for forgiveness, a reorientation of the will, or both (Num 21:7 — confession + intercession request; 2Sa 24:10 — confession + "please take away the iniquity"). Hollow confession (VCG-03) produces the verbal form without this inner reorientation (Deu 1:41).*

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Working description: *Conscience suppression is the inner condition in which the person's moral-witness faculty (conscience) fails to register, actively denies, or refuses to acknowledge their own sinful state. The suppression operates in three modes: active verbal denial of sin (Jer 2:35 — "I have not sinned"), genuine epistemic self-blindness (Jer 16:10 — "what sin have we committed?"), and habituated absence of the fear of God producing persistent sinning without inner recognition (Ecc 8:12; 1Cor 15:34). The person may be objectively sinful (Jer 2:35 — God will bring them to judgment; Tit 3:11 — self-condemned) while subjectively claiming innocence or remaining unaware of their condition. The characteristic is the inverse of CHAR-3 (Confession): where confession voices the conscience's verdict, conscience suppression silences or falsifies it.*

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Working description: *Refusal to repent is the sustained volitional condition in which the will persistently declines to turn from a sinful course that the person knows they are called to forsake. The characteristic is constituted by a series of non-departures — each moment the will could turn and does not — accumulating into a settled inner disposition of remaining on the sinful path. It ranges from passive non-departure (the Kings who "did not depart from" the sins of Jeroboam — 2Ki 13:2/11/14:24) to active clinging (2Ki 3:3 — "clung to the sin") to bodily-metaphor hardening (Neh 9:29 — "stubborn shoulder... stiffened neck"). In the NT, it reaches its sharpest form as deliberate ongoing sinning after knowledge of truth (Heb 10:26). The primary faculty is the will; the primary location is the heart in its incomplete-commitment mode (2Ki 10:31 — "not with all his heart").*

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Working description: *Habitual defection is the settled condition of the will in which sinning has become the default directional pattern rather than the episodic exception. It is characterised by: the person-type terms of the sinner (*hachotet*) as a constituted moral identity (Ecc 7:26; 9:2/18; Pro 11:31/13:22); continuous-present sinning as the operational state (1Jo 3:6 — "keeps on sinning"); the self-reinforcing dynamic of institutionalised sinning (Hos 8:11 — altars for sinning producing more sinning); and the historical persistence of the pattern across generations (Hos 10:9 — from Gibeah; Heb 3:17 — forty years). The characteristic is distinct from the single act (CHAR-1) and from the specific volitional refusal to turn (CHAR-5): it is what those characteristics produce when sustained — a formed inner disposition that requires no new decision to sin, because sinning has become the will's operational default.*

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Working description: *Contagious sin is the inner moral dynamic in which a leader's personal sinful commitment is transmitted to the community under their authority through the exercise of that authority. The transmission mechanism is the Hiphil causative: the leader does not merely sin themselves (Qal) but causes others to sin (Hiphil). The source is always the leader's inner will committed to the sinful course (Jeroboam "walked in the way" — 1Ki 16:26; kings "walked in his sin" — 1Ki 15:26); the channel is the authority relationship ("I exalted you... leader over my people" — 1Ki 16:2); the result is the community's redirected inner orientation away from God (2Ki 17:21 — "drove them from following the Lord"). The characteristic operates through three stages: inner source (leader's sinful will) → authority transmission (Hiphil causative) → structural deposit (altars, institutions — 2Ki 23:15 — that embed and perpetuate the transmitted orientation).*

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Working description: *Political revolt (CHAR-8) is the decisive volitional act of breaking submission to an established governing authority, expressed through the pa.sha (H6586) political-revolt register. The act involves both negative departure from governing submission (rebelling from, revolting from — 2Ki 8:20/22; 2Ch 21:8/10) and positive assertion of independent authority (setting up a king of their own — 2Ki 8:20). The characteristic operates in the political domain — governing relationships between peoples and kingdoms — rather than the personal moral domain. Its most distinctive analytical feature is the causal connection to the inner spiritual condition: 2Ch 21:10 links Libnah's revolt directly to Jehoram's forsaking of God, revealing that the inner abandonment of God produces the outer fragmentation of political-covenantal order. The revolt carries the moral weight of wilful transgression (as the pa.sha root confirms) while being expressed in the political register.*

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Working description: *Sinful speech (CHAR-9) is sin committed through the mouth — the externalisation of inner moral corruption in harmful, defaming, or presumptuous speech directed at God or persons. It operates across three registers: (1) slander and abusive speech generated from the corrupted heart and directed at persons (VCG-01 — "out of the heart come... slander," Mat 15:19); (2) blasphemy-as-divine-authority-claim — presumptuous speech usurping what belongs to God alone, treated in the NT judicial context as the charge against Jesus (VCG-02 — "He is blaspheming! Who can forgive sins but God alone?" Mar 2:7); (3) blasphemy-as-constitutive-identity — the creature whose very being is defined by defiant anti-God speech, most fully realised in Revelation's beast imagery (VCG-03 — "full of blasphemous names," Rev 17:3). The primary inner-being locus is the heart (Mat 15:19); the speech is the heart's outer expression.*

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Working description: *Specialised sinful mechanisms (CHAR-10) names three distinct inner pathways through which sin operates: (1) Enticement through desire — the person's own desire-faculty (epithumia) is the hook through which temptation lures and captures (Jam 1:14 — "lured and enticed by his own desire"; 2Pe 2:14 — "hearts trained in greed" as the enticement apparatus; 2Pe 2:18 — enticement targeting those barely free from error); (2) Collective hypocrisy — social identity is falsified through joining in acted performance alongside others, with community-corrupting contagion effect (Gal 2:13 — "acted hypocritically along with him, so that even Barnabas was led astray"); (3) Apostasy — covenantal identity is abandoned through inner departure from the covenantal standing one has received (Act 21:21 — "forsake Moses"). Each mechanism is cross-registered with another cluster: M14 (desire/temptation), M08 (pride/hypocrisy), M31 (faith/unbelief).*

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Working description: *Sin as universal condition (CHAR-11) is the structural inner-being state in which every human person stands — not primarily an act (CHAR-1) or a habitual pattern (CHAR-6) but the ontological condition of being under sin's dominion, falling short of God's glory, carrying a standing moral debt before God, and subject to death as the condition's consequence. The corpus evidences three registers of this condition: (1) Wickedness as constituted moral character — the settled inner quality of evil as a defining identity (VCG-01 — rish.ah, Mal 1:4; al.vah, Hos 10:9); (2) Sin as moral debt requiring divine forgiveness and removal — the standing obligation that the redemptive acts address (VCG-02 — hamartia in the forgiveness register); (3) Sin as an enslaving, indwelling power that rules over the person and produces death — the master relationship that resists the person's own will to good (VCG-03 — hamartia in the power register, especially Romans 5-8). Rom 3:23 — "all have sinned and fall short of the glory of God" — is the definitional summary: universal scope + structural deficiency from the created end.*

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Working description: *Sin as enslaving power (CHAR-12) is the characteristic in which sin operates as an active governing force that masters the inner person's will — specifically through the mechanism of habitual practice producing constitutional slavery (Joh 8:34 — "everyone who practices sin is a slave to sin") and through the universal structural imprisonment that Scripture discloses (Gal 3:22 — "imprisoned everything under sin"). The enslaved person is constitutionally captive: their will is no longer free toward God. The deepest marker of the enslaved condition is allegiance-direction: 1Jo 3:8 — "whoever makes a practice of sinning is of the devil." The liberation from enslavement occurs through new birth (1Jo 3:9 — "God's seed abides in him... he cannot keep on sinning") and through Christ's protective intervention (1Jo 5:18 — "he who was born of God protects him, and the evil one does not touch him"). The characteristic is differentiated by eschatological consequence: 1Jo 5:16 names a form of sin that leads to death as the enslaving power's terminal outcome.*

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Working description: *Sin as divine record (CHAR-13) is the standing objective moral condition in which every human person's sin exists before God as a retained, accumulated account — recorded, named, not hidden from divine memory, and not erased by the person's ignorance or concealment from others. The corpus evidences five sub-registers: (1) Individual moral liability (chet — VCG-01): each person bears their own sin-record; (2) Broad chat.tat record (VCG-05 — 113 verses): sin as an act that creates a moral fact requiring priestly resolution; (3) Cha.ta.ah as objective moral category requiring covering (VCG-02): the record requires a covering act; (4) The Jeroboam-sin legacy (VCG-04 — 46 verses): a named institutional sin-pattern transmitted across royal generations as a defined recorded legacy; (5) The Job surveillance register (VCG-03): God actively searching and monitoring for sin as a divine investigator. The characteristic's definitive image is Jer 17:1 — "the sin of Judah is written with a pen of iron; with a point of diamond it is engraved on the tablet of their heart" — the record is both divinely maintained and internally inscribed.*

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Working description: *Forgiveness sought and received (CHAR-14) is the bi-directional characteristic in which the inner person moves volitionally toward God in appeal for the removal of the sin-record (the seeking dimension), and God responds by declaring, granting, or enacting the covering/removal of that record (the receiving dimension). The corpus evidences this through three registers: (1) The Levitical kip.pu.rim atonement system (VCG-01 — 12 verses): institutionalised annual and occasional seeking through the prescribed sacrifice and priestly mediation; (2) The Levitical sin-offering (VCG-03 — 10 verses): individual and communal seeking through the chat.tat offering system when specific sins become known; (3) Christological forgiveness declaration (VCG-02 — 12 verses): seeking through repentance and faith and receiving through Christ's atoning blood and authoritative declaration. The characteristic's primary anchor is Mat 26:28 — "my blood of the covenant, which is poured out for many for the forgiveness of sins" — naming the definitive once-for-all mechanism that replaces the annual kip.pu.rim cycle.*

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Working description: *Generational sin (CHAR-15) is the corporate moral condition that originates in an ancestral sinning act (Isa 43:27 — "your first father sinned") and is sustained across generations through the ongoing sinning of successive communities who inherit and continue the pattern. The inner person carries a moral liability not only for their own acts but for the accumulated sinning history of those before them. The corpus (8 verses, all cha.ta — VCG-01) evidences three dimensions: (1) The originating ancestral act (Isa 43:27); (2) The persistent corporate sinning pattern sustained across generations (Psa 78:17/32; Isa 64:5 — "a long time in our sins"); (3) The corporate confession that names the condition before God (1Ki 8:47 — "we have sinned"; Jer 8:14 — "we have sinned against the Lord"). God's promise to cleanse the accumulated backsliding (Eze 37:23) names the eschatological resolution.*

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Working description: *The sinner as moral character (CHAR-16) is the constitutive inner moral identity of the person defined by sin — not primarily the act (CHAR-1) or the structural condition (CHAR-11) but what kind of person they are at their moral core. The corpus evidences three registers: (1) The extreme moral type (VCG-03 — 14 verses): persons whose moral character is thoroughly defined by sin — Sodom's "great sinners against the Lord" (Gen 13:13), the Amalekites devoted to destruction (1Sa 15:18); (2) The social-moral category (VCG-01 — 30 verses): the sinner as a publicly recognised class whose status carries exclusion from community and stigma — "tax collectors and sinners" as social pairing (Mat 9:10/11); (3) The constituted/imputed identity (VCG-02 — 20 verses): the sinner-identity as formally established status — "many were made sinners" through Adam (Rom 5:19); "Christ Jesus came into the world to save sinners" (1Ti 1:15). The primary anchor is Rom 5:19 for the constituted dimension and Gen 13:13 for the extreme-type dimension.*

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Working description: *Guilt as inner-being state (CHAR-17) is the conscience's recognition of moral liability before God — the subjective inner experience of being guilty, of bearing a wrong that cannot be hidden. The corpus evidences five registers: (1) The conscience-recognition moment (VCG-01 — 18 verses): guilt-realization arising when a violation becomes known — "when he realizes his guilt" (Lev 4:13/22/27; 5:2/3/4/5) — the inner trigger for confession and restitution; (2) Guilt as accumulated weight (VCG-02 — 19 verses): the mounting, compounding condition — Ezr 9:6 "our guilt has mounted up to the heavens" — guilt accumulating beyond the head; (3) Guilt as transferable burden (VCG-03 — 16 verses): the guilt-weight that can be borne by another — Aaron on his forehead (Exo 28:38); Abigail's self-substitution (1Sa 25:24); (4) Guilt's punitive-consequence dimension (VCG-04 — 18 verses): the a.von/punishment register — Cain's "my punishment is greater than I can bear" (Gen 4:13); Ezekiel's enacted bearing (Eze 4:4/5/6); (5) Guilt exposed, indelible, and removed (VCG-05 — 26 verses): Jer 2:22 — indelible despite soap; Isa 6:7 — taken away by divine act. The characteristic is distinguished from CHAR-13 (the objective divine record) by being the subjective inner experience of what that record means to the conscience.*

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Working description: *Iniquity as accumulated moral crime (CHAR-18) is the inner dimension of accumulated moral wrongdoing — crime in its moral-spiritual sense, the store of inner wrongdoing before God as a measured, generational, heart-seated reality. The corpus evidences eight registers: (1) Priestly bearing (VCG-01 — 17V): Aaron confessing Israel's iniquities over the scapegoat (Lev 16:21/22); (2) Generational transmission (VCG-02 — 18V): iniquity of fathers visited on children to the third and fourth generation (Exo 20:5); (3) Divine memory (VCG-03 — 28V): God's omniscient awareness — "iniquity of Ephraim is bound up; his sin is kept in store" (Hos 13:12); (4) Personal ownership (VCG-04 — 29V): each soul dies for its own crime — Eze 18:20; (5) Overwhelming weight (VCG-05 — 30V): "gone over my head; like a heavy burden, they are too heavy for me" (Psa 38:4); (6) Pardon and removal (VCG-06 — 21V): servant bears/is crushed for iniquities of all (Isa 53:5/6/11); (7) Self-destructive force (VCG-07 — 15V): "ensnare him, held fast in cords of his sin" (Pro 5:22); (8) Heart-seated origin (VCG-08 — 4V): "taken their idols into their hearts... stumbling block of their iniquity" (Eze 14:3/4/7). Distinguished from CHAR-17 (the subjective experience of guilt) by being the objective moral-crime reality that subsists before God whether felt or not.*

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Working description: *Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing (CHAR-19) is the wilful defiance of known moral or covenantal order — the will that knowingly crosses a boundary or breaches a covenant. The corpus evidences nine registers: (1) Against God in covenant (VCG-01 — 27V): "children have I reared... but they rebelled" (Isa 1:2) — relational betrayal; (2) Personal moral breach (VCG-09 — 34V): "transgression speaks to the wicked deep in his heart" (Psa 36:1); (3) Interpersonal breach (VCG-08 — 19V): "love covers all offenses" (Pro 10:12); (4) Revolt (VCG-02 — 7V): "whole head is sick and whole heart faint" (Isa 1:5) — sa.rah's systemic collapse; (5) Oppressive weight (VCG-07 — 14V): "bound into a yoke... set upon my neck" (Lam 1:14); (6) Pardoned and erased (VCG-06 — 13V): "as far as east from west" (Psa 103:12); (7) Threshold crossing (VCG-03 — 13V): "for three transgressions... and for four" (Amo 1:3); (8) Law-violation (VCG-04 — 15V): "where there is no law there is no transgression" (Rom 4:15); (9) Adam-paradigm (VCG-05 — 5V): "one man's trespass" (Rom 5:15) — the foundational boundary-crossing. Distinguished from CHAR-1 (wilful sinning as act) by the emphasis on the knowing crossing of a known boundary, and from CHAR-18 (iniquity as accumulated crime) by being specifically the act-of-defiance rather than the accumulated moral-crime weight.*

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Working description: *Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin (CHAR-20) is the inner disposition of deliberate unfaithfulness — the will that breaks covenantal loyalty, betrays a trust, acts treacherously against God or persons. Three registers: (1) Unfaithfulness toward God (VCG-01 — 57V): the primary covenant-betrayal directed upward — Judah taken into exile "because of their breach of faith" (1Ch 9:1); Saul died "for his breach of faith" (1Ch 10:13); Ahaz became "yet more faithless" under distress (2Ch 28:22); (2) Relational treachery between persons (VCG-02 — 34V): the horizontal faithlessness within human covenant bonds — "guard yourselves in your spirit, and do not be faithless to the wife of your youth" (Mal 2:15); "like Adam they transgressed the covenant; there they dealt faithlessly with me" (Hos 6:7); marital ordeal (Num 5:12/27); (3) Constitutional inner character (VCG-03 — 10V): the settled identity of the betrayer — "the traitors have betrayed, with betrayal the traitors have betrayed" (Isa 24:16); "I knew you would surely deal treacherously" (Isa 48:8). Distinguished from CHAR-19 (transgression as boundary-crossing) by its relational-betrayal emphasis and from CHAR-18 (iniquity as accumulated crime) by its covenant-loyalty dimension. Cross-register flags with M13 (Truth/Faithfulness) and M31 (Faith/Unbelief) travel with all three VCGs.*

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Working description: *Perversion as inner inversion (CHAR-21) is the inner state or disposition of moral distortion — twisting what is right, corrupting what was good, inverting the moral order from within. Five registers: (1) Perversity of speech (VCG-01 — 10V): "perverted heart devises evil, continually sowing discord" (Pro 6:14); "perverted speech" as wisdom's named hatred (Pro 8:13); (2) Perversion of judgment (VCG-02 — 6V): "bribe blinds the clear-sighted and subverts the cause of those who are in the right" (Exo 23:8); (3) Perversion of mind, will, and way (VCG-03 — 19V): "we have sinned and have acted perversely and wickedly" (1Ki 8:47); "twisted mind is despised" (Pro 12:8); "you turn things upside down!" (Isa 29:16); (4) Sexual perversion and moral degeneracy (VCG-04 — 4V): bestiality and incest named "perversion" (Lev 18:23/20:12); "turned degenerate and become a wild vine" (Jer 2:21); (5) Moral corruption, decay, and lewdness (VCG-05 — 25V): "old self corrupt through deceitful desires" (Eph 4:22); "depraved in mind" (1Ti 6:5); "slaves of corruption" (2Pe 2:19). Distinguished from CHAR-19 (boundary-crossing) by operating as inner structural distortion rather than knowing-violation, and from CHAR-18 (accumulated crime) by being the twisting of the moral faculty rather than the accumulated record.*

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Working description: *Injustice as moral failure of right conduct (CHAR-22) is the inner state/disposition of doing wrong toward persons — unjust conduct, unjust character, the moral faculty bent toward wrongdoing against others and against right order. Three registers: (1) Judicial and commercial injustice (VCG-01 — 20V): "you shall do no injustice in court" (Lev 19:15); "till unrighteousness was found in you" (Eze 28:15); (2) Injustice as oppression and harm to persons (VCG-02 — 33V): "in your hearts you devise wrongs; your hands deal out violence on earth" (Psa 58:2); "the unjust knows no shame" (Zep 3:5); "drinks injustice like water" (Job 15:16); (3) Character of the unjust person (VCG-03 — 19V): "dishonest in a very little is also dishonest in much" (Luk 16:10); "the righteous for the unrighteous" (1Pe 3:18). Cross-register flag: M26 (Righteousness/Justice) on all terms — CHAR-22 is M10's entry-point into the justice/righteousness cluster. Distinguished from CHAR-21 (perversion as inner inversion) by its other-directed focus: injustice is always toward persons and against right-order.*

---

## T1.3 — Boundary

### T1.3.1

**Question:** What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The structural opposite is evidenced in two registers. (1) *Integrity of heart / blamelessness*: Gen 20:6 — God says Abimelech "acted from integrity of heart" and intervened to prevent sinning. The opposite of wilful sinning is the will aligned with integrity, acting in correspondence with moral truth rather than against it. (2) *Righteousness / not sinning*: Eze 3:21 — "if you warn the righteous person not to sin, and he does not sin, he shall surely live" places non-sinning and righteousness as a linked opposite pair. Eze 18:4/20 contrast the sinning soul (who dies) with the righteous person. Psa 119:11 ("I have stored up your word in my heart, that I might not sin against you") presents the word-saturated will as the inner condition that opposes sinning. The structural opposites are integrity, righteousness, and will-alignment with God's word.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The structural opposite operates at two levels. (1) At the *intentionality* level: the opposite of unintentional sinning is CHAR-1 (wilful sinning) — the sin committed with knowledge and deliberate will. Num 15:30 (not in scope but contextually adjacent) contrasts the unintentional offering with the "high-handed" sinner who sins defiantly — this explicit contrast in Numbers 15 establishes wilful defiance as the structural opposite. (2) At the *sin/no-sin* level: the opposite is sinless integrity — the person who neither wilfully nor inadvertently violates God's commands. The corpus does not evidence this positive opposite directly within its 18 verses, but Lev 5:5's confession-and-remedy structure implies that the resolved state (forgiven, standing restored) is the positive terminus the characteristic points toward.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The structural opposite is *silence in the face of recognised sin* — the person who knows they have sinned but does not name it. The corpus evidences this opposite through contrast: 2Sa 19:20 (Shimei — "your servant knows that I have sinned... I have come... the first") — the one who comes forward stands in contrast to those who stay silent. The corpus does not explicitly name the opposite within its own 34 verses, but CHAR-4 (Conscience suppression) is the adjacent characteristic that names what happens when the conscience registers sin and is refused rather than voiced. The structural opposite is: sin recognised, conscience engaged, but the speaking withheld — the un-confessing person before a known sin.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The structural opposite is *active conscience* — the inner faculty functioning in its proper moral-witness mode. The corpus names this opposite through contrast: Ecc 8:12 — "those who fear God, because they fear before him" is the structural opposite of the sinner who does evil repeatedly without that fear. 1Cor 15:34 — "wake up from your drunken stupor, as is right" — the command to wake implies the opposite state of wakeful moral alertness. Jer 2:35 — the structural opposite of "I have not sinned" is the confessional "I have sinned" (CHAR-3). The structural opposite is thus: the conscience awake, functioning, and voicing its verdict — which is CHAR-3 (Confession) in its most active form and CHAR-17 (Guilt as inner-being state) in its felt-condition form.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The structural opposite is *repentance* — the turning of the will from the sinful course toward God. The corpus names this opposite through its own negation: "did not turn aside from" (2Ki 10:29) implies that turning aside would be the positive; "would not obey" (Neh 9:29) implies that obeying would be the opposite. Eze 33:12 — "the wickedness of the wicked, he shall not fall by it when he *turns from* his wickedness" — turning from wickedness is explicitly named as the alternative to the sinning that overrides prior righteousness. The structural opposite is the turning/departure that the will refuses — the repentance that, once performed, reverses the condition.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The structural opposite is named in 1Jo 3:6: "no one who abides in him keeps on sinning" — *abiding in Christ* is the structural opposite. Where habitual defection is the settled pattern of ongoing sinning, abiding in Christ is the settled pattern of ongoing relationship that prevents habitual sinning. The Ecclesiastes person-type pair — sinner vs God-pleaser — also names the opposite: Ecc 7:26 — "he who pleases God escapes her, but the sinner is taken by her" — pleasing God (the inner disposition of God-orientation) is the structural opposite of the sinner's disposition. Pro 13:22's implicit opposite is the "good man" who leaves an inheritance: moral integrity and legacy as the opposite of the sinner's redirected wealth.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The structural opposite is the leader whose inner commitment to God is transmitted to the community through the same authority relationship, forming them toward God. The corpus names this opposite through contrast: 2Ki 23:15 — Josiah's demolition of Jeroboam's altar — Josiah is the implicit structural opposite of Jeroboam: a leader whose inner commitment to God drives the dismantling of the sin-transmitting structures. Exo 23:33 — "they shall not dwell in your land, lest they make you sin against me" — the implicit opposite is the community that remains uninfluenced by the foreign sinning direction, maintaining its God-orientation. The structural opposite of contagious sin is contagious righteousness — leadership whose inner commitment transmits righteous orientation to the community.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — The structural opposite is *loyal submission to governing authority* — the prior relationship that revolt breaks. The corpus names this opposite through the negation: "Edom revolted from the rule of Judah" (2Ki 8:20) implies that prior to the revolt, Edom was under Judah's rule in a submission relationship. The "to this day" markers (1Ki 12:19; 2Ki 8:22) name the ongoing revolt as the negation of what the governing relationship would have been. The structural opposite — submission — is the original condition from which the revolt departs. No dedicated positive vocabulary for submission appears in the corpus, but the revolt-language itself implies the prior submission as its structural precondition.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The structural opposite is *edifying and truth-speaking speech* — speech that builds up, honours God, and speaks truthfully of persons. The corpus names the positive opposite through commands of renunciation: Eph 4:31 — "let all bitterness and... slander be put away from you" — implies speech that edifies in place of slander; Col 3:8 — "put them all away: anger, wrath, malice, slander... from your mouth" — implies a speech-set that is truthful, kind, and God-honouring. The structural opposite of VCG-02's divine-authority usurpation is proper acknowledgment of God's authority and identity. The structural opposite of VCG-03's constitutive defiance is the worship and praise that acknowledges God as God.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Each mechanism has a distinct structural opposite. (1) *Enticement*: the structural opposite is the desire-faculty oriented toward God rather than toward sinful objects — desire that draws the person toward righteousness rather than sin. Jam 1:14's "his own desire" as the hook is opposed by the desire that is sanctified and directed toward what is good. (2) *Collective hypocrisy*: the structural opposite is authentic communal identity — living truthfully in community without performing an identity one does not hold. Gal 2:13's "led astray by their hypocrisy" is opposed by the integrity Paul asserts in confronting Peter (Gal 2:11 context). (3) *Apostasy*: the structural opposite is covenantal faithfulness — remaining in the covenantal standing one has received (Act 21:21 — "forsake Moses" opposed by continuing in Moses's law).

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The structural opposite is named across the corpus in three forms matching the three VCG registers. (1) *Against VCG-01 wickedness*: righteousness as a settled identity — the implicit opposite of "the wicked country" (Mal 1:4) is the righteous nation. (2) *Against VCG-02 standing debt*: forgiveness and justification — the removal of the debt condition: Rom 4:7/8 — "lawless deeds are forgiven... the Lord will not count his sin" — the non-counting state is the opposite of the condition of sin counted against the person. (3) *Against VCG-03 sin-power*: the state of being "under grace" rather than "under sin" (Rom 6:14), "freed from sin" (Rom 6:18/22), "dead to sin and alive to God" (Rom 6:11). The fullest opposite statement: Rom 6:22 — "set free from sin and become slaves of God... fruit leading to sanctification... eternal life."

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — The structural opposite is *freedom from sin's mastery through new birth and faith*. (1) *New birth as counter-power*: 1Jo 3:9 — "no one born of God makes a practice of sinning, for God's seed abides in him" — the abiding seed is the structural opposite of the abiding sin-master; the born-of-God condition structurally prevents the enslaving power's hold. (2) *Christ's protection*: 1Jo 5:18 — "he who was born of God protects him, and the evil one does not touch him" — the protective guardianship of Christ is the structural opposite of sin's enslaving mastery. (3) *Faith-promise*: Gal 3:22 — "the promise by faith in Jesus Christ... given to those who believe" — faith as the mechanism of receiving the promise is the structural opposite of the imprisonment that universal sin-condition constitutes.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — The structural opposite is *sin forgiven and removed from divine memory*. Multiple metaphors name it: (1) *Blotting out*: Isa 43:25 — "I will not remember your sins"; Eze 33:16 — "none of the sins that he has committed shall be remembered against him"; (2) *Casting behind the back*: Isa 38:17 — "you have cast all my sins behind your back" — removed from the divine sight; (3) *Casting into the sea*: Mic 7:19 — "you will cast all our sins into the depths of the sea" — the record disposed of permanently; (4) *Covering*: Psa 85:2 — "you covered all their sin" — the record concealed from divine judgment; (5) *The new-covenant promise*: Jer 31:34 — "I will remember their sin no more" — the ultimate eschatological opposite of the divine record.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — The structural opposite is the *unforgiven sin-record remaining in force*. On the human side: the failure to seek — Lev 4:14 implies that when sin "becomes known" and no remedy is sought, the record remains; Jos 24:19 (CHAR-13 corpus) — God "will not forgive your transgressions or your sins" names the condition of unforgiveness. On the divine side: Mar 3:29 — "whoever blasphemes against the Holy Spirit never has forgiveness, but is guilty of an eternal sin" — the single case in the corpus where the seeking-and-receiving is permanently foreclosed: the eternal sin that has no forgiveness names the absolute structural opposite.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — The structural opposite is *generational faithfulness* — a lineage characterised by covenant-keeping rather than sinning. Eze 37:23's positive — "I will save them from all the backslidings in which they have sinned, and will cleanse them; and they shall be my people, and I will be their God" — names the restored covenant-community as the opposite condition: cleansed from the accumulated pattern, restored to God-people relationship. The opposite of the "long time in our sins" (Isa 64:5) is the community that remembers God's ways and works righteousness (Isa 64:5 — "you meet him who joyfully works righteousness, those who remember you in your ways" — the positive foil stated in the same verse).

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — The structural opposite is the *righteous person* as the contrasting moral-character type. Psa 1:1/5 — the righteous man who walks not in the way of sinners; excluded sinners stand opposite to "the congregation of the righteous"; Pro 13:21 — "disaster pursues sinners, but the righteous are rewarded with good" — the righteous/sinner opposition is explicit. In the NT: Mat 9:13 — "I came not to call the righteous, but sinners" — the righteous and the sinner are the two poles; Rom 5:19 — "the many were made sinners... the many will be made righteous" — the constituted sinner-identity finds its direct opposite in the constituted righteous-identity.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — The structural opposite is *the state of being acquitted / not guilty*. Psa 34:22 — "none of those who take refuge in him will be condemned" — the not-condemned state is the direct opposite of the guilty state; Psa 34:21 — the wicked are condemned (guilty); Psa 34:22 — those who take refuge in God are not condemned (not guilty). Isa 6:7 — "your guilt is taken away" — the removed-guilt state is the opposite of the guilt-state. Lev 5:19 — "he has indeed incurred guilt before the Lord" — its opposite is the cleared-of-guilt standing. Ezr 9:15 — "none can stand before you because of this" — the opposite is the standing-before-God-freely state that cleared guilt enables.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — The structural opposite is *moral blamelessness — the state of no iniquity upon the person*. Psa 32:2 — "blessed is the man against whom the Lord counts no iniquity, and in whose spirit there is no deceit" — the not-counted state is the explicit opposite; Jer 50:20 — "iniquity shall be sought in Israel, and there shall be none" — the eschatological opposite is iniquity's total absence; 2Sa 22:24 — "I was blameless before him, and I kept myself from guilt" — blamelessness is the active moral opposite, sustained through self-restraint. Eze 18:20 — "the righteousness of the righteous shall be upon himself" — the righteous person's moral account is the direct structural opposite of the wicked person's iniquity upon himself.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — The structural opposite is *faithful covenant-keeping — the will that remains within the known boundary*. Hos 14:9 — "the upright walk in them, but transgressors stumble in them" — the upright walker is the structural opposite; Psa 32:1/2 — "blessed is the one whose transgression is forgiven, whose sin is covered... in whose spirit there is no deceit" — the no-deceit, no-transgression state; Rom 2:25 — "circumcision indeed is of value if you obey the law" — obedience to the law is the structural opposite of parabasis (transgression of the law); 2Sa 22:24 / Psa 18:23 — "I was blameless before him, and I kept myself from guilt" — the blamelessness of deliberate self-restraint within the boundary.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — The structural opposite is *covenant faithfulness — the settled inner disposition of steadfast loyalty to the bond*. Psa 25:3 — "they shall be ashamed who are wantonly treacherous" paired with "none who wait for you shall be put to shame" — the waiting-on-God is the structural opposite of treacherous waiting-for-self; Psa 119:158 — "I look at the faithless with disgust, because they do not keep your commands" — the command-keepers are the structural opposite; Mal 2:15/16 — "guard yourselves in your spirit, and let none of you be faithless" — the guarded-spirit faithfulness; Pro 11:3 — "the integrity of the upright guides them, but the crookedness of the treacherous destroys them" — integrity (*tummāh* — blamelessness, completeness) is the named structural opposite.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — The structural opposite is *moral straightness — the inner constitution aligned with God's created order*. Pro 8:13 — wisdom's hatred of perversion implies wisdom's straightness as the opposite; Pro 10:31 — "the mouth of the righteous brings forth wisdom, but the perverse tongue will be cut off" — the wisdom-producing righteous is the structural opposite; 2Pe 1:4 — "having escaped from the corruption that is in the world" — escape-from-corruption into divine-nature-participation; Eph 4:22-24 — "put off your old self which is corrupt" contrasted with "put on the new self, created after the likeness of God in true righteousness and holiness" — the new self in God's likeness is the structural opposite.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — The structural opposite is *righteousness/justice as right conduct* (*tsedaqah*/*dikaiosynē*) — named explicitly in multiple verses. Lev 19:15 — "in righteousness shall you judge your neighbor" — the impartial righteousness; Deu 32:4 — "just and upright is he" — the divine character as the standard; Zep 3:5 — "the Lord within her is righteous; he does no injustice" — God's righteousness as injustice's opposite; Psa 119:3 — "who also do no wrong, but walk in his ways" — the upright walk in God's ways as the structural opposite of doing wrong.

---

### T1.3.2

**Question:** What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Wilful sinning explicitly excludes several inner conditions. (1) *Divine restraint / protection*: Gen 20:6 — God's external intervention is what prevented sinning; sinning is what happens when that protection is not operative or is refused. (2) *Intercession*: 1Sa 12:23 — Samuel identifies ceasing to pray for Israel as itself a sin; sinning and faithful intercession stand in opposition. (3) *Covenant faithfulness*: Jos 7:11 — "Israel has sinned; they have transgressed my covenant" — sinning is the act of covenant-breaking. (4) *God's word dwelling in the heart*: Psa 119:11 — the stored word guards against sinning. (5) *Self-restraint of speech*: Psa 39:1 — guarding the mouth resists sinning with the tongue. The characteristic resists and excludes every inner condition that aligns the will with God: covenant faithfulness, stored word, intercession, restraint, and divine protection.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Unintentional sinning explicitly excludes *deliberate defiance*: the bishgagah qualifier (Lev 4:2; Num 15:27/28) specifically marks the act as not arising from a will consciously set against God's command. The Lev 5:1 verse (willful silence of a witness who "knows the matter yet does not speak") sits at the boundary — it involves a person who *knows* but withholds testimony, which approaches deliberate omission. The Pass A meaning marks it as "willful silence" — conscience is engaged because knowledge is present. This borderline verse reveals that CHAR-2 excludes acts where the person's knowledge of the moral reality was operative at the moment of the act. The characteristic resists: deliberateness, defiance, and conscience-active commission.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Confession explicitly excludes and resists three things. (1) *Denial*: confession names the act as sin, which excludes the alternative of denying it occurred or denying it was wrong. The hollow-confession verse (Deu 1:41) shows denial's proximate alternative — not denying the sin verbally but denying it in action by proceeding autonomously. (2) *Self-justification*: the corpus's genuine confessions are notable for their absence of excuse — 1Ch 21:17 ("It is I who have sinned and done great evil. But these sheep, what have they done?") is self-accusatory without self-justification; Luk 15:21 ("I am no longer worthy to be called your son") accepts the full moral consequence without appealing to mitigating circumstances. (3) *Displacement*: Num 12:11 (Aaron — "we have done foolishly and have sinned") and Num 21:7 both own the community's sin rather than displacing it onto others.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Conscience suppression excludes and resists: (1) *Accurate moral self-knowledge*: Jer 16:10 — the people's failure to recognise their sin excludes the self-knowledge that would name it correctly. (2) *The fear of God*: Ecc 8:12 — "those who fear God" is explicitly contrasted with the sinner who lacks this inner orientation — the fear of God as an operative inner state is excluded by conscience suppression. (3) *Confession*: Jer 2:35 — the active "I have not sinned" is the verbal exclusion of what confession would say; the denial explicitly resists the confessional naming. (4) *Shame and awakening*: 1Cor 15:34 — "I say this to your shame" — Paul's appeal to shame presupposes that the shame-response is what the stupor resists; the continued sinning excludes the shame-and-awakening that right moral awareness would produce.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The characteristic explicitly excludes and resists: (1) *Obedience to God's law*: 2Ki 10:31 — "not careful to walk in the law of the Lord, the God of Israel" — law-walking is what refusal to repent excludes. (2) *Complete heart-commitment*: 2Ki 10:31 — "with all his heart" — wholehearted inner alignment is what the divided/non-turned will resists. (3) *Response to warning*: Neh 9:29 — "you warned them in order to turn them back... yet they acted presumptuously and did not obey" — responsive turning to prophetic warning is what the stubborn will resists. (4) *The sacrifice*: Heb 10:26 — deliberate sinning after knowing truth closes off sacrifice — refusal to repent excludes the use of the divine remedy.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Habitual defection explicitly excludes: (1) *Abiding in Christ*: 1Jo 3:6 — the mutually exclusive relationship: "no one who abides in him keeps on sinning; no one who keeps on sinning has either seen him or known him" — abiding and habitual sinning are structural contraries. (2) *Pleasing God*: Ecc 7:26 — "he who pleases God escapes her, but the sinner is taken" — the sinner's orientation is defined by not pleasing God. (3) *Moral legacy*: Pro 13:22 — the sinner's wealth cannot be transmitted; habitual defection excludes the capacity to build a lasting good inheritance. (4) *Escape from moral entrapment*: Ecc 7:26 — the sinner "is taken" by the snare — habitual defection is the condition of being caught rather than escaping.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Contagious sin explicitly excludes: (1) *The community following the Lord*: 2Ki 17:21 — "Jeroboam drove Israel from following the Lord" — following the Lord is what contagious sin excludes from the community's orientation. (2) *The uninterrupted God-human authority chain*: 1Ki 16:2 — God elevated the leader to form his people; contagious sin breaks the intended chain (God → leader → people toward God) and replaces it with leader → people away from God. (3) *The community's moral independence from the leader's sin*: Exo 23:33 — the divine command to prevent foreign nations from dwelling in the land is precisely to prevent the loss of moral independence; contagious sin excludes the community's capacity to maintain their own God-orientation in the face of the leader's transmitted sin.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Political revolt explicitly excludes: (1) *Governing submission*: 2Ki 8:20 — "revolted from the rule of" — the ruling authority's governance is what revolt refuses; (2) *Covenantal political loyalty*: 1Ki 12:19 — "rebellion against the house of David" — the Davidic covenantal authority structure is what Israel's revolt resists; (3) *The divine order that political authority structures express*: 2Ch 21:10 — the revolt is linked to the ruler's forsaking of God — revolt against political authority mirrors and is linked to the inner revolt against God's authority.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Sinful speech explicitly excludes: (1) *Truthful speech about God and persons*: Rev 2:9 — "the slander of those who say that they are Jews and are not" — sinful speech excludes honest identity; (2) *Proper acknowledgment of God's exclusive authority*: Mar 2:7 — "who can forgive sins but God alone?" — sinful speech claims divine prerogatives rather than acknowledging them; (3) *Creaturely constraint in speech*: Jude 9 — Michael withholds the blasphemous judgment — sinful speech resists the creaturely humility that acknowledges speech's limits before God; (4) *Heart-generated righteous speech*: Mat 15:19 — slander comes from the corrupted heart; pure heart-generated speech is what sinful speech corrupts and displaces.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — (1) *Enticement (deleazō)*: excludes the person's resistance of their own desire as the mechanism's entry point (Jam 1:14); excludes the "unsteady souls'" capacity to maintain stability (2Pe 2:18 — targets those "barely escaping"). (2) *Collective hypocrisy (sunupokrinomai)*: excludes honest self-presentation before others (Gal 2:13 — the acted performance replaces authentic identity); excludes Barnabas's capacity for independent moral judgement (he was "led astray" by the collective hypocrisy). (3) *Apostasy (apostasia)*: excludes continued covenantal faithfulness (Act 21:21 — "forsake Moses" = abandon circumcision and ancestral customs).

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The condition explicitly excludes: (1) *Justification by works*: Rom 3:20 — "by works of the law no human being will be justified in his sight, since through the law comes knowledge of sin" — the condition is too total for law-works to remedy; (2) *Self-rescue*: Eph 2:1 — "dead in trespasses and sins" — the dead person cannot self-revive; (3) *Righteousness*: Rom 6:20 — "when you were slaves of sin, you were free in regard to righteousness" — slavery to sin is a total condition that excludes even the possibility of righteousness from within; (4) *Sanctification and eternal life*: Rom 6:22 — freedom from sin is the precondition for the fruit of sanctification and eternal life; under sin, these are unavailable.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — The enslaving power explicitly excludes: (1) *Freedom of will toward God*: Joh 8:34 — the slave to sin cannot freely choose toward God; the will's God-directed freedom is what the enslavement eliminates; (2) *The practice of righteousness*: Rom 6:1/2 — "continue in sin... live in it" — living in sin excludes living in righteousness by the same logic (one cannot simultaneously live in two opposed domains); (3) *The born-of-God non-sinning pattern*: 1Jo 3:9 — "he cannot keep on sinning, because he has been born of God" — the enslaving power excludes this constitutional sinlessness-pattern; those still under sin's mastery cannot produce the born-of-God pattern.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — The divine record explicitly excludes: (1) *Concealment from God*: Num 32:23 — "your sin will find you out" — the record resists the person's attempt to hide it; Job 10:14 — "if I sin, you watch me and do not acquit me" — the record precludes acquittal through divine surveillance; (2) *Transfer of liability to another*: Deu 24:16 — "each one shall be put to death for his own sin" — the record resists being assigned to someone else; (3) *Self-exculpation through prosperity*: Hos 12:8 — "in all my labors they cannot find in me iniquity or sin" — Ephraim's wealth-based self-exculpation is explicitly unfounded; the record persists regardless of material standing.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — The characteristic explicitly excludes: (1) *Self-generated forgiveness*: the priestly mediation (Lev 10:17 — priest bears the congregation's iniquity) and Christ's blood (Mat 26:28) both establish that forgiveness requires an external mediatorial mechanism; self-forgiveness is excluded as an option; (2) *Forgiveness without seeking*: Act 2:38 — "repent and be baptized... for the forgiveness" — the grammatical structure makes repentance the condition of forgiveness-reception; passive receipt without seeking is not evidenced; (3) *Forgiveness for the eternal sin*: Mar 3:29 — the blasphemy against the Holy Spirit resists all seeking; the characteristic cannot operate in that direction.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — The characteristic explicitly excludes: (1) *Belief in God's wonders*: Psa 78:32 — "they still sinned; despite his wonders, they did not believe" — the persistent sinning is rooted in unbelief; belief in God's demonstrated power is what the sinning-pattern resists; (2) *Response to God's provision*: Psa 78:17 — "sinned still more against him, rebelling against the Most High in the desert" — the rebellion is against God's own desert provision; the sinning-pattern resists gratitude and appropriate response; (3) *Learning from the ancestral warning*: Isa 43:27 — the first father's sinning named as Israel's starting-point implies the warning that the pattern carries and which each generation resists receiving.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — The sinner-identity explicitly excludes: (1) *Standing in judgment*: Psa 1:5 — "sinners will not stand in the judgment" — the sinner-identity is incompatible with standing under divine scrutiny; (2) *Membership in the righteous congregation*: Psa 1:5 — "nor sinners in the congregation of the righteous"; (3) *Divine responsiveness*: Joh 9:31 — "God does not listen to sinners" — the sinner-identity cuts off divine hearing; (4) *Association with Christ's holiness*: Heb 7:26 — Christ "separated from sinners" — the sinner-identity is structurally incompatible with the high priestly holiness.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — The characteristic explicitly excludes: (1) *Standing before God*: Ezr 9:15 — "none can stand before you because of this" — guilt-state excludes the capacity to stand in God's presence; (2) *Self-concealment*: Jer 2:22 — "the stain of your guilt is still before me" — guilt cannot be hidden from God by any human self-cleansing effort; (3) *Self-exculpation*: Gen 44:16 — "how can we clear ourselves? God has found out the guilt of your servants" — the divine discovery of guilt forecloses self-justification; (4) *Acquittal without address*: Lev 5:19 — guilt is incurred before the Lord — it cannot simply evaporate; it requires addressing through the prescribed remedy.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — The characteristic explicitly excludes: (1) *Divine acceptance*: Lev 7:18 — offering eaten on the third day is "tainted" and the person "shall bear his iniquity" — iniquity nullifies the acceptance that the offering would have granted; (2) *Covenant standing*: Isa 59:2 — "your iniquities have made a separation between you and your God" — iniquity excludes unimpeded God-relationship; (3) *Answered prayer*: Isa 59:2 — "your sins have hidden his face from you so that he does not hear" — iniquity excludes divine responsiveness; (4) *Standing before God*: Psa 130:3 — "if you, O Lord, should mark iniquities, O Lord, who could stand?" — iniquity, if fully accounted, excludes every person from standing before God.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — The characteristic explicitly excludes: (1) *Covenant membership*: Eze 20:38 — "I will purge out the rebels from among you... they shall not enter the land of Israel" — transgression excludes from the restored community; Eze 37:23 — no longer defiling themselves with transgressions is the condition for becoming "my people"; (2) *Divine pardon in certain cases*: Exo 23:21 — "he will not pardon your transgression"; Jos 24:19 — "he will not forgive your transgressions"; (3) *Wisdom and understanding*: Hos 14:9 — transgressors stumble in the Lord's right ways — the capacity to walk in wisdom is excluded by transgression; (4) *Divine prosper*: Pro 28:13 — "whoever conceals his transgressions will not prosper."

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — The characteristic explicitly excludes: (1) *God's continued presence*: Jos 22:31 — "today we know that the Lord is in our midst, because you have not committed this breach of faith" — the absence of faithlessness is the condition of divine presence; Eze 39:23 — "I hid my face from them" — faithlessness drives God's face away; (2) *Divine blessing and stability*: Pro 13:15 — "the way of the treacherous is their ruin"; Pro 11:3 — "the crookedness of the treacherous destroys them"; (3) *Standing in the covenant community*: Eze 20:38 (CHAR-19 adjacent) — rebels purged from among Israel; 2Ch 30:7 — those who were faithless made "a desolation"; (4) *Reliable relational presence*: Pro 25:19 — "trusting in a treacherous man in time of trouble is like a bad tooth or a foot that slips."

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — The characteristic explicitly excludes: (1) *Wisdom and knowledge*: Pro 2:12 — wisdom delivers from "men of perverted speech" — perversity and wisdom are mutually exclusive; 1Ti 6:5 — "depraved in mind and deprived of the truth" — perversity of mind excludes truth; (2) *Inheritance of the kingdom*: 1Cor 15:50 — "the perishable cannot inherit the imperishable" — the corruptible state is constitutively incompatible with God's kingdom; (3) *Divine favour*: Deu 32:20 — God hides his face from a perverse generation; (4) *Proper function of judgment*: Exo 23:8 — bribery-perversion blinds and subverts what judgment is designed to produce.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — The characteristic explicitly excludes: (1) *Inheritance of God's kingdom*: 1Cor 6:9 — "the unrighteous will not inherit the kingdom of God" — the unjust character disqualifies from the kingdom; (2) *Reliable trustworthiness*: Luk 16:11 — "if you have not been faithful in the unrighteous wealth, who will entrust to you the true riches?" — injustice forfeits the trust that enables greater stewardship; (3) *Standing before the righteous*: Pro 29:27 — "an unjust man is an abomination to the righteous" — injustice makes the person morally repugnant to those who value right conduct; (4) *Functioning as a judge*: 1Cor 6:1 — "does he dare go to law before the unrighteous?" — the unjust are unsuitable arbiters.

---

### T1.3.3

**Question:** What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The evidence marks three clear boundaries. (1) *Not identical to unintentional sinning*: the cultic-atonement corpus (VCG-04) includes Lev 4:22 ("when a leader sins, doing unintentionally") and Lev 5:15 ("commits a breach of faith and sins unintentionally") — this category (CHAR-2 in the programme) is present within VCG-04 as the cultic-remedy context, but the wilful register proper is marked by the knowing, deliberate quality. (2) *Not guilt as an inner state*: the corpus distinguishes the act of sinning (CHAR-1) from the experience of guilt that follows it (CHAR-17 — Guilt as inner-being state). 2Sa 12:13 shows sinning acknowledged, then guilt removed by God; the sequence distinguishes act from experienced condition. (3) *Not refusal to repent*: Hos 4:7 and 13:2 (escalating sinning) border on CHAR-5 (Refusal to repent), but the wilful-sinning register remains at the level of the act committed, not the subsequent refusal of the will to turn from it. The boundary between CHAR-1 and CHAR-5 is temporal: the act of sinning precedes the question of whether to repent.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Three clear boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-1 (Wilful sinning)*: the boundary is at the point of inner knowledge — CHAR-1 requires the person to know the act is wrong and proceed; CHAR-2 occurs when that knowledge is absent. (2) *Not CHAR-3 (Confession)* as such: Lev 5:5 ("when he realizes his guilt... and confesses") shows confession as the *response* to unintentional sinning once awareness arrives — confession is the adjacent characteristic that follows, not the characteristic itself. (3) *Not the cultic-purification process per se*: VCG-02 uses cha.ta in its ritual-cleansing sense for sacred objects — this is not a person sinning unintentionally but a ritual process. The cultic register is included in the sub-group because it shares the same vocabulary and some of the same theological logic (objective defilement requiring remedy), but its inner-being content for persons is minimal.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*
