**[CHAR-3]** E — Three clear boundaries. (1) *Not repentance itself*: confession is the naming of sin; repentance (CHAR-5's opposite) is the turning of the will away from it. They are contiguous: Num 21:7 shows confession followed by intercession request (the turning); Deu 1:41 (VCG-03) shows confession without the turning — the hollow form. Confession can occur without repentance, which is what makes VCG-03's hollow acknowledgment analytically possible. (2) *Not forgiveness*: Eze 33:16 — the cancellation of sin — is the adjacent characteristic (CHAR-14) that follows confession; the verse evidences what God does in response to confession, not confession itself. (3) *Not mere recognition of guilt*: CHAR-17 (Guilt as inner-being state) is the inner condition that precedes or accompanies confession; confession is the externalisation of that recognition in speech. Guilt is the inner state; confession is its voiced expression.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Three clear boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-2 (Unintentional sinning)*: unintentional sinning involves genuine ignorance of the prohibition at the moment of the act; conscience suppression involves ongoing non-recognition of sin despite available moral knowledge (Jer 16:10 — the people have been told God's words; their ignorance is not innocent). (2) *Not CHAR-5 (Refusal to repent)*: CHAR-5 is where the person recognises sin but refuses to turn from it; CHAR-4 is where the recognition itself is absent or denied. The boundary is at the conscience's registration: CHAR-4 ends and CHAR-5 begins when the person knows what they did and is refusing to turn — not when they are denying they did it. (3) *Not simple ignorance*: Jer 16:10's people are not without moral instruction; Jer 2:35's person is actively claiming innocence. Both cases involve a failure of conscience that goes beyond mere lack of information.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Three clear boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-4 (Conscience suppression)*: conscience suppression is where the person does not recognise they have sinned or need to turn; refusal to repent is where the person knows (Heb 10:26 — "after receiving the knowledge of the truth") and refuses. The boundary is at conscience-registration: CHAR-4 = conscience not registering; CHAR-5 = conscience registers (or knowledge is present) but the will refuses to act on it. (2) *Not CHAR-6 (Habitual defection)*: habitual defection is the sustained pattern of sinning without the specific will-act of refusing; refusal to repent implies a decision-point where turning was available and withheld. (3) *Not CHAR-1 (Wilful sinning)*: wilful sinning is the single act of committing the known wrong; refusal to repent is the ongoing decision not to stop and reverse.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Three clear boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-1 (Wilful sinning)*: CHAR-1 is the discrete act of committing a known wrong; CHAR-6 is the settled pattern that those acts have established over time. The single act of CHAR-1 may not constitute CHAR-6; CHAR-6 requires the pattern. (2) *Not CHAR-5 (Refusal to repent)*: CHAR-5 is the specific volitional moment of withholding the turn; CHAR-6 is the dispositional state that makes that refusal natural rather than contested — the habitual sinner may not need to actively refuse to repent because turning has become so alien to the formed will's direction. (3) *Not CHAR-4 (Conscience suppression)*: conscience suppression is the failure of the conscience to register sin; habitual defection is the settled pattern of sinning regardless of whether the conscience registers it. The two can co-exist but are analytically distinct.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-5 (Refusal to repent)*: contagious sin is the Hiphil-caused transmission of sin through authority; CHAR-5 is the individual will refusing to turn. The community members who receive the contagious sin may themselves exhibit CHAR-5, but the contagious sin itself is the transmission event, not the recipient's volitional response. (2) *Not CHAR-6 (Habitual defection)*: habitual defection is the formed dispositional pattern in an individual over time; contagious sin is the causal mechanism through which a leader transmits their sinful direction. The community's habitual defection may result from sustained contagious sin, but the contagious sin is the transmission, not the resulting disposition. (3) *Not mere bad example*: contagious sin involves the authority relationship as the transmission channel — the leader's sin reaches the community specifically because the leader has authority over them. Peer influence without authority is not contagious sin in the CHAR-7 sense; the characteristic requires the Hiphil causative authority structure.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-19 (Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing)*: the same root pa.sha operates in both, but CHAR-8 uses it in the political-military submission-breaking register (peoples and kingdoms), while CHAR-19 uses it in the personal-covenantal moral register (individuals crossing God's moral boundaries). (2) *Not CHAR-5 (Refusal to repent)*: political revolt is a decisive break-away action, not the sustained volitional refusal to turn from sinning; CHAR-5 requires a recognised sinning course that the will refuses to exit. (3) *Not mere political non-compliance*: political revolt involves a positive assertion of independence (2Ki 8:20 — "set up a king of their own") and a decisive relational rupture, not merely passive non-performance of obligations.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not merely offensive speech without inner moral origin*: sinful speech in this corpus is specifically speech that originates in inner moral corruption (Mat 15:19 — from the heart) or constitutive identity (VCG-03). Culturally offensive speech without this inner-corruption origin falls outside the characteristic. (2) *Not every sin that involves speech*: the definition specifies "blasphemy and slander" — the blasfēmia/blasfēmos vocabulary specifically. Other speech-sins (lying, deceptive speech, idle words) fall in other M10 characteristics. (3) *Not the accusation of blasphemy itself*: the false charge of blasphemy against Jesus (VCG-02) is not itself CHAR-9 in its primary form — rather, the accusation reveals what blasphemy is by its false application to the one who cannot blaspheme because he is God.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-1 (Wilful sinning)*: the mechanisms of CHAR-10 name the pathways to sin rather than the wilful moral act itself. Enticement (Jam 1:14) is the luring process before the sinful act; hypocrisy (Gal 2:13) is the identity-falsification rather than a discrete moral act; apostasy (Act 21:21) is the departure from covenantal standing rather than a specific sin-act. (2) *Not CHAR-6 (Habitual defection)*: CHAR-10 names specific mechanisms — enticement through desire, hypocrisy, apostasy — not the settled habituation of the will toward sin. (3) *Not their respective cross-cluster partners*: deleazō is cross-registered with M14 (desire/temptation) — CHAR-10 covers the M10 moral-failure dimension of enticement; M14 covers the desire/temptation dimension separately.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Four boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-1 (Wilful sinning)*: CHAR-11 is the structural condition; CHAR-1 is the discrete act. Every wilful sinning act (CHAR-1) expresses the universal condition (CHAR-11), but CHAR-11 is not reducible to any specific act. (2) *Not CHAR-12 (Sin as enslaving power)*: while VCG-03 overlaps conceptually with CHAR-12, CHAR-11's defining scope is the universal condition affecting all persons; CHAR-12 addresses the enslaving power as a distinct characteristic. (3) *Not the specific sinful act whose forgiveness VCG-02 announces*: VCG-02 names the forgiveness-remedy, not the specific acts being forgiven; it addresses the condition at the level of its removal. (4) *Not guilt as inner-state*: 1Cor 7:28/36 — "you have not sinned" — uses the term negatively to define what the condition is not in specific cases; these negative uses clarify the characteristic's scope by showing what falls outside it.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-11 (Sin as universal condition)*: CHAR-11 is the universal structural condition all persons stand in; CHAR-12 is the specific active governing function of sin as a master over the will. CHAR-11 is the broader category; CHAR-12 names the power-mechanism within it. (2) *Not CHAR-6 (Habitual defection)*: CHAR-6 is the settled dispositional direction of the will toward sin; CHAR-12 is the active power-structure that governs the will and prevents free choice otherwise. CHAR-6 describes the will's direction; CHAR-12 describes the external-to-internal governing force that has captured the will. (3) *Not Eph 4:26's anger becoming sin*: Eph 4:26 — "be angry and do not sin" — is at the boundary of the corpus but addresses the prevention of anger becoming sin, rather than the state of being under sin's enslaving mastery; it is the weakest connection to the characteristic's core definition.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-17 (Guilt as inner-being state)*: CHAR-13 is the objective record before God — the moral fact existing independently of the person's subjective feeling; CHAR-17 is the inner experience of guilt as a felt burden. The record exists whether felt or not; guilt (CHAR-17) is the subjective experience of the record. (2) *Not CHAR-1 (Wilful sinning)*: CHAR-1 is the discrete act of sinning; CHAR-13 is what that act becomes once recorded — the accumulated moral account. (3) *Not CHAR-11 (Sin as universal condition)*: CHAR-11 is the structural condition all persons stand in; CHAR-13 is the specific accumulated record of particular acts within that condition.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-3 (Confession)*: confession is one of the seeking-acts that may accompany forgiveness-seeking (Num 5:7 in CHAR-13's context; Psa 32:5), but it is the speech-act of acknowledgment rather than the full characteristic of seeking-and-receiving forgiveness; CHAR-3 is a component that may precede CHAR-14. (2) *Not CHAR-13 (Sin as divine record)*: CHAR-13 is the record that requires forgiveness; CHAR-14 is the seeking and receiving of that record's removal — CHAR-13 is what CHAR-14 addresses. (3) *Not CHAR-11 (Sin as universal condition)*: CHAR-11 is the structural condition all persons stand in; CHAR-14 is the specific seeking-and-receiving event that addresses one dimension of that condition.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-1 (Wilful sinning)*: CHAR-1 is the discrete individual wilful act; CHAR-15 is the inherited corporate condition within which individual sinning acts occur. Individual wilful sinning (CHAR-1) contributes to and expresses the generational condition (CHAR-15) but is not identical with it. (2) *Not CHAR-11 (Sin as universal condition)*: CHAR-11 is the structural ontological condition all persons share; CHAR-15 is the specific lineage-transmission mechanism. CHAR-11 is broader; CHAR-15 is a specific mode of entry into the condition. (3) *Not CHAR-13 (Sin as divine record)*: CHAR-13 is the accumulated moral account before God; CHAR-15 is the specific generational mechanism through which some of that account is inherited rather than personally accumulated.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-1 (Wilful sinning)*: CHAR-1 is the discrete sinning act; CHAR-16 is the constituted moral identity produced through and expressed in such acts; a person may commit sinning acts (CHAR-1) without yet being constituted as "the sinner" as a recognisable moral type. (2) *Not CHAR-11 (Sin as universal condition)*: CHAR-11 is the structural ontological condition all persons share; CHAR-16 is the characterological identity that some persons have been constituted into or recognised as — not all persons are called "sinners" in the technical VCG sense. (3) *Not CHAR-13 (Sin as divine record)*: CHAR-13 is the accumulated moral account before God; CHAR-16 is the person-type that account has produced — the sinner is the person whose accumulated acts have constituted them as a recognisable moral category.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-13 (Sin as divine record)*: CHAR-13 is the objective moral account before God — the record exists whether the person feels it or not; CHAR-17 is the subjective inner experience of that record — the conscience's awareness of what CHAR-13 holds. CHAR-13 is objective; CHAR-17 is subjective. (2) *Not CHAR-1 (Wilful sinning)*: CHAR-1 is the act that creates the guilt; CHAR-17 is the subsequent inner state that follows the act; (3) *Not CHAR-16 (Sinner as moral character)*: CHAR-16 is the constituted identity of the person defined by sin; CHAR-17 is the inner experiential state of carrying guilt at any given moment — a person can bear CHAR-17 guilt without yet being CHAR-16's constituted sinner-type.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-17 (Guilt as inner-being state)*: CHAR-17 is the subjective inner experience of moral liability — the conscience's felt recognition; CHAR-18 is the objective moral-crime reality before God that subsists whether the conscience registers it or not. Hos 12:8 — Ephraim denies iniquity can be found in him — but the iniquity is real (God knows — Hos 13:12); the denial is a CHAR-17 conscience-failure, not a CHAR-18 non-existence. (2) *Not CHAR-1 (Wilful sinning)*: CHAR-1 is the discrete sinning act; CHAR-18 is the accumulated store of moral crime that sinning acts have produced; (3) *Not CHAR-15 (Generational sin)*: CHAR-15 is the transmission mechanism through generations; CHAR-18 includes the generational dimension (VCG-02) but is not limited to it — it also encompasses individual personal crime (VCG-04 — Eze 18:20).

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-2 (Unintentional sinning)*: CHAR-2 lacks the knowing-deliberate dimension; Rom 4:15 — "where there is no law there is no transgression" — requires knowledge of the boundary; 1Ti 2:14 — "the woman was deceived and became a transgressor" — deception diminishes the deliberate dimension; (2) *Not CHAR-18 (Iniquity as accumulated moral crime)*: CHAR-18 is the accumulated crime-weight before God; CHAR-19 is the specific act of boundary-crossing that generates that accumulation; the two overlap (Exo 34:7 names both) but CHAR-19 is the act while CHAR-18 is the account; (3) *Not mere social offence*: Gen 50:17 — the brothers' transgression required forgiveness; but CHAR-19 is specifically the *knowing* crossing of a moral line, not merely offensive behaviour without moral definition.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-19 (Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing)*: CHAR-19 is the knowing-crossing of a known boundary (law-violation requiring a law — Rom 4:15); CHAR-20 is the betrayal of a relational covenant bond (requiring a prior trust relationship); CHAR-20 adds the intimate-bond dimension — the betrayal of someone who counted on you; (2) *Not CHAR-5 (Refusal to repent)*: CHAR-5 is the ongoing hard heart that refuses to turn; CHAR-20 is the active act of betrayal within an existing covenant; the unfaithful person may not yet have refused repentance — their unfaithfulness may trigger remorse (Ezr 10:6 — Ezra mourned the faithlessness); (3) *Not mere social unreliability*: CHAR-20 requires a covenant context — the prior bond that is broken; Pro 25:19 — the treacherous man in time of trouble — this enters CHAR-20 territory when the trust was covenantal rather than mere social expectation.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-19 (Transgression as boundary-crossing)*: CHAR-19 is the knowing step-over of a known line; CHAR-21 is the structural inner distortion that bends the moral faculty itself — a twisted mind (Pro 12:8) is not primarily transgressing a law but operating from a corrupted cognitive apparatus; (2) *Not CHAR-18 (Iniquity as accumulated crime)*: CHAR-18 is the accumulated moral-crime account before God; CHAR-21 is the inner structural corruption that generates those crimes — the twisted heart (Pro 6:14) that produces continuous evil; (3) *Not purely physical decay*: Several VCG-05 NT verses (1Cor 15:42/50; 2Cor 4:16; Col 2:22; Rom 8:21) address bodily perishability in a cosmological-anthropological sense more than moral inner-being content. These carry cross-register flags (M23/M35) — noted.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Three boundaries. (1) *Not CHAR-21 (Perversion as inner inversion)*: CHAR-21 is the inner structural distortion of the moral faculty; CHAR-22 is that distortion specifically expressed as wrong-conduct toward others; CHAR-21 is constitutive, CHAR-22 is other-directed and conduct-specific; (2) *Not CHAR-19 (Transgression)*: CHAR-19 is the knowing boundary-crossing; CHAR-22 adds the specific other-victim dimension — injustice is done *toward* persons, not merely *past* a known boundary; (3) *Not mere carelessness*: Psa 58:2 — "in your hearts you devise wrongs" — injustice is a deliberate devising; Psa 64:6 — "they search out injustice, saying, 'We have accomplished a diligent search'" — the active, purposeful character distinguishes CHAR-22 from inadvertent wrong.

---

## T1.4 — Modes of Operation

### T1.4.1

**Question:** In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The corpus reveals four distinct modes of operation. (1) *As a willed act of transgression directed vertically against God* (VCG-01): the inner person knowingly crosses a boundary God has set — Gen 39:9 (Joseph's refusal names the act's relational target); Eze 18:4 (the individual soul's sinning carries mortal consequence). (2) *As a willed harm directed horizontally against another person* (VCG-02): the inner wrongdoing is enacted in the relational sphere — "sin against his neighbor" (1Ki 8:31), "sins against you" (Mat 18:15). (3) *As a reflexive act of self-damage* (Pro 8:36; 1Cor 6:18): sinning against wisdom or against one's own body shows the will turning destructively inward. (4) *As an act that grows in intensity and compulsion over time* (Hos 4:7; 13:2): "the more they sinned against me" — a mode where the single act opens toward a pattern. These four modes share the will as the operative faculty but differ in directionality.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Two distinct modes of operation within the personal-moral register (VCG-01). (1) *The ignorance mode*: the person acts without any awareness of the moral status of the act — Lev 4:2 ("sins unintentionally"), Num 15:27 ("sins unintentionally"). The conscience is not engaged at the moment of action because the morally relevant fact is not yet known. This is the purest form of the characteristic: the will acts, but not against a registered moral reality. (2) *The disclosure mode*: the sin becomes known — "when he realizes his guilt" (Lev 5:5), "the sin which they have committed becomes known" (Lev 4:14, adjacent to this corpus), "the sin which he has committed is made known to him" (Lev 4:23). At this point conscience engages and the person moves into the confession-and-remedy sequence. The characteristic thus operates in a before-awareness and after-awareness mode, with the transition point being the moment of disclosure or realisation.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Three distinct modes. (1) *Conscience-initiated, spontaneous confession*: 2Sa 24:10 — "David's heart struck him" — conscience moves inward before any external prompt, and confession follows. This is confession in its purest inner-being form: the moral witness within the person activates unprompted and drives the speech-act. (2) *Externally-prompted confession*: Exo 9:27/10:16 (Pharaoh — confession under plague judgment), Num 21:7 (people — confession under serpent judgment), 1Sa 26:21 (Saul — confession after David's mercy). These operate through external events triggering recognition and naming. (3) *Sustained, extended intercession-confession*: Neh 1:6 ("confessing the sins... day and night"), Dan 9:5/8/11/15 — sustained comprehensive naming across multiple dimensions. This mode is not a single moment but a prolonged practice of naming before God. The three modes differ in origin (inner/external) and duration (single moment/sustained) but share the naming structure.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Three evidenced modes. (1) *Active verbal denial*: Jer 2:35 — "I have not sinned" / "I am innocent" — conscience suppression externalised in a speech-act that falsely claims moral standing. This is the most active mode: the person speaks against the conscience's verdict even where it dimly exists. (2) *Perceptual self-blindness*: Jer 16:10 — the people's "what sin have we committed?" — the conscience is not firing at all; the question is genuine. This is the most passive mode: the moral-witness faculty simply does not produce the signal. (3) *Habituation producing moral stupor*: Ecc 8:12; 1Cor 15:34 — repeated sinning or continued sinning under ignorance of God. This is the developmental mode: the conscience has been progressively suppressed through habit and lack of God-knowledge until it operates at minimal capacity.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Three modes. (1) *Passive continuation*: the will remains on the sinful course by default — the Kings pattern "did not depart from" (2Ki 13:2; 14:24; 15:9) presents an apparently passive mode: the will simply continues without turning. (2) *Active clinging*: 2Ki 3:3 — "he *clung* to the sin of Jeroboam" — the will actively holds the sinful course, making the refusal an act of attachment. (3) *Active hardening against correction*: Neh 9:29 — "stubborn shoulder and stiffened their neck and would not obey" — the will actively resists the call to turn; the refusal is not passive but a stiffening against God's word. These three modes share the common feature of the will not departing, but differ in the will's active contribution to the non-departure.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Three modes. (1) *Will-hardening through repetition*: Exo 9:34 — "sinned yet again and hardened his heart" — the act of sinning again hardened the will's resistance capacity; each repetition makes the will more disposed toward the next sinning act. (2) *Self-reinforcing institutional embedding*: Hos 8:11 — "altars multiplied for sinning, they have become to him altars for sinning" — the sinning pattern builds structures (altars, institutions, practices) that produce more sinning; the inner disposition externalises into structures that feed back and deepen the inner disposition. (3) *Historical-generational entrenchment*: Hos 10:9 — "from the days of Gibeah, you have sinned... there they have continued" — the pattern persists across time and generations as an unbroken inner orientation that each generation receives and sustains.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Three modes within the *leader* (source): (1) *Walking in the sinful course as the leader's own inner commitment*: 1Ki 16:26 — "walked in all the way of Jeroboam" — the leader's personal inner alignment to the sinful path is the prerequisite for transmission; (2) *Misusing the authority position*: 1Ki 16:2 — "I... made you leader... and you have walked in the way of Jeroboam" — God names the misuse of the given authority as the indictment; (3) *Building structures that transmit the sinning*: Jer 32:35 — "they built the high places of Baal... to cause Judah to sin" — the constructive agentive act embeds the transmission into a permanent structure. Within the *community* (recipient): the inner moral direction is bent — 2Ki 17:21 — "drove Israel from following the Lord" — the community's inner God-orientation is replaced by the sinning direction transmitted through the leader's authority.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — The corpus evidences two inner modes. (1) *Opportunistic-volitional mode*: 2Ki 1:1 and 2Ki 3:5 — both Moab revolts occur "after the death of Ahab" — the death of the governing authority creates an opportunity that the subject-people's will seizes for revolt. The inner mode is: assessing the weakened authority position and choosing to break submission at the opportune moment. (2) *Spiritually-grounded mode*: 2Ch 21:10 — Libnah's revolt linked to Jehoram forsaking the Lord — the inner ground for revolt is the ruler's own spiritual abandonment; the revolt appears to arise from the vacuum of legitimate spiritual authority that Jehoram's forsaking created. These two modes represent different inner dynamics: opportunistic calculation vs response to spiritual-authority vacuum.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Three inner modes. (1) *Heart-corruption externalised through speech (VCG-01)*: the characteristic operates as the externalisation of the heart's moral corruption — Mat 15:19 — the heart generates evil thoughts, and slander is their verbal expression. The inner mode is: corrupt heart → corrupting speech. (2) *Presumptuous will claiming divine status (VCG-02)*: the characteristic operates through the will's presumption — claiming for oneself (or treating others as claiming) what belongs to God alone (Mar 2:7; Joh 10:33). The inner mode is: presumptuous will → blasphemous claim. (3) *Constitutive identity-level defiance (VCG-03)*: the characteristic is not an act at all but the creature's total orientation against God — Rev 13:1 — blasphemy as the constitutive character. The inner mode is: total anti-God orientation → defiant speech as the self's expression.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Three distinct inner modes. (1) *Desire-exploitation (deleazō)*: the mechanism works through the desire-faculty — Jam 1:14 — "lured and enticed by his own desire" — the inner motivational capacity is the mechanism's entry point and operative force. 2Pe 2:14 — "hearts trained in greed" — the desire has been deliberately formed toward sin through training, becoming a self-generating enticement apparatus. (2) *Identity-performance (sunupokrinomai)*: the mechanism works through the social-identity capacity — Gal 2:13 — "acted hypocritically along with him" — the inner identity is expressed through a social performance that does not match the true covenantal identity. (3) *Departure from covenantal standing (apostasia)*: the mechanism works through the will's decisional abandonment of the covenantal framework — Act 21:21 — "forsake Moses" names the departure as an act.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Four distinct inner modes from the corpus. (1) *As indwelling power hijacking agency*: Rom 7:17/20 — "sin that dwells within me" — sin operates as an internal occupying force that produces actions the conscious will does not choose; (2) *As a competing law in the members*: Rom 7:23 — "the law of sin that dwells in my members" — sin operates as a counter-authority within the body, waging war against the mind's law; (3) *As a self-activating force exploiting the commandment*: Rom 7:8/9 — "sin, seizing an opportunity through the commandment, produced in me all kinds of covetousness" — sin operates by using God's good law as its instrument of arousal; (4) *As a predatory force seeking mastery*: Gen 4:7 — "sin is crouching at the door. Its desire is for you, and you must rule over it" — sin operates as an external-becoming-internal predator seeking to dominate the will.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Three distinct inner modes. (1) *Practice-generated captivity*: Joh 8:34 — "everyone who practices sin is a slave to sin" — sin enslaves through the repetition of sinning; each practice-act deepens the captivity; (2) *Universal structural imprisonment*: Gal 3:22 — "the Scripture imprisoned everything under sin" — sin functions as a universal enclosure that Scripture declares, confining all persons under its power regardless of individual practice patterns; (3) *Allegiance-capture*: 1Jo 3:8 — "whoever makes a practice of sinning is of the devil" — the enslaving power reaches the deepest constitutional level — the person's allegiance is captured and redirected toward the devil's identity rather than God's.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Four distinct inner modes. (1) *As an internal inscription*: Jer 17:1 — "engraved on the tablet of their heart" — the record operates internally, inscribed on the heart's structure; (2) *As a persistent inner accusation*: Psa 51:3 — "my sin is ever before me" (VCG-02) — the record operates as an inner presence that occupies conscience continually; (3) *As a weight producing physical effects*: Psa 38:3 — "there is no health in my bones because of my sin" — the record operates on the physical body through its moral weight; (4) *As an invisible moral account affecting life-quality*: Jer 5:25 — "your sins have kept good from you" — the record operates by blocking divine blessing without the person necessarily knowing the mechanism.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Three distinct inner modes. (1) *As volitional turning toward God*: Act 2:38 — "repent" (metanoeō — a change of mind and direction); Exo 32:30 — "I will go up to the Lord" — the will's movement toward God as the source of forgiveness is the primary inner mode; (2) *As self-affliction in seeking*: Lev 23:27 — "you shall afflict yourselves" — the Day of Atonement requires inner self-affliction as the seeking posture; (3) *As faith receiving the declaration*: Act 10:43 — "everyone who believes in him receives forgiveness of sins through his name" — belief is the inner receptive mode in the NT register; Luk 7:47 — "her sins... are forgiven — for she loved much" — love is the inner receptive disposition evidencing that forgiveness has been received.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Three inner modes evidenced. (1) *As an inherited unbelief disposition*: Psa 78:32 — "despite his wonders, they did not believe" — the sinning pattern is rooted in an inherited capacity for unbelief that does not yield to experienced divine power; (2) *As a prolonged inner condition*: Isa 64:5 — "in our sins we have been a long time" — the condition is not episodic but characterises the inner-being state over an extended time; (3) *As a pattern recognised and confessed corporately*: 1Ki 8:47 — "we have sinned and have acted perversely and wickedly" — the corporate inner recognition of the generational pattern is the conscience's response.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Three distinct inner modes. (1) *As self-recognised identity*: Luk 5:8 — "I am a sinful man, O Lord" — Peter's spontaneous inner recognition of his sinner-identity in the presence of holiness; Luk 18:13 — "be merciful to me, a sinner" — the tax collector's self-confession of the sinner-identity; 1Ti 1:15 — Paul's "of whom I am the foremost" — the inward claim of the worst-sinner identity; (2) *As externally assigned identity*: Mat 9:11 — "why does your teacher eat with tax collectors and sinners?" — others name the category; Joh 9:24 — "we know that this man is a sinner" — authoritative external declaration; (3) *As constituted imputed standing*: Rom 5:19 — "made sinners through Adam's disobedience" — the identity is constituted from outside the person.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Five distinct inner modes corresponding to the five VCGs. (1) *As conscience-recognition event*: Lev 5:5 — "when he realizes his guilt... and confesses" — the guilt operates as a moment of dawning inner recognition; (2) *As mounting accumulation*: Ezr 9:6 — "guilt has mounted up to the heavens" — guilt operates as a growing weight that progressively overwhelms; (3) *As unbearable burden*: Gen 4:13 — "my punishment is greater than I can bear" — guilt-as-punitive-weight operates as an inner load exceeding capacity; (4) *As conscience-stagger*: 1Sa 25:31 (pu.qah) — "pangs of conscience" — guilt operates as an inner stumbling that destabilises moral footing; (5) *As indelible stain*: Jer 2:22 — "the stain of your guilt is still before me" — guilt operates as an inner defilement that no self-generated effort removes.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Five distinct inner modes. (1) *As a measured, accumulating store*: Gen 15:16 — "not yet complete" — iniquity accumulates toward a threshold; 2Ch 33:23 (cross-ref) and Jer 25:12 — the store builds until judgment; (2) *As an overwhelming weight*: Psa 38:4 — "gone over my head; like a heavy burden, they are too heavy for me" — the weight presses on the whole person; (3) *As a heart-seated originating force*: Eze 14:3 — "taken their idols into their hearts... stumbling block of their iniquity before their faces" — the iniquity begins in the heart's chosen orientation; (4) *As a self-destructive ensnaring force*: Pro 5:22 — "the iniquities of the wicked ensnare him, and he is held fast in the cords of his sin"; (5) *As a separating barrier*: Isa 59:2 — "your iniquities have made a separation between you and your God" — iniquity operates as a structural relational barrier.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Five distinct inner modes. (1) *As an inner voice*: Psa 36:1 — "transgression speaks to the wicked deep in his heart" — transgression operates as an internal counselling voice that drives out the fear of God; (2) *As a threshold-crossing act*: Amos 1:3/6/9 — the counted transgressions that reach the threshold; Rom 4:15 — the law-violation as specific crossing; (3) *As a dominating power*: Psa 19:13 — "great transgression" exercising dominion; Pro 29:6 — transgression ensnaring the evil man; (4) *As identity-level character*: Isa 48:8 — "called a rebel from birth"; Isa 57:4 — "children of transgression"; (5) *As relational rupture*: Isa 59:13 — "transgressing, and denying the Lord, and turning back from following our God" — the inner act of turning away is constitutive.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Five distinct inner modes. (1) *As settled inner disposition*: Isa 48:8 — foreknown constitutional bent of the will; 2Ch 28:22 — deepening under distress rather than breaking; (2) *As act of inner allegiance-transfer*: 1Ch 5:25 — "broke faith with the God of their fathers, and whored after the gods of the peoples" — the will's active transfer of loyalty to false objects; (3) *As hidden inner duplicity*: Jer 12:6 — "though they speak friendly words to you" — the treachery is concealed behind friendly appearance; (4) *As inner hardening*: 2Ch 28:22 — "in the time of his distress he became yet more faithless to the Lord" — the will deepens its unfaithfulness under circumstances that would normally generate repentance; (5) *As spirit-level orientation*: Mal 2:15/16 — "guard yourselves in your spirit, and do not be faithless" — the spirit is the named locus requiring vigilance against faithlessness.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Five distinct inner modes. (1) *As a perverted heart continually devising evil*: Pro 6:14 — "with perverted heart devises evil, continually sowing discord" — the heart is the origin of the continuous evil-devising; (2) *As a depraved mind robbed of truth*: 1Ti 6:5 — "depraved in mind and deprived of the truth" — the cognitive faculty is corrupted at its root; (3) *As corruption through deceitful desire*: Eph 4:22 — "corrupt through deceitful desires" — the desire-faculty is the active agent of the corruption; (4) *As cognitive-relational inversion*: Isa 29:16 — the creature denying the creator — the mind inverts the proper creature-creator relationship; (5) *As degenerative transformation*: Jer 2:21 — "turned degenerate and become a wild vine" — a process of inner moral transformation in the wrong direction.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Four distinct inner modes. (1) *As a heart-devised scheme*: Psa 58:2 — "in your hearts you devise wrongs" — injustice is planned from the heart's deliberating centre; Psa 64:6 — "they search out injustice" with "diligent search" — deliberately planned; (2) *As a thoroughly internalised appetite*: Job 15:16 — "a man who drinks injustice like water" — the characteristic has become the person's natural sustenance; (3) *As shameless character*: Zep 3:5 — "the unjust knows no shame" — the inner moral-response faculty is insensible; (4) *As a fixed scalar trait*: Luk 16:10 — "dishonest in very little is also dishonest in much" — the inner character is consistent at every scale.

---

### T1.4.2

**Question:** Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The evidence shows clear contextual differentiation. In the God-directed register (VCG-01), sinning is primarily a covenantal and relational act with communal consequence: 1Ki 8:33/35 show national defeat and drought following the people's sinning against God; the scope is corporate. In the interpersonal register (VCG-02), sinning is personal and remedial: Mat 18:15 specifies a repair process (confrontation → listening → forgiveness) that is individual. In the cultic register (VCG-04), sinning operates as an objective cultic fact requiring prescribed remediation regardless of the person's subjective emotional state — the sin offering is brought on realisation, not on feeling. The constitutional level also differs: in Gen 20:6, God restrains sinning from outside the person; in Psa 119:11 and Psa 4:4, the internal resources of stored word and reflective pondering are the operative mechanisms. The characteristic operates at both the social/communal and individual constitutional levels.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Yes. The corpus evidences contextual differentiation. (1) *Individual context* (Lev 4:2; Num 15:27; Num 22:34): a single person sins unintentionally and the remedy is personal (a female goat, a sin offering, confession). (2) *Leadership/priestly context* (Lev 4:3; Lev 8:15/9:15): the anointed priest's sinning "brings guilt on the people" — the same unintentional act carries communal consequence when the actor holds representative authority, requiring a bull (costlier offering) and broader atonement. (3) *Communal context* (Lev 9:15 — "the people's offering"): the community's collective sin addressed through Aaron's prescribed communal sin offering. (4) *Cultic-spatial context* (VCG-02 — altar, sanctuary): the cha.ta verb applied to sacred spaces rather than persons. The direction also differs: individual sin operates vertically (person → God's standard violated); priestly sin radiates outward to the community.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Yes. *By context*: individual confession (VCG-01) operates at the personal conscience level and produces personal plea (2Sa 24:10 — "please take away the iniquity of your servant"); corporate confession (VCG-02) operates at community level and produces collective appeal (1Sa 7:6 — corporate fasting + confession precedes Samuel's mediation). *By direction*: God-directed confession (predominant in VCG-01: "I have sinned against the Lord," Dan 9:11) and person-directed acknowledgment (2Sa 19:20 — Shimei confessing before the returning king; Mat 27:4 — Judas confessing to the priests). *By depth*: Daniel's extended multi-dimensional confession (Dan 9:5 — "sinned and done wrong and acted wickedly and rebelled") represents constitutional-depth engagement; Pharaoh's single-sentence formula (Exo 9:27) represents surface engagement. The constitutional depth of the confession correlates with the genuineness of the inner-being transformation it produces.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Yes. By *context*: the Jeremiah passages (Jer 2:35; 16:10) show conscience suppression operating within the covenantal relationship — Israel claiming innocence before the Lord who has declared judgment. The Ecclesiastes passages (Ecc 2:26; 8:12) show it within the wisdom register — the sinner as a general human type defined by absence of God-orientation. The NT passages (1Cor 15:34; Tit 3:11) show it within the community-of-faith context — believers warned against or described as exhibiting conscience suppression. By *constitutional level*: the active-denial mode (Jer 2:35) operates at the speech/will level; the perceptual blindness mode (Jer 16:10) operates at the cognitive-perceptive level; the habituated absence (Ecc 8:12; 1Cor 15:34) operates at the dispositional/formational level.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Yes. (1) *Leadership context*: the Kings pattern (1Ki 16:31; 2Ki 3:3; 10:29–31; 13:2/6/11; 14:24; 15:9/18/24/28) shows refusal to repent operating at a leadership level where the leader's refusal transmits the sinful course to the people ("which he made Israel to sin"). The leader's inner refusal has communal scope. (2) *Communal context*: 2Ki 13:6; Neh 9:29 — the whole community "did not depart from" or "would not obey" — collective refusal operating through communal formation. (3) *Individual post-truth context*: Heb 10:26 — a single person who has received knowledge of truth and deliberately continues sinning — individual refusal in a context of maximum available information. (4) *Formerly-righteous context*: Eze 18:24 / 33:12 — the person who has been righteous and then turns away, sinning against their prior standing.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Yes. (1) *Individual psychological context*: Exo 9:34 — Pharaoh's individual will-hardening cycle (plague ceases → sin again → harden heart → next plague) — the pattern operates through individual psychological cycles of relief-from-pressure enabling sinning. (2) *National/communal context*: 2Ki 17:7; Hos 10:9 — habitual defection as a communal pattern of a whole people — national defection from covenant allegiance operating through shared practices (idolatry, false worship). (3) *Institutional context*: Hos 8:11 — the characteristic operating through religious institutions (altars) that have been misdirected and now reproduce the sinning orientation. (4) *Ontological/theological context*: 1Jo 3:6 — habitual sinning as the defining marker of not knowing Christ — the characteristic operates as an indicator of fundamental spiritual condition.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Yes. (1) *Pre-emptive/warning context*: Exo 23:33; Deu 20:18 — contagious sin is anticipated before it occurs; the warning names the mechanism in advance (foreign nations will cause Israel to sin through proximity and teaching). (2) *Monarchic leadership context*: the Kings corpus (1Ki 14:16 through 2Ki 23:15) — contagious sin operates through the formal authority of kingship; the king's inner commitment is transmitted to Israel through royal authority. (3) *Prophetic accusation context*: Jer 32:35 — specific leaders building specific sinning structures (high places) that cause specific abominations (child sacrifice). (4) *Historical retrospect/judgment context*: 2Ki 17:21 — the narrator explaining Israel's exile as the consequence of Jeroboam's contagious sin across generations.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Yes, across two clear contexts. (1) *Vassal-state political context*: 2Ki 1:1; 3:5/7 (Moab), 2Ki 8:20/22; 2Ch 21:8/10 (Edom) — smaller nations breaking from the control of Israel or Judah; the revolt is a bid for national independence. (2) *Intra-covenantal political context*: 1Ki 12:19; 2Ch 10:19 — the northern tribes of Israel breaking from the house of David; the revolt is within the covenant community, breaking the Davidic governing structure. The intra-covenantal revolt is theologically weightier because it breaks not merely a political authority but a covenantally grounded one.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Yes, across the three VCG contexts. (1) *Communal-relational context (VCG-01)*: slander operates between persons within community relationships — Eph 4:31; Col 3:8 address this within the church community; the characteristic damages interpersonal relationships. (2) *Judicial-christological context (VCG-02)*: blasphemy operates as a formal legal charge in the trial of Jesus (Mat 26:65; Mar 14:64) — the judicial context makes the speech-act a capital offense with death-sentence consequence. (3) *Eschatological-cosmic context (VCG-03)*: blasphemy operates as the defining characteristic of the eschatological anti-God power (Rev 13:1/5/6) — the cosmic context makes it the constitutive orientation of the creature entirely given over to God-defiance.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Yes, across the three mechanisms. (1) *Enticement*: operates through the vulnerable points of the desire-faculty — 2Pe 2:18 specifically targets those "barely escaping from those who live in error" — the context of vulnerability shapes where enticement is most effective. (2) *Collective hypocrisy*: operates specifically in communal-social contexts — Gal 2:13 — the presence of others who are acting hypocritically is required for sunupokrinomai to occur (the *sun-* prefix requires a social context). (3) *Apostasy*: operates in the context of covenantal-identity challenge — Act 21:21's accusation occurs in the context of the Gentile mission's challenge to the Jewish-covenantal framework.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Yes. (1) *Under law (VCG-03 — Romans 7)*: sin exploits the commandment as an opportunity — "sin, seizing an opportunity through the commandment" (Rom 7:8) — the law context activates sin's power within the person who has the law; (2) *Without law*: Rom 5:13 — "sin indeed was in the world before the law was given" — the condition exists before law, though it is not legally counted without law; the condition's reality precedes its legal articulation; (3) *In unbelief*: Joh 16:9 — "concerning sin, because they do not believe in me" — the Spirit convicts of the sin that is constituted specifically by unbelief; (4) *In the mortal body*: Rom 6:12 — "let not sin therefore reign in your mortal body, to make you obey its passions" — the mortal body is the site in which the condition seeks to operate through passions.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Yes. (1) *Individual-practice context*: Joh 8:34 — the enslavement operates through individual habitual practice (the one who practices sin); the mechanism is personal and accumulative. (2) *Universal-cosmic context*: Gal 3:22 — the imprisonment operates at the universal level — everything confined under sin; the mechanism is structural and comprehensive, not dependent on individual practice. (3) *Community-protection context*: 1Jo 5:16/18 — the enslaving power's reach is addressed within the community context of intercessory prayer and the protective role of the born-of-God; the mechanism operates against a community within which some may still be under sin's reach (5:16 — the sinning brother).

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Yes. (1) *Individual context*: chet (VCG-01) — each person bears their own sin personally; Deu 24:16 — individual personal liability; (2) *Corporate-national context*: VCG-04 Jeroboam-sin legacy — the record operates at the national level, accumulated across royal generations, with the whole people affected by the leader's named sin-pattern; (3) *Divine-surveillance context*: VCG-03 — Job perceives God as actively searching for and watching his sin, creating a condition of personal surveillance; (4) *Covenantal context*: VCG-05 sevenfold discipline passages (Lev 26:18/21/24/28) — the record triggers covenant consequences at specific thresholds.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Yes — significantly. (1) *Levitical priestly context* (VCG-01): the seeking operates through prescribed ritual (bringing the animal, laying hands, priestly action); the individual's inner seeking is mediated through the institutional framework; (2) *Individual-sin context* (VCG-03 — Lev 4:3/14/5:6/10): the seeking is triggered when the sin "becomes known" — an individual recognition moment generates the seeking-event; (3) *Intercessory context* (Exo 32:30/31 — VCG-02/03): Moses seeks forgiveness on behalf of others — the seeking is not for the seeker's own record but for another's; (4) *Christological-declarative context* (VCG-02 NT): seeking is through repentance/faith and receiving is through direct declaration (Luk 7:48 — "your sins are forgiven").

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Yes. (1) *Wilderness context* (Psa 78:17/32): the generational pattern operates through continued rebellion despite miraculous provision — God's visible acts are the context in which the inherited sinning persists; (2) *Exile context* (1Ki 8:47; Jer 8:14): the generational pattern has produced the condition of captivity; the confession occurs in exile, where the corporate consequences of the accumulated sin are most visible; (3) *Prophetic-covenantal context* (Isa 43:27; Isa 64:5): the pattern is named in its originating dimension (first father) and its prolonged-duration dimension ("a long time"), allowing both the origin and the extent to be addressed.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Yes — three contextual modes. (1) *Extreme-type context* (VCG-03): the identity is totalising — Gen 13:13 — "great sinners against the Lord" — the sinful character defines the entire person or people; (2) *Social-stigma context* (VCG-01): the identity operates through social exclusion and contamination-fear — Mat 9:11; Luk 7:37/39 — the social category carries contamination risk that the observant avoid; (3) *Gospel context* (VCG-02 NT): the identity is the basis of Christ's saving mission — 1Ti 1:15 — "came into the world to save sinners" — the worst sinner-identity is the target of grace rather than the disqualifier from it.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Yes across the five VCGs. (1) *Individual-unintentional context* (VCG-01): guilt operates through conscience-recognition after a violation; the recognition is the key moment — Lev 4:13 — "they realize their guilt"; (2) *Communal-accumulated context* (VCG-02): guilt operates as a generational and corporate weight — Ezr 9:7 — "from the days of our fathers... we have been in great guilt"; (3) *Priestly-liturgical context* (VCG-03): guilt operates as a transferable burden borne representationally — Exo 28:38 — Aaron bears the people's cultic guilt; (4) *Punitive-judicial context* (VCG-04): guilt operates through the weight of earned consequence — Gen 4:13 — Cain's punishment; Eze 4:4/5/6 — enacted punishment-bearing; (5) *Prophetic-judgment context* (VCG-05): guilt operates through its indelibility before God (Jer 2:22) and its exposure at the time of divine reckoning (Eze 21:23/24).

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Yes across the eight VCG registers. (1) *Priestly-cultic context* (VCG-01): iniquity operates as a transferable ritual burden addressed through institutional mediation (Lev 16:21/22 — Aaron confesses over scapegoat); (2) *Generational context* (VCG-02): iniquity operates as a transmitted moral inheritance visited on children (Exo 20:5); (3) *Divine-memory context* (VCG-03): iniquity operates as a sealed record in God's sight (Hos 13:12 — "bound up and kept in store"); (4) *Personal context* (VCG-04): iniquity operates as an individually owned crime that attaches to the person (Eze 18:20 — "upon himself"); (5) *Self-destructive context* (VCG-07): iniquity operates as an internal corrupting force that rusts from within (Eze 24:23 — "rot away in your iniquities").

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Yes across the nine VCG registers. (1) *Divine-covenant context* (VCG-01): transgression operates as relational betrayal of the nurturing God (Isa 1:2) — the relational betrayal dimension dominates; (2) *Legal context* (VCG-04): transgression operates as law-violation with judicial consequences (Rom 2:23 — "dishonor God by breaking the law"); (3) *Interpersonal context* (VCG-08): transgression operates as breach of trust or relational duty (Exo 22:9 — breach of custodial trust; Pro 17:9 — covering an offense seeks love); (4) *Threshold context* (VCG-03): transgression operates as a countable accumulation (Amos 1:3 — "for three... and for four") toward a divine tolerance limit; (5) *Revolt context* (VCG-02): transgression operates as vocal, active inner defiance that destroys the whole person (Isa 1:5 — "whole head sick and whole heart faint").

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Yes across the three VCG registers. (1) *Vertical toward God* (VCG-01): faithlessness operates as direct covenant-betrayal against the God who constituted the bond; Eze 20:27 — treachery equated with blasphemy; the relational damage is at the deepest level; (2) *Horizontal toward persons* (VCG-02): faithlessness operates as betrayal of human trust within a known relational bond — marital (Num 5:12; Mal 2:14), fraternal (Job 6:15), civic (Judg 9:23); (3) *Constitutional character* (VCG-03): faithlessness operates as an identity-level character trait — Isa 24:16 (compounded betrayal), Isa 33:1 (the one who will be betrayed in turn), Isa 48:8 (foreknown from birth). VCG-01 is the primary theological register; VCG-02 the relational-human register; VCG-03 the character-level register.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Yes across the five VCG registers. (1) *Speech context* (VCG-01): perversity operates through the tongue — Pro 6:14 — twisted heart devising evil sown through speech; (2) *Judicial context* (VCG-02): perversity operates through bribery corrupting the discernment faculty (Exo 23:8); (3) *Personal moral context* (VCG-03): perversity operates as the twisted inner life direction — Jer 3:21 — "perverted their way and forgotten the Lord"; (4) *Sexual-created-order context* (VCG-04): perversity operates as violation of the categories God established in creation (Lev 18:23 — te.vel); (5) *Cosmic-spiritual context* (VCG-05): perversity operates as a universal corruption from which all of creation needs liberation (Rom 8:21).

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Yes across the three VCG registers. (1) *Judicial context* (VCG-01): injustice operates as partiality and bribery — Psa 82:2 — "judge unjustly and show partiality to the wicked" — the relational-authority context shapes the judicial mode; Lev 19:15 — "you shall do no injustice in court" — the court context defines this mode; (2) *Oppression context* (VCG-02): injustice operates as violent harm against persons — Psa 58:2 — "your hands deal out violence on earth"; Job 15:16 — thoroughly internalised appetite for wrong; (3) *Character context* (VCG-03): injustice operates as a stable identity-level disposition — Luk 16:10 — fixed across small and large; shameless insensibility (Zep 3:5).

---

### T1.4.3

**Question:** Does this characteristic have a communicative or speech-based mode of operation — and if so, how does it function?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Speech-based sinning is explicitly evidenced. Psa 39:1 ("I will guard my ways, that I may not sin with my tongue") locates sinning's communicative mode in unguarded speech — the tongue as the instrument. Job 2:10 ("Job did not sin with his lips") confirms that under suffering the lips are the point of potential sinning. Job 31:30 ("I have not let my mouth sin by asking for his life with a curse") shows speech as a vehicle for directing sinful aggression against an enemy. Ecc 5:6 ("let not your mouth lead you into sin") frames the mouth as an organ that leads the whole person into sin through rash speech before the divine messenger. Isa 29:21 shows sinning through false verbal accusation in public proceedings. The communicative mode operates in the outward direction (speech expressing inner sinful orientation) and the self-implicating direction (rash speech creating liability before God).

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Limited speech-based content. Lev 5:5 ("when he realizes his guilt... and confesses the sin he has committed") shows the confession as the verbal component — the spoken acknowledgment of the sin once it surfaces to awareness. Lev 5:1 (the borderline witness-silence verse) involves a speech failure: the person who should testify but does not speak — sin of omission through silence. Num 22:34 (Balaam's confession — "I have sinned, for I did not know") is a speech-act: verbal confession of the inadvertent sin with an offer to reverse course. The communicative mode is primarily *confessional* (speech following realisation) rather than the *constitutive* role speech plays in CHAR-1 (where speech can itself be the sinning act). For CHAR-2, speech is the remedy-initiating mechanism rather than the mode of the sinning itself.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Confession is constitutively speech-based: the characteristic is defined by the verbal naming act. The corpus evidences three specific speech-modes. (1) *Direct verbal declaration*: "I have sinned" / "We have sinned" — the formulaic spoken confession that names the act (Exo 9:27; Judg 10:10; Dan 9:5; Luk 15:21). (2) *Written/prayed confession*: Neh 1:6 — "confessing the sins of the people of Israel... that I now pray before you day and night"; Dan 9:5 — an extended prayer-confession. The written/prayed form extends the speech-act into sustained verbal engagement with God. (3) *Public declaration*: Job 33:27 — "He sings before men and says: 'I sinned and perverted what was right'" — confession offered publicly to a human audience. The speech-based mode is the defining operation: without the speaking, the inner recognition remains conscience and guilt (CHAR-17) but does not become confession (CHAR-3).

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Yes — the most vivid form of conscience suppression is speech-based. Jer 2:35 — "you say, 'I am innocent; surely his anger has turned from me'" and "I have not sinned" — the characteristic is enacted in these spoken claims. The speech-mode operates as a *false declaration of moral standing*: where CHAR-3 (Confession) uses speech to name sin truthfully, conscience suppression uses speech to falsely deny it. The speech-based mode of CHAR-4 is the inverted mirror of CHAR-3's confessional speech: same grammatical form (first-person declaration about one's own moral state), opposite content (denial vs naming).

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Limited speech-based evidence. 1Ki 16:31 — Ahab treating Jeroboam's sins "as a light thing" implies an internal evaluative speech-act: the characterisation of established wickedness as minor is a verbal-cognitive minimisation. The corpus does not evidence refusal to repent primarily through speech-acts but through *action/non-action*: the will's refusal is expressed through what it does (clings, remains, walks in) and does not do (does not depart, does not turn). Rom 6:15 — "are we to sin because we are not under law but under grace?" — the hypothetical question implies that refusal to repent can be voiced as a theological argument, which Paul emphatically rejects ("By no means!"). The characteristic can be articulated as a position, but its primary mode is dispositional, not verbal.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(S)*

**[CHAR-6]** S — The corpus contains no explicit speech-based mode for habitual defection. The characteristic operates primarily through inner dispositional formation (Exo 9:34 — hardened heart), institutional structure (Hos 8:11 — altars), and sustained relational orientation (2Ki 17:7 — fearing other gods). The Ecclesiastes person-type statements (Pro 11:31; 13:22; Ecc 7:26; 9:2/18) are observer-descriptions rather than speech acts of the habitually sinning person. 1Sa 2:25 — "they would not listen to the voice of their father" — names a speech-reception failure (habitual non-listening) that could be considered communicative, but this is a resistance to others' speech rather than the characteristic's own communicative mode.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Limited speech-based evidence. Deu 20:18 — "that they may not *teach* you to do according to all their abominable practices" — the teaching mode is explicitly named: contagious sin can operate through verbal instruction in the sinning practices. The foreign nations teach Israel; the teaching is a communicative mode through which the sinning orientation is transmitted. 1Ki 16:2 — God's indictment is verbal/prophetic — but this is God's speech about contagious sin, not the mechanism of contagious sin itself. The primary mode of contagious sin is structural-behavioural (walking in the sinful path, building altars) rather than verbal, but the teaching-mode (Deu 20:18) is a secondary speech-based mechanism.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Limited speech evidence. 2Ki 3:7 — Jehoram "sent word to Jehoshaphat king of Judah: 'The king of Moab has rebelled against me'" — the revolt is communicated verbally in the diplomatic-military context; the king names the revolt in requesting military alliance. The speech here is not the revolt itself but its public articulation in the political-diplomatic register. The revolt itself is expressed through action (setting up a king — 2Ki 8:20) rather than primarily through speech.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Yes — sinful speech is constitutively speech-based: it is definitionally an act of the mouth. Mat 15:19 — "out of the heart come... slander" — the slander is the speech. Mat 26:65 — "He has uttered blasphemy" — the utterance is the act. Rev 13:5 — "a mouth uttering haughty and blasphemous words" — the mouth is named as the instrument. The speech-based mode is not a secondary feature but the defining form of the characteristic: without the externalisation in speech, the inner corruption remains CHAR-4/16 territory rather than CHAR-9.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Limited speech evidence. 2Pe 2:18 — "speaking loud boasts of folly, they entice" — the enticement in this instance operates through speech: the loud boasting is the communicative vehicle through which the sensual enticement is delivered. Act 21:21 — "teach all the Jews... to forsake Moses" — the accusation implies that Paul's teaching (speech) is the mechanism through which apostasy is transmitted. Gal 2:13's hypocrisy is primarily behavioural (acting) rather than speech-based. The speech-based mode is present for enticement (2Pe 2:18) and apostasy-transmission (Act 21:21) but not dominant across the characteristic.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Limited speech evidence. The primary mode of CHAR-11 is structural (condition) and power-dynamic (enslaving force) rather than verbal. However: (1) *Speech of confession*: VCG-02 — Mat 3:6; Mar 1:5 — "confessing their sins" at baptism — the condition is publicly acknowledged through verbal confession as part of repentance; (2) *Speech of declaration*: VCG-02 — Jesus's verbal forgiveness declarations (Mat 9:2 — "your sins are forgiven") — the condition is addressed and removed through authoritative verbal declaration; (3) *The Spirit's convicting speech*: Joh 16:8/9 — the Spirit "will convict the world concerning sin" — the condition requires an external verbal-divine agent to make it known to the person who does not self-recognise it.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(S)*

**[CHAR-12]** S — The 9-verse corpus does not evidence a communicative or speech-based mode for sin's enslaving power. The characteristic operates through practice-to-slavery (Joh 8:34), universal imprisonment (Gal 3:22), and allegiance-capture (1Jo 3:8) — all structural rather than verbal-communicative modes. The enslaving power does not speak or communicate; it governs.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Yes — in two registers. (1) *Prophetic declaration of the record*: Isa 58:1 — "declare to my people their transgression, to the house of Jacob their sins" — the prophet's speech makes the record known to those who have suppressed it; Mic 3:8 — "to declare to Jacob his transgression and to Israel his sin" — the Spirit-empowered prophet is specifically commissioned to voice the record. (2) *Testifying record*: Isa 59:12 — "our sins testify against us" — the record itself speaks as a witness against the person in a judicial-communicative mode.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Yes — on both sides. (1) *Human-side speech*: Exo 32:31 — Moses verbally names the sin before God ("Alas, this people has sinned a great sin"); the speech-act of naming the sin before God is part of the seeking; (2) *Divine-side speech*: Luk 7:48 — "your sins are forgiven" — the forgiveness declaration is a speech-act; Mat 26:28 — "for this is my blood of the covenant... poured out for many for the forgiveness of sins" — the institution-declaration at the Last Supper is speech announcing the mechanism of forgiveness; Act 10:43 — "to him all the prophets bear witness" — the prophetic testimony to forgiveness is a speech-tradition.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Yes — the corporate confession is the speech-mode. 1Ki 8:47 — "saying, 'We have sinned and have acted perversely and wickedly'" — the speech-act of corporate confession is the verbal form through which the generational pattern is acknowledged; Jer 8:14 — "because we have sinned against the Lord" — the corporate speech-act of naming the sin before God and the community. The corporate confessional "we" is the characteristic's distinctive communicative form: it is not individual private confession but communal speech that acknowledges the shared inherited condition.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Yes — in both directions. (1) *Self-confession*: Luk 5:8 — "I am a sinful man, O Lord"; Luk 18:13 — "be merciful to me, a sinner"; 1Ti 1:15 — "of whom I am the foremost" — the inward identity expressed through verbal self-declaration; (2) *External declaration*: Joh 9:24 — "we know that this man is a sinner" — authoritative community verdict spoken aloud; Gal 2:15 — "Gentile sinners" — ethnic-religious category named in speech; (3) *Hostile speech as identity-expression*: Jude 15 — "the harsh things that ungodly sinners have spoken against him" — the sinner's identity is expressed through their verbal opposition to God.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Yes — in two directions. (1) *Confession*: Lev 5:5 — "confesses the sin he has committed" — guilt's natural speech-mode is confession; the inner guilt-recognition moves into verbal acknowledgment before God; Num 5:7 — "he shall confess his sin" — the guilt is spoken outward; (2) *Acknowledgment of guilt before another*: Gen 42:21 — "in truth we are guilty concerning our brother" — the brothers' verbal acknowledgment of guilt to one another; Gen 44:16 — Judah's "God has found out the guilt of your servants" — verbal acknowledgment of guilt before Joseph. The guilt-state thus has a speech-mode of honest naming — both before God (confession) and before others (acknowledgment).

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Yes — in three speech-modes. (1) *Confession*: Lev 16:21 — "Aaron shall confess over it all the iniquities of the people of Israel" — the verbal act of naming iniquity over the scapegoat; Psa 38:18 — "I confess my iniquity; I am sorry for my sin"; Lev 26:40 — "if they confess their iniquity and the iniquity of their fathers"; (2) *Self-accusation*: Jer 14:7 — "though our iniquities testify against us" — iniquity is personified as a witness speaking against the person in God's court; (3) *Denial*: Hos 12:8 — "they cannot find in me iniquity or sin" — the self-deceived conscience's speech-denial of existing iniquity; Job 31:33 — "if I have concealed my transgressions... by hiding my iniquity in my heart" — the alternative is named as speech-concealment.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Yes — in three speech-modes. (1) *Transgression as inner speech*: Psa 36:1 — "transgression speaks to the wicked deep in his heart" — the characteristic has an inner-voice dimension; (2) *Revolt expressed through verbal rebellion*: Isa 59:13 — "speaking oppression and revolt, conceiving and uttering from the heart lying words"; Jer 28:16 — "you have uttered rebellion against the Lord" — the spoken word is the revolt's expression; (3) *Confession of transgression*: Psa 32:5 — "I will confess my transgressions to the Lord" — the voluntary speech-act of naming and owning the transgression; Psa 38:18 — "I confess my iniquity"; Pro 28:13 — "he who confesses and forsakes them will obtain mercy."

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Yes — in two modes. (1) *Treachery through friendly speech*: Jer 12:6 — "they speak friendly words to you" while acting treacherously — the verbal dimension of faithlessness is the friendly-word mask over the betraying action; Psa 59:5 — "those who treacherously plot evil" — speech that plans betrayal; (2) *Confession of faithlessness*: Lev 26:40 — "if they confess their iniquity and... treachery" — verbal acknowledgment before God; Ezr 10:2 — "we have broken faith with our God" — the community's verbal confession; Ezr 10:10 — "you have broken faith and married foreign women" — Ezra's verbal indictment. The speech-mode is either the mask of treachery (friendly words concealing betrayal) or its reversal through honest confession.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Yes — VCG-01 (10 verses) is entirely the speech-perversion register. Pro 6:14 — perverted heart devises evil and sows discord through speech; Pro 8:13 — perverted speech named as wisdom's hated counterpart; Pro 10:31 — "the perverse tongue will be cut off"; Pro 23:33 — "your heart utter perverse things" — drunkenness producing heart-generated perverted speech. The speech-mode of perversion is the most extensively evidenced in the corpus: VCG-01 dedicates 10 verses entirely to the tongue/lips/mouth as perversity's primary communicative expression.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Yes — through the verbal-wrongdoing dimension. Isa 59:3 — "your tongue mutters wickedness" — injustice is uttered; Job 6:30 — "is there any injustice on my tongue?" — the tongue as the potential organ of verbal injustice; Job 13:7 — "will you speak falsely for God and speak deceitfully for him?" — injustice as theological-speech falsehood; Zep 3:13 — "they shall do no injustice and speak no lies" — injustice and lying speech paired as the two modes being eliminated in the remnant. Speech is CHAR-22's secondary expressive mode after conduct.

---

## T1.5 — Immediate Response

### T1.5.1

**Question:** What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The corpus reveals two divergent immediate responses to encountering wilful sinning. (1) *Conscience-activation and moral recognition*: Gen 42:22 — Reuben's immediate response to the brothers' sinning against Joseph is to invoke the reckoning that follows: "so now there comes a reckoning for his blood." The guilty party's immediate response is awareness of consequence. Gen 20:9 — Abimelech's immediate response to learning of the sin brought upon him is protest and confrontation: "you have brought on me and my kingdom a great sin." (2) *Moral refusal and naming*: Gen 39:9 — Joseph's immediate response to the temptation is to name it as "great wickedness and sin against God" — conscience-active refusal before the act is committed. The pattern suggests that the most immediate inner-being response to encountering wilful sinning (whether in oneself or from another) is moral recognition — the conscience registering the moral quality of the act.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The immediate inner-being response, once the sin surfaces to awareness, is *guilt-recognition and its confessional expression*. Lev 5:5 — "when he realizes his guilt in any of these and confesses the sin he has committed" — names realisation-plus-confession as the immediate sequence. Balaam (Num 22:34) responds immediately to the angel's disclosure with: "I have sinned, for I did not know... if it is evil in your sight, I will turn back" — the immediate inner response is acknowledgment plus readiness to reverse. This immediate response distinguishes CHAR-2 from CHAR-4 (Conscience suppression): the person who suppresses awareness is not exhibiting CHAR-2 but its failure mode. The normative immediate response evidenced in the corpus is conscience engaging promptly once awareness arrives.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The corpus evidences varied immediate responses when one person confesses to another. (1) *Forgiveness/mercy offered*: Luk 15:20 (context — the father runs and embraces before the prodigal has completed his confession speech); 1Sa 26:21 — Saul promises "I will no more do you harm" in response to David's mercy that prompted his confession. (2) *Indifference or dismissal*: Mat 27:4 — the priests' response to Judas's confession is "What is that to us? See to it yourself" — the confession is heard but the recipients are unmoved. (3) *God's response*: Eze 33:16 — sins not remembered. The immediate response from the human side is not uniform; from the divine side the corpus points toward reception and cancellation.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The corpus evidences two divine responses to conscience suppression in others. (1) *Prophetic declaration of judgment*: Jer 2:35 — God responds to Israel's false innocence claim with "Behold, I will bring you to judgment" — the immediate response to the denial of sin is the announcement of accountability. (2) *Call to awakening and shame*: 1Cor 15:34 — "Wake up from your drunken stupor, as is right, and do not go on sinning... I say this to your shame" — Paul's response to conscience suppression in the community is an appeal to shame and alertness. Both responses treat conscience suppression as a condition requiring external correction, since the person's inner conscience is not performing its corrective function.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The corpus shows two patterns of response when refusal to repent is confronted externally. (1) *Continued non-departure*: the Kings corpus shows that prophetic and covenantal warnings did not break the pattern — the formula "did not depart from" applies even to kings who received divine word. Neh 9:29 — "you warned them... yet they acted presumptuously" — the warning met by presumptuousness is the inner response. (2) *Public rebuke required*: 1Ti 5:20 — "those who persist in sin, rebuke them in the presence of all, so that the rest may stand in fear" — the persistent refuser's response is not changed by normal correction; only public confrontation aimed at producing communal fear addresses it. The immediate inner response of the person who refuses to repent is continued refusal — the characteristic is by definition one that does not yield to normal correction.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Two response patterns. (1) *Continued hardening*: Exo 9:34 — Pharaoh "sinned yet again and hardened his heart" immediately upon the plague ceasing — the response to the relief from external pressure is to sin again and harden further. The confrontation (plague) produces temporary cessation, then resumed sinning with increased hardening. (2) *Non-response to correction*: 1Sa 2:25 — Eli's sons "would not listen to the voice of their father" — the habitual defector's characteristic response to correction is non-listening. The habitual pattern has become sufficiently entrenched that the father's voice produces no corrective effect.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The corpus evidences two responses when the community encounters the leader's transmitted sin. (1) *Compliance and adoption*: the dominant pattern in the Kings corpus — Israel/Judah follows the leader's sinning path; 1Ki 15:26 — "walked in the way of his father, and in his sin which he made Israel to sin" — the community walks in the transmitted path. The immediate response is alignment with the leader's sinning direction. (2) *Escalation*: 1Ki 14:22 — "Judah did what was evil... more than all that their fathers had done" — the community does not merely replicate the transmitted sin but escalates beyond it. The immediate response to contagious sin from a prior generation can be to exceed the transmitted level.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Two response patterns. (1) *Military response sought*: 2Ki 3:7 — Jehoram's immediate response to Moab's revolt is to summon Jehoshaphat for military alliance against Moab; the response is military-political engagement. (2) *Permanent fracture accepted*: 1Ki 12:19 / 2Ch 10:19 — "to this day" — the narrator's assessment implies that the response to Israel's revolt from the Davidic house was not immediate restoration but the acceptance of a permanent division. The responses differ: revolt against a vassal nation triggers military response; revolt against the governing authority within the covenant community produces lasting fracture.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Two response patterns. (1) *Judicial/legal response*: VCG-02 — the immediate response to the charge of blasphemy is judicial verdict: Mat 26:65 — the high priest tears his robes and calls for witnesses; Mar 14:64 — "they all condemned him as deserving death" — the immediate response is escalation to capital punishment. (2) *Community correction*: VCG-01 — Eph 4:31; Col 3:8 — the immediate response prescribed is renunciation and replacement with edifying speech.
