The responses differ by context: blasphemy against God in the judicial context produces a death-verdict; slander in the community context produces a call to put it away.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Different response patterns across the three mechanisms. (1) *Enticement*: Jam 1:14 — the immediate response is "lured" — the person is drawn toward the temptation through their desire; the luring is the immediate inner-being effect of encountering the enticement. 2Pe 2:18 — the "barely escaping" persons are the susceptible targets whose immediate response to enticement is toward re-capture. (2) *Collective hypocrisy*: Gal 2:13 — Barnabas's "led astray" — the immediate response of the susceptible community member is to follow the collective performance rather than maintaining independent authentic identity. (3) *Apostasy*: Act 21:21 — the immediate response within the accusing community is alarm at the perceived defection from the covenantal framework.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Different responses across the VCG registers. (1) *VCG-01 response*: the condition of wickedness as identity produces judgment — Mal 4:1 — "shall set them ablaze"; Mal 1:4 — "I will tear down" — the response of God to the condition of settled wickedness is judicial destruction. (2) *VCG-02 response*: the condition encountered in the context of Jesus's ministry produces wonder and resistance — Luk 7:49 — "who is this, who even forgives sins?" — bystanders cannot categorise the one who addresses the condition; Mar 2:7 — "who can forgive sins but God alone?" — the scribes resist the implication of Jesus's authority over the condition. (3) *VCG-03 response*: awareness of the condition under the law produces inner conflict — Rom 7:9 — "when the commandment came, sin came alive and I died" — the inner response is a death-experience as the condition's full weight becomes known.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Two response patterns. (1) *The enslaved person's non-response*: the enslaved person continues in sin — Rom 6:1 — "continue in sin" is the rhetorical form of the question about what the enslaved might do; the enslaved state is characterised by continued sinning. (2) *The born-of-God person's structural non-response to the enslavement*: 1Jo 3:9 — "he cannot keep on sinning, because he has been born of God" — the born-of-God person encounters the enslaving power but the God's-seed-indwelling constitutionally prevents it from gaining its typical hold. The protective dimension (1Jo 5:18 — "the evil one does not touch him") names the specific absence of the enslaving power's grip for the born-of-God person.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Multiple response patterns across the corpus. (1) *Confession*: Num 5:7 — "he shall confess his sin that he has committed" — the encounter with the record that "is made known" (Lev 4:23/28) triggers the confession-response; Psa 32:5 — "I acknowledged my sin to you... I said, 'I will confess my transgressions to the Lord'" — the immediate response to facing the record is acknowledgment. (2) *Sorrow*: Psa 38:18 — "I am sorry for my sin" — the encounter produces grief as an immediate affective response. (3) *Plea for pardon*: Exo 10:17 — Pharaoh's "forgive my sin, please, only this once" — the record encountered produces an urgent appeal for its cancellation.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Luk 7:47 — "she loved much" — the woman's love is the most immediate inner-being response to received forgiveness: the magnitude of forgiveness received produces a proportional love-response. Col 2:13 — "made alive" — the immediate inner response to forgiveness received is new life displacing prior death. Lev 16:30 — "you shall be clean before the Lord from all your sins" — the purity-status is the immediate declared condition following the atonement's completion. The immediate inner response thus ranges from the affective (love — Luk 7:47), through the vital (alive — Col 2:13), to the relational-status (clean — Lev 16:30).

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Corporate confession. 1Ki 8:47 — "they turn their heart in the land... and repent and plead with you... saying, 'We have sinned and have acted perversely and wickedly'" — the immediate inner response to encountering the generational condition in exile is heart-turning, repentance, and verbal confession. Jer 8:14 — "we have sinned against the Lord" — the corporate recognition produces a speech-act of acknowledgment. The most immediate response is thus the collective recognition and naming of the condition before God.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Two contrasting immediate responses. (1) *Prostration and plea*: Luk 5:8 — "he fell down at Jesus' knees, saying, 'Depart from me, for I am a sinful man'" — the immediate inner response to recognising the sinner-identity in the presence of holiness is prostration, awe-dread, and the impulse to distance Jesus from the defiled self; Luk 18:13 — "stood far off, would not even lift up his eyes to heaven, but beat his breast, saying, 'God, be merciful to me, a sinner'" — the immediate inner response is physical self-abasement and penitential appeal; (2) *Dread*: Isa 33:14 — "sinners in Zion are afraid; trembling has seized the godless" — the sinner's immediate inner response to God's consuming presence is terror.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — The immediate response pattern across VCG-01 is: recognition → shame or distress → remedial action. Gen 42:21 — "in truth we are guilty concerning our brother, in that we saw the distress of his soul... that is why this distress has come upon us" — the immediate inner response is interpretive: the brothers connect their current suffering to their past guilty act; Ezr 9:6 — "I am ashamed and blush to lift my face to you" — shame is the immediate inner-affective response to guilt-recognition; Gen 4:13 — Cain's "my punishment is greater than I can bear" — the immediate inner response to the punitive guilt-dimension is despair.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — The immediate responses vary across the corpus. (1) *Conscience-strike*: 2Sa 24:10 — "David's heart struck him after he had numbered the people" — the immediate inner response to the iniquity is conscience activation; (2) *Shame and face-avoidance*: Ezr 9:6 — "I am ashamed and blush to lift my face to you, my God, for our iniquities have risen higher than our heads" — shame and the inability to face God are immediate; (3) *Request for removal*: 2Sa 24:10 — David immediately says "please take away the iniquity of your servant" — the immediate movement is toward plea for divine removal; (4) *Despair*: Psa 40:12 — "my iniquities have overtaken me, and I cannot see; they are more than the hairs of my head; my heart fails me" — the crushing weight produces immediate inner collapse.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — The immediate responses vary significantly. (1) *Shame and exposure*: Lam 1:22 — "because of all my transgressions; for my groans are many, and my heart is faint" — the immediate response is grief and inner collapse; Ezr 10:13 — "we have greatly transgressed in this matter" — corporate acknowledgment; (2) *Dominion over the will*: Psa 19:13 — "let them not have dominion over me!" — the immediate threat is enslavement; (3) *Self-justification and denial*: Pro 28:24 — "Whoever robs his father... says, 'That is no transgression'" — the immediate response in hardened conscience is denial; (4) *Despairing awareness*: Eze 33:10 — "surely our transgressions and our sins are upon us, and we rot away because of them. How then can we live?" — despairing recognition.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — The immediate responses vary. (1) *Grief and mourning in the witness*: Ezr 9:4 — "those who trembled at the words of the God of Israel... gathered around me while I sat appalled until the evening sacrifice" — the spiritually aware person's immediate response to witnessing faithlessness is appalled grief; Ezr 10:6 — Ezra "mourning over the faithlessness of the exiles," fasting and drinking nothing; (2) *Shame*: Dan 9:7 — "to us open shame" — the immediate experiential consequence; Psa 25:3 — "they shall be ashamed who are wantonly treacherous" — shame; (3) *Hardening*: 2Ch 28:22 — "in time of his distress he became yet more faithless" — the perverse response of deepened unfaithfulness; (4) *Despair and desolation*: Lam 1:2 — "all her friends have dealt treacherously with her" producing weeping bitterly.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — The immediate responses include confession and self-indictment. 1Ki 8:47 — "we have sinned and have acted perversely and wickedly" — immediate communal confession naming perversity specifically; Dan 9:5 — "we have sinned and done wrong and acted wickedly and rebelled" — the comprehensive confessional self-indictment; 2Sa 24:17 — "I have sinned, and I have done wickedly" — David's immediate self-indictment upon seeing the plague; Job 33:27 — "I sinned and perverted what was right" — confessional first-person recognition.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Varied across positions. (1) *Response of the one suffering injustice*: Job 6:29 — "please turn; let no injustice be done. Turn now; my vindication is at stake" — urgent plea for relief; Psa 43:1 — "vindicate me, O God, and defend my cause against an ungodly people, from the deceitful and unjust man deliver me" — immediate appeal to God for deliverance; (2) *Response of the righteous observer*: Psa 37:1 — "fret not yourself because of evildoers; be not envious of wrongdoers" — the warning against fretful envy; (3) *Non-response of the unjust*: Zep 3:5 — "the unjust knows no shame" — no inner response at all.

---

### T1.5.2

**Question:** Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The immediate response varies across the corpus. In VCG-03 (deterrence/restraint), the immediate response is refusal and resistance (Gen 39:9, Job 1:22, Psa 4:4, Psa 39:1). In VCG-01 (God-directed sinning), the immediate response evidenced is often external consequence rather than internal registration — drought (1Ki 8:35), defeat (1Ki 8:33), expulsion (Eze 28:16). In VCG-02 (interpersonal), the immediate response includes protest (Gen 20:9), accountability-assumption (Gen 43:9, Gen 44:32), and confrontation-call (Mat 18:15). In VCG-04 (cultic), the immediate response is the realisation of guilt triggering the obligation to bring an offering (Lev 4:23 — "the sin which he has committed is made known to him"). The variation suggests that immediate response is shaped by the directional mode (God-directed vs interpersonal vs reflexive) and by whether the person is the agent or the recipient of the sinning.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The immediate-response evidence is consistent within the VCG-01 moral register: realisation → confession/remedy in Lev 5:5, Num 22:34, and the cultic remedy framework of Lev 4:2/Num 15:27/28. The 1Sa 14:33/34 verses show a slightly different pattern: Saul responds to the *report* of the people sinning by urgently stopping the behaviour ("You have dealt treacherously; roll a great stone to me here") — the immediate response is corrective action rather than personal confession, because Saul is the leader addressing corporate sinning rather than the sinner confessing personally. The VCG-02 cultic-purification verses evidence no inner personal response (the ritual is applied to objects, not persons). The response is consistent in the personal-moral register and absent in the cultic-object register.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The immediate response varies substantially depending on whether confession is genuine or hollow, and who receives it. Genuine individual confession to God (2Sa 24:10; Dan 9:5; Mic 7:9) is met with the expectation of divine response — Mic 7:9 ("until he pleads my cause") implies confident awaiting. Hollow confession (Deu 1:41) produces no external divine response — the people proceed on their own. Corporate confession (Judg 10:10/15; 1Sa 7:6/12:10) consistently triggers communal intercession and divine engagement. Person-directed confession (Mat 27:4) can be dismissed. The variation reveals that the immediate response is shaped by: (a) the genuineness of the confession (genuine vs hollow), (b) the direction of the confession (God vs persons), and (c) the recipient's own moral orientation.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The corpus shows consistent external responses of *divine or prophetic confrontation* with conscience suppression: Jer 2:35 (God announces judgment for the denial), Jer 16:10 (God has already declared judgment via the prophetic message that prompts the question), 1Cor 15:34 (Paul rebukes and calls to shame), Tit 3:11 (the divisive person is to be warned). The consistent response is that the external moral authority (God, prophet, apostle) supplies what the suppressed conscience cannot: the accurate moral verdict that the person's inner faculty is failing to produce.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The immediate response is consistent: the corpus shows no instance where the refusal-to-repent pattern is broken within the evidence presented. Every king formula ends with "did not depart from" — the confrontation with the available turn never produces the turn within these verse-portraits. Neh 9:29's "warned them... yet they acted presumptuously" — the warning is met by increased presumptuousness, not by turning. The consistency suggests that refusal to repent as a settled volitional disposition is highly resistant to immediate correction; its resolution, when it occurs, is not evidenced within the corpus of these 18 verses.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The corpus shows a consistent pattern: habitual defection does not yield to ordinary correction. Exo 9:34 (resumed sinning after plague-cessation), 1Sa 2:25 (non-listening to father), Heb 3:17 (40 years of sustained sinning despite divine provocation) — all show the pattern persisting under pressure, warning, and correction. The only structural break in the corpus is 1Jo 3:6's positive alternative: abiding in Christ breaks the pattern — but this requires a fundamental inner reorientation, not merely correction or warning. The immediate response to correction is consistently continued defection; only transforming union with Christ produces structural change.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The Kings corpus shows consistent compliance as the dominant response. Across 12+ king-formula repetitions, the pattern is: leader transmits the sinning direction → subsequent leaders and people follow. The exception is 2Ki 23:15's Josiah — who responds to the transmitted sinning legacy by demolishing its structural deposit rather than complying. Josiah's response is the outlier that confirms the pattern's consistency: every other response in the corpus is compliance or escalation; Josiah's demolition of the altar is the singular reversal. The variable is whether the response is compliance (dominant) or reversal (exceptional).

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Variable. Military response (2Ki 3:7), permanent fracture (1Ki 12:19; 2Ki 8:22), and the implicit context of 2Ch 21:10 (revolt as consequence of the ruler's spiritual state, without an immediate human response named) represent three different response patterns. The corpus shows no consistent single response: the specific authority relationship and political context shapes the response. What is consistent is that the revolt produces a recognisable break that is named and remembered — in every case the revolt is recorded as a significant political event with lasting consequence.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Variable. Judicial condemnation (VCG-02 — Mat 26:65; Mar 14:64), community correction imperatives (VCG-01 — Eph 4:31; Col 3:8), and shock/questioning (Mar 2:7 — "why does this man speak like that?") represent different immediate responses shaped by the relational and legal context. The VCG-03 beast context does not evidence an immediate human response — the blasphemy is the beast's constitutive orientation rather than an addressable speech-act.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Variable across the three mechanisms. Enticement's immediate response is being drawn toward the lure (Jam 1:14); hypocrisy's is social conformity (Gal 2:13); apostasy's is departure from covenantal standing (Act 21:21). Even within deleazō, the responses vary: Jam 1:14 describes the enticed person's inner drawing; 2Pe 2:14 describes the enticers' own inner formation; 2Pe 2:18 describes the targets' vulnerability. The characteristic's composite nature produces irreducible response variability across its three mechanisms.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Variable across VCG registers and contexts. Judgment (VCG-01 — wickedness meets divine response), wonder and resistance (VCG-02 — who can forgive?), and inner death-experience (VCG-03 — the law's arrival activates the condition's lethal force) are all distinct immediate responses. Within VCG-02, even the immediate response to forgiveness-declaration varies: some receive it with faith (Mat 9:2 — the paralytic's faith context), others question Jesus's authority (Mar 2:7), others wonder at his identity (Luk 7:49). The characteristic's universality means it is encountered differently depending on whether the person is under law, in unbelief, or in the context of the gospel's offer.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Variable depending on the person's constitutional state. For the un-born-again person: the enslaving power holds and the response is continued sinning (Joh 8:34 — slavery through practice; Rom 6:2 — "live in it"). For the born-of-God person: the enslaving power is structurally resisted (1Jo 3:9 — "cannot keep on sinning"; 1Jo 5:18 — "does not keep on sinning"). For the endangered person within the community: 1Jo 5:16 — prayer and life given through intercession — the response available is communal-intercessory.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Variable. Confession (Num 5:7; Psa 32:5), sorrow (Psa 38:18), and plea for pardon (Exo 10:17; Num 12:11) are the positive responses. But several verses show non-response or resistance: Jer 16:10 — the people cannot identify their sin when under judgment — the immediate response to the prophet's declaration is incomprehension rather than acknowledgment; Hos 12:8 — Ephraim denies the record ("they cannot find in me iniquity or sin") — self-deception is the immediate response. The response to the divine record depends on whether the conscience is engaged (confession/sorrow) or suppressed (denial/incomprehension).

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Variable. Love (Luk 7:47), life (Col 2:13), cleanness (Lev 16:30), and Spirit-reception (Act 2:38 — "you will receive the gift of the Holy Spirit") are all immediate responses named in the corpus. The variation reflects the different registers: the Levitical register names ritual purity-status (clean); the NT personal register names the affective and vital responses (love; alive); the Pentecost register names Spirit-reception. The consistent underlying element is relational restoration: forgiveness received restores the person to full standing before God, but this restoration is experienced differently across the corpus's registers.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Variable. 1Ki 8:47 and Jer 8:14 both show corporate confession as the immediate response in the exile-context. But Psa 78:17/32 shows the opposite: the immediate response to God's continued provision is *more sinning and unbelief*, not confession. The response thus depends on the moment in the generational cycle: in exile (where consequences are obvious), confession is the immediate response; in desert-provision (where consequences are not yet visible), persistent sinning is the immediate response.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Variable across the three VCG registers. VCG-01/02 authentic self-recognition produces prostration and plea (Luk 5:8; Luk 18:13). VCG-03 extreme sinner in judgment context produces dread and trembling (Isa 33:14). The extreme-type sinners of VCG-03 may have no recognition response at all during their sinning: Amo 9:10 — "who say, 'Disaster shall not overtake or meet us'" — the immediate response is presumptuous self-confidence, not recognition. The response thus varies from authentic self-abasement (Luk 5:8) through penitential appeal (Luk 18:13) to eschatological dread (Isa 33:14) to defiant denial (Amo 9:10).

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Variable. Shame (Ezr 9:6 — "I am ashamed and blush"), despair (Gen 4:13 — "greater than I can bear"), interpretive retrospection (Gen 42:21 — connecting past guilt to present suffering), and remedial initiative (Lev 6:4 — "realized his guilt and will restore") are all immediate inner responses evidenced. The variable response reflects the three guilt-registers: guilt-recognition in the Lev 4/5/6 priestly context produces remedial initiative; guilt-accumulation in Ezr 9 produces shame; guilt-as-punitive-weight in Gen 4 produces despair. The response type varies with the guilt-register experienced.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Variable. The conscience-engaged person responds with shame and plea (Ezr 9:6; 2Sa 24:10); the overwhelmed person responds with despair (Psa 40:12; Psa 38:4 — "too heavy for me"); the self-deceived person shows no immediate response at all — Hos 12:8 — "they cannot find in me iniquity" — the iniquity is present but produces no internal response because the conscience is suppressed. Amo 9:10's sinners (CHAR-16) — presuming no disaster will come — illustrate the response-less extreme. The immediate response thus ranges from acute conscience-awareness (2Sa 24:10) through overwhelming despair (Psa 40:12) to complete denial (Hos 12:8).

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Variable across the VCG registers. In the personal-awareness register (VCG-09 — Psa 51:3 — "I know my transgressions, and my sin is ever before me") the immediate response is honest self-recognition. In the revolt register (VCG-02 — Isa 1:5 — the people continue to rebel despite being struck down) the immediate response is defiant persistence. In the oppressive-weight register (VCG-07 — Eze 33:10 — "we rot away") the immediate response is despair. In the interpersonal register (VCG-08 — Pro 28:24 — "that is no transgression") the immediate response can be conscience-suppression. The response ranges from honest recognition (Psa 51:3) through defiance (Isa 1:5) to denial (Pro 28:24).

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Variable. Shame (Dan 9:7; Psa 25:3) is the appropriate affective response to recognised faithlessness. Grief and mourning (Ezr 9:4/10:6) is the prophetically-sensitive person's immediate response to witnessing others' faithlessness. Hardening (2Ch 28:22 — Ahaz becoming yet more faithless under distress) is the perverse immediate response of the constitutionally faithless person. Desolation (Lam 1:2 — weeping bitterly when friends deal treacherously) is the victim's immediate response to experienced faithlessness. The immediate response ranges from shame-to-repentance through grief-for-others through hardening to victimised desolation.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Variable. Confession and self-indictment (1Ki 8:47; Dan 9:5) are the productive responses. Deflection onto God appears in Pro 19:3 — "a man's folly brings his way to ruin, his heart rages against the Lord" — the immediate response to self-produced perversion is heart-rage against God rather than self-recognition. 2Pe 2:19 — those who promise freedom while enslaved to corruption — show no recognition response at all. Isa 29:16 — those who deny the creator — have an inverted response that produces further perversion rather than recognition. The range is from honest confession to deflection to complete non-recognition.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Variable by position. The victim's response is urgent appeal and vindication-seeking (Job 6:29; Psa 43:1). The righteous observer's response is the temptation toward fretful envy (Psa 37:1) — addressed by the psalmist's counsel not to fret. The unjust person's inner response is shameless absence of response (Zep 3:5). The witness with a functioning conscience responds by committing to remove injustice (Job 34:32 — "if I have done iniquity, I will do it no more").

---

### T1.5.3

**Question:** Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The evidence is not globally silent on immediate response (see T1.5.1 and T1.5.2), but the corpus is notably sparse on the immediate inner response of the sinning agent in the God-directed register (VCG-01). The verses in VCG-01 primarily record the fact of sinning and its consequences (national disaster, exile) rather than the sinning person's immediate inner experience of committing the act. Eze 18:4/20 declare outcome (death) without describing the sinner's immediate inner response at the moment of sinning. This silence may reflect the prophetic genre's interest in consequence over phenomenology.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The VCG-02 cultic-purification verses (Exo 29:36; Lev 8:15; Lev 9:15; Eze 43:20/22; Eze 45:18) are silent on inner personal response — because in this register no personal moral act is in view; the cha.ta verb applies to the cleansing of objects. This silence is expected given the register, not a gap in the evidence.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The corpus is not globally silent on immediate response (T1.5.1 and T1.5.2 show the range). The specific silence is on the confessor's immediate inner-being experience at the moment of speaking the confession — the corpus describes what comes before (conscience activated) and what comes after (plea, forgiveness, dismissal), but the moment of speaking itself is not described phenomenologically. The inner experience of the act of naming one's own sin is present in 2Sa 24:10 (heart-struck) but the moment of actual speech is not described separately from the surrounding conscience-activation.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The Ecclesiastes verses (Ecc 2:26; 8:12) and Job 35:6 do not evidence immediate response scenarios — they describe the state of conscience suppression as an observed condition (the sinner defined by not-pleasing-God, doing evil a hundred times) rather than as an encounter. The corpus is silent on the inner immediate response of the conscience-suppressed person themselves — they do not appear to experience an immediate internal response because the conscience that would generate it is suppressed.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The corpus is not silent on immediate response — the response is consistently continued refusal (T1.5.1 and T1.5.2). However, the inner phenomenological experience of the person who is refusing to repent — what it feels like from within — is not evidenced. The corpus describes the condition and its external expression (non-departure) but not the person's inner experience of the moment of confrontation.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The inner phenomenological experience of the person within habitual defection — what the pattern feels like from within — is not evidenced in the corpus. The corpus describes the condition (settled direction toward sin) and its external markers (altars multiplied, non-listening, sinning yet again) but does not describe the inner subjective experience of being habitually oriented toward sin.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The inner phenomenological experience of the community members receiving the transmitted sin — what it feels like from within to be formed toward sin by a leader's authority — is not described in the corpus. The corpus describes the outcomes (Israel sinning, following the Lord being abandoned) but not the subjective inner experience of the transmission.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — The inner phenomenological experience of the revolting party — what the inner person experiences in the moment of revolt — is not described in the corpus. The corpus describes the political-military facts and consequences of revolt, not the inner subjective experience of the decision to revolt.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The inner phenomenological experience of the person who commits sinful speech — what they experience in the moment of blasphemy or slander — is not described in the corpus. The corpus describes the acts, their origins (the heart — Mat 15:19; conceit — 1Ti 6:4), and the responses they provoke, but not the inner experience of the speaker in the moment of sinful speech.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(S)*

**[CHAR-10]** S — The inner phenomenological experience of the person in the moment of being enticed, joining in hypocrisy, or departing from covenantal standing — what these mechanisms feel like from within — is not described in the corpus. The corpus describes the mechanisms and their consequences, not the inner subjective experience of undergoing them.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The inner phenomenological experience of the person who has not yet encountered the good news of the condition's remedy — what it feels like to live under sin's dominion without awareness of the gospel — is not directly described in the corpus. The corpus describes the condition (VCG-01/03), its remedy-announcement (VCG-02), and specific responses to the remedy-announcement, but not the raw subjective experience of living under the condition without reference to its remedy.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(S)*

**[CHAR-12]** S — The inner phenomenological experience of the person in the moment of sin's enslaving power taking hold — what it feels like from within to move from free practice to constituted slavery — is not described in the corpus. The corpus describes the structural state (slavery — Joh 8:34) and its prevention (new birth — 1Jo 3:9) but not the subjective experience of the enslavement process itself.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — For the many persons described as carrying the Jeroboam-sin legacy (VCG-04 — 46 verses of kings who "walked in the sins of Jeroboam and did not depart"), the immediate inner response to the record is not described. The corpus characterises their conduct and its consequences but not the moment-by-moment subjective experience of carrying the recorded sin-pattern.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — For the kip.pu.rim atonement passages (VCG-01 — Exo 29:36; 30:10/16; Lev 23:27/28; 25:9; Num 5:8; 29:11; 2Ch 29:23/24), the immediate inner response of the individual receiving the atonement's benefit is not described. The corpus characterises the ritual mechanism and its purpose but not the individual worshipper's moment-by-moment inner experience of the atonement's completion.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — For the prophetic passages (Isa 43:27; Isa 64:5; Isa 65:20; Eze 37:23), the immediate inner response of the person who hears the naming of the generational pattern is not directly described. The naming of the first father's sin (Isa 43:27) and the prolonged-sin condition (Isa 64:5) describe the condition without specifying the hearer's immediate inner response.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — For the social-stigma sinner-category (VCG-01 — Mat 9:10; Luk 15:1/2; Luk 7:37) — the sinners who draw near to Jesus, recline at table, or approach with ointment — the immediate inner response of receiving the sinner-label from others is not directly described. The corpus characterises their behaviour (drawing near, reclining, approaching) but not the moment-by-moment inner experience of bearing the externally assigned sinner-identity.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — For the communal accumulated guilt contexts (VCG-02 — 2Ch 24:18; 2Ch 28:10/13; 1Ch 21:3), the immediate inner response of the individual community-members to the collectively incurred guilt is not described. The corpus names the guilt and its communal consequences (divine wrath) but not the individual's moment-by-moment inner experience of bearing the community's accumulated guilt-weight.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — For the generational-transmission register (VCG-02 — Exo 20:5; Deu 5:9; Lev 26:39-43), the immediate inner response of individual community members to inherited iniquity from ancestors is not described. The corpus names the transmission and its consequences (rotting in exile — Lev 26:39) but not the moment-by-moment inner experience of the person discovering they bear their fathers' iniquity as a personal burden.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — For the threshold-accumulation register (VCG-03 — Amos 1:3/6/9 — nations whose transgressions are counted toward judgment), the immediate inner response of the transgressing nations to their own accumulation is not described. The corpus names the transgressions and the divine judgment-threshold but not the moment-by-moment inner experience of Damascus, Gaza, Tyre, Edom, Moab, Ammon, Judah, and Israel as they commit and accumulate their counted transgressions.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — For VCG-03's constitutional-character register (Isa 24:16; Isa 33:1; Isa 48:8; Jer 3:8/11), the immediate inner response of the person who has been characterised by treachery from before birth (Isa 48:8) to their own constitutional unfaithfulness is not described. The corpus names the identity and its divine foreknowledge but not the moment-by-moment inner experience of the person constitutionally given over to faithlessness.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — For VCG-04's sexual perversion (Lev 18:23/20:12 — bestiality and incest named "perversion"), the immediate inner experience of the person committing these acts is not described. The corpus names the acts and their classification as perversion and their penalty (death) but not the inner recognition or response of the one committing them.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — For VCG-01's judicial context (Eze 18:8 — "withholds his hand from injustice") and commercial context (Lev 19:35 — "do no wrong in judgment, in measures"), the immediate inner experience of the person who is actively withholding their hand is described in the negative (what they don't do) rather than the positive inner-experience dimension. The corpus names the restrained act but not the inner sensation of restraining.

---

## T1.6 — Sustained Effect

### T1.6.1

**Question:** What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Sustained wilful sinning produces three evidenced trajectories in the inner being. (1) *Escalating compulsion*: Hos 4:7 ("the more they increased, the more they sinned against me") and Hos 13:2 ("they sin more and more, and make for themselves metal images") show sinning intensifying with each repetition — a self-reinforcing dynamic where the will's engagement with wrongdoing makes subsequent sinning more likely and more elaborate. (2) *Corporate moral deformation*: Isa 1:4 describes a "sinful nation, a people laden with iniquity" — collective identity reshaped around sinning, with estrangement from God as the settled condition. (3) *Accumulation of debt and consequence*: 1Ki 8:33/35/50 show sinning accumulating into a record that triggers defeat, drought, and captivity — sustained sinning produces a weight of consequence that falls on communities and individuals.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The corpus for CHAR-2 is primarily an act-and-remedy corpus — it does not evidence sustained-effect trajectories in the way CHAR-1 (escalating sinning) does. The Levitical framework (Lev 4:2; Num 15:27/28) addresses individual occurrences rather than a pattern that produces inner-being states over time. The sustained-effect evidence that is present: Lev 4:3 ("the anointed priest who sins, thus bringing guilt on the people") shows that repeated priestly sinning would accumulate communal guilt — a sustained inner-being effect on the community (collective guilt-load). The Eze 43/45 purification corpus suggests that sacred spaces accumulate defilement over time requiring periodic remediation — a sustained ritual-contamination dynamic. Within the personal-moral register, the corpus is predominantly episodic rather than developmental.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The corpus evidences two trajectories from sustained confession. (1) *Moral clarity and self-knowledge*: Dan 9:5's cascade — "sinned and done wrong and acted wickedly and rebelled, turning aside from your commandments" — is itself a sustained differentiation of the multiple dimensions of moral failure. Extended confession produces greater inner articulation of what the sin was and how it operated. (2) *Expectation of vindication*: Mic 7:9 — "I will bear the indignation of the Lord because I have sinned against him, until he pleads my cause" — the sustained posture of confession opens toward a confident future orientation. Job 33:27 — "I sinned and perverted what was right, and it was not repaid to me" — the restored man who has confessed publicly now bears the memory of sin that was not punished: a grace-shaped self-knowledge.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The corpus evidences two sustained trajectories. (1) *Accumulated judgment*: Jer 2:35 — God will bring judgment; the sinning that has gone unacknowledged accumulates as a growing liability before God. Jer 16:10 — the people face "all this great evil" as the consequence of the sin they did not recognise. The inner-being consequence is not felt within the conscience-suppressed state but accumulates externally as judgment. (2) *Moral warping*: Tit 3:11 — "warped and sinful" — sustained conscience suppression produces a constitutional deformation of character. The person who habitually refuses the conscience's verdict becomes progressively distorted inwardly — the warping is the long-term inner-being consequence of sustained suppression.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Two sustained inner-being effects are evidenced. (1) *Constitutional hardening*: Neh 9:29's "stubborn shoulder and stiffened their neck" is the end-state of sustained refusal — the bodily-metaphor names a constitutional posture of resistance that has become characteristic. The stiffening is a formed disposition, not a single act. (2) *Loss of prior standing*: Eze 18:24 — "none of the righteous deeds that he has done shall be remembered" — sustained refusal to repent (turning from righteousness to sin) produces the erasure of the prior moral record. Eze 33:12 — "the righteous shall not be able to live by his righteousness when he sins" — prior righteousness cannot sustain the person who has entered persistent sinning.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Two sustained inner-being effects. (1) *Progressive will-hardening*: Exo 9:34 — "sinned yet again and hardened his heart" — each iteration of sinning produces a harder inner disposition; the pattern is self-reinforcing and self-deepening. (2) *Structural blindness to God*: 1Jo 3:6 — "no one who keeps on sinning has either seen him or known him" — sustained habitual sinning produces or reveals a fundamental inability to perceive and know God. The sustained effect is not merely moral but epistemic-relational: the habitual sinner cannot see God.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Two sustained inner-being effects. (1) *Progressively diverted allegiance*: 2Ki 17:21 — "drove Israel from following the Lord" — the sustained effect is the progressive movement of the community's inner allegiance away from God. Over generations of leadership transmitting the same sinning direction, the community's inner orientation is increasingly shaped away from God-following. (2) *Escalating provocation of God*: 1Ki 14:22 — "more than all that their fathers had done" — sustained contagious sin across generations produces not stable sinning but escalating sinning; each generation receiving the transmitted sin adds to it, producing an escalating relational offence against God.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — The corpus evidences *persistent political fracture* as the sustained consequence. 1Ki 12:19 / 2Ch 10:19 — "Israel has been in rebellion against the house of David to this day" — the revolt produces an ongoing relational rupture that persists indefinitely. 2Ki 8:22 / 2Ch 21:10 — "Edom revolted from the rule of Judah to this day" — similarly permanent. The sustained inner-being consequence for the revolting community is: a settled condition of political independence from the prior governing relationship, which has become a permanent identity marker ("to this day").

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Two sustained inner-being trajectories. (1) *Progressive inner corruption deepened by the speech that expresses it*: 1Ti 6:4 — slander arising from conceit and unhealthy craving — the characteristic both expresses and reinforces the inner corruption that generated it; sustained slander deepens the diseased will. (2) *Permanent forfeiture of forgiveness in the unforgivable case*: Mat 12:31 — "the blasphemy against the Spirit will not be forgiven" — sustained and definitive blasphemy against the Spirit produces an irreversible inner condition: the permanent foreclosure of forgiveness.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — (1) *Enticement*: 2Pe 2:14 — "hearts trained in greed" — sustained enticement through desire produces a formed inner character: the heart has been deliberately trained toward sinful appetite, making enticement the person's natural operating mode. The mechanism becomes self-perpetuating: desire trained toward sin produces more susceptibility to desire-based enticement. (2) *Collective hypocrisy*: Gal 2:13 — "even Barnabas was led astray" — sustained collective hypocrisy corrupts the community's moral integrity; individuals lose their capacity for independent authentic identity. (3) *Apostasy*: Act 21:21 — "forsake Moses" — the departure from covenantal identity produces a person defined by the absence of the covenantal framework that previously constituted their identity.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Four sustained inner-being effects. (1) *Death*: Rom 6:23 — "the wages of sin is death" — the condition's sustained operation produces death as its final output; Eph 2:1 — "dead in trespasses and sins" — the sustained state is spiritual death. (2) *Hardening*: Heb 3:13 — "hardened by the deceitfulness of sin" — sustained operation of the universal condition through sin's deceitfulness progressively hardens the inner person against correction. (3) *Accumulation to full measure*: 1Th 2:16 — "filling up the measure of their sins" — the condition's sustained operation produces an accumulating offense before God that eventually reaches its full measure and triggers judgment. (4) *Insatiable appetite*: 2Ti 3:6 — "burdened with sins and led astray by various passions" — the condition produces a burdened inner person susceptible to multiple passions.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Two sustained inner-being effects. (1) *Constitutional slavery*: Joh 8:34 — "a slave to sin" — the sustained practice of sinning produces a constituted inner state of slavery; what began as acts becomes a governing inner identity-condition. (2) *Allegiance-redirection to the devil*: 1Jo 3:8 — "is of the devil, for the devil has been sinning from the beginning" — sustained sinning moves the person's deepest allegiance-marker from God-image to devil-identification; the enslaving power over time produces a comprehensive identity-reorientation at the deepest constitutional level.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Four sustained inner-being effects. (1) *Separation from God*: Isa 59:2 — "your iniquities have made a separation between you and your God, and your sins have hidden his face from you" — accumulated record produces relational estrangement; (2) *Rotting and decay*: Eze 33:10 — "our sins are upon us, and we rot away because of them" — the accumulated record produces inner moral decay; (3) *Physical deterioration*: Psa 38:3 — "there is no soundness in my flesh... there is no health in my bones because of my sin" — the weight of the record produces bodily consequences over time; (4) *Loss of blessing*: Jer 5:25 — "your sins have kept good from you" — sustained accumulation of the record progressively closes off the positive divine provision.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Three sustained inner-being effects. (1) *Love as sustained orientation*: Luk 7:47 — "he who is forgiven little, loves little" — the magnitude of sustained love is proportional to the magnitude of forgiveness received; forgiveness produces love as an ongoing inner orientation; (2) *Life replacing death*: Col 2:13 — "dead in your trespasses... made alive" — the life produced by forgiveness received is a sustained constitutional change, not a momentary affect; (3) *Spirit indwelling*: Act 2:38 — "you will receive the gift of the Holy Spirit" — the Spirit's indwelling following forgiveness is the most significant sustained inner-being consequence in the NT register.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Three sustained inner effects. (1) *Prolonged condition of sinning*: Isa 64:5 — "in our sins we have been a long time" — the sustained inner state is one of persistent sin-conditionedness over an extended period; (2) *Unbelief resistant to evidence*: Psa 78:32 — "in spite of all this, they still sinned; despite his wonders, they did not believe" — sustained generational sinning produces a hardened unbelief that does not yield to divine demonstration; (3) *Corporate doom*: Jer 8:14 — "the Lord our God has doomed us to perish... because we have sinned" — the sustained sinning produces an inner sense of hopelessness and doom within the corporate community.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Three sustained inner-being effects. (1) *Moral totality*: Gen 13:13 — "great sinners against the Lord" — sustained sinfulness produces a totality of moral character defined by sin; the individual identity becomes comprehensively sinful rather than partially; (2) *Self-deceived presumption*: Amo 9:10 — "who say, 'Disaster shall not overtake or meet us'" — sustained sinner-identity produces a false inner sense of security; the habitual sinner stops perceiving the threat that their condition poses; (3) *Wandering from truth*: Jam 5:20 — "whoever brings back a sinner from his wandering" — the sustained sinner-identity is characterised as an ongoing directional drift away from truth toward death.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Four sustained inner-being effects. (1) *Increasing accumulation*: 2Ch 33:23 — "Amon incurred guilt more and more" — the sustained guilt-state grows over time without address; (2) *Physical incapacitation*: Ezr 9:6 — "I am ashamed and blush to lift my face to you" — the posture of guilt cannot lift its face before God; Eze 33:10 (CHAR-13 context) — rotting away; (3) *False-heart-deepening*: Hos 10:2 — "their heart is false; now they must bear their guilt" — the sustained guilt-state accompanies and deepens a false inner disposition; (4) *Inner stumbling*: Hos 5:5 — "Israel and Ephraim shall stumble in his guilt" — the sustained guilt-weight causes the person to lose moral footing progressively.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Four sustained inner-being effects. (1) *Progressive accumulation toward threshold*: 2Ch 28:13 (cross-ref) — "our guilt is already great, and there is fierce wrath against Israel" — the sustained accumulation intensifies toward crisis; Gen 15:16 — "not yet complete" — the accumulation is ongoing; (2) *Bodily and vital decay*: Psa 31:10 — "my strength fails because of my iniquity, and my bones waste away" — sustained iniquity produces bodily deterioration; (3) *Increasing moral blindness*: Psa 36:2 — the wicked person "flatters himself in his own eyes that his iniquity cannot be found out" — sustained iniquity deepens self-deception; (4) *Self-destructive entrapment*: Pro 5:22 — "the iniquities of the wicked ensnare him, and he is held fast in the cords of his sin" — the sustained iniquity produces a self-created bondage from which the person cannot free himself.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Four sustained inner-being effects. (1) *Systemic inner collapse*: Isa 1:5 — "the whole head is sick, and the whole heart faint" — sustained revolt produces comprehensive inner-being deterioration; (2) *Enslaving bondage*: Pro 29:6 — "an evil man is ensnared in his transgression" — the accumulated transgression becomes the trap; Lam 1:14 — "bound into a yoke... set upon my neck... my strength to fail" — the sustained burden produces physical and volitional incapacitation; (3) *Identity-level characterisation*: Isa 48:8 — "from before birth called a rebel" — sustained transgression becomes the defining identity label; Isa 57:4 — "children of transgression" — generationally transmitted; (4) *Moral blindness toward God*: Jer 2:29 — "you have all transgressed against me" yet they "contend" with God — the sustained transgressor has lost accurate moral self-assessment.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Four sustained inner-being effects. (1) *Progressive hardening*: 2Ch 28:22 — "in the time of his distress he became yet more faithless" — the sustained disposition deepens rather than breaks; the will's faithlessness becomes more entrenched the more it is enacted; (2) *Eventual ruin*: Pro 11:3 — "the crookedness of the treacherous destroys them"; Pro 13:15 — "the way of the treacherous is their ruin"; Pro 11:6 — "the treacherous are taken captive by their lust" — the sustained treachery produces the destruction of the self; (3) *Exile and desolation*: 1Ch 9:1 — Judah exiled "because of their breach of faith"; 2Ch 30:7 — "he made them a desolation"; Dan 9:7 — "open shame... in all the lands to which you have driven them"; (4) *Communal pollution*: 2Ch 36:14 — "exceedingly unfaithful... polluted the house of the Lord" — sustained faithlessness corrupts what the person is entrusted to protect.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Four sustained inner-being effects. (1) *Progressive corruption through desire*: Eph 4:22 — "corrupt through deceitful desires" — ongoing active corruption; (2) *Enslavement to the corrupting force*: 2Pe 2:19 — "slaves of corruption. For whatever overcomes a person, to that he is enslaved" — the sustained perversion produces volitional captivity; (3) *Destruction by one's own instincts*: Jude 10 — "destroyed by all that they, like unreasoning animals, understand instinctively" — the perversion produces self-destruction through unreasoning impulse; (4) *Deprivation of truth*: 1Ti 6:5 — "depraved in mind and deprived of the truth" — sustained mind-perversion produces the inability to access truth.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Four sustained effects. (1) *Thoroughgoing internalization*: Job 15:16 — "drinks injustice like water" — sustained injustice produces the condition where wrongdoing is as natural as drinking; (2) *Shamelessness*: Zep 3:5 — "the unjust knows no shame" — the conscience's shame-response is eliminated; (3) *Calamity*: Pro 22:8 — "whoever sows injustice will reap calamity; the rod of his fury will fail" — sustained injustice produces proportionate self-destruction; (4) *Exclusion from God's kingdom*: 1Cor 6:9 — "the unrighteous will not inherit the kingdom of God" — the sustained character of injustice forecloses the eschatological inheritance.

---

### T1.6.2

**Question:** What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The sustained-effect evidence points to: (1) *Vulnerability to temptation*: Neh 13:26 — Solomon's sustained exposure to foreign women produced a sinning that "even him" — the beloved and gifted king — could not resist, suggesting that sustained sinning erodes the will's resistance capacity. (2) *Estrangement from God*: Isa 1:4 ("they have forsaken the Lord, they have despised the Holy One of Israel, they are utterly estranged") describes a settled orientation of alienation as the outcome of sustained national sinning. (3) *Increased elaborateness of idolatry*: Hos 13:2 — sinning "more and more" produces "metal images, idols skillfully made" — an escalating investment in what replaces God. (4) *Moral weight on subsequent generations*: Neh 13:26 (Solomon's foreign-women vulnerability), the cultic-atonement system's communal dimension (Lev 4:3 — "if it is the anointed priest who sins, thus bringing guilt on the people") suggest that sustained sinning by leaders creates a moral weight borne by communities.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-2]** S — The 18-verse corpus provides insufficient evidence to characterise the sustained inner-being effects of repeated unintentional sinning on the inner person. The Levitical system's standing provision for unintentional sin (daily altar purification: Exo 29:36; annual sanctuary purification: Eze 45:18) implies that the accumulated effect of unintentional violations on the person and community requires ongoing remedial attention — but the corpus does not describe the inner-being state produced by this accumulation. This is a genuine evidential silence within the CHAR-2 corpus.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Sustained genuine confession establishes: (1) *Moral transparency before God*: Neh 1:6 — "confessing... day and night" — a posture of ongoing moral openness toward God that refuses accumulation of unacknowledged sin. (2) *Capacity for intercession*: Daniel's confession (Dan 9:5/8/11/15) is simultaneously a personal and an intercessory act — he names his own sin and his community's, establishing the intercessor's posture of identifying with those for whom he pleads. (3) *Humility of self-assessment*: 1Ch 21:17 — "It is I who have sinned" — sustained ownership of personal sin rather than displacement builds the inner quality of honest self-accountability.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Sustained conscience suppression establishes: (1) *Self-deception as a settled inner orientation*: Jer 2:35 — claiming "I am innocent" moves from a single false claim to a settled self-understanding that has lost contact with moral reality. (2) *Constitutional warping*: Tit 3:11 — "warped" names a deformation of the inner person's basic moral structure — the continued refusal of conscience's witness reshapes the inner person away from moral accuracy. (3) *Spiritual stupor*: 1Cor 15:34 — "drunken stupor" as the sustained state — moral alertness is progressively diminished until the person is in a state analogous to intoxication. (4) *Knowledge-absence*: 1Cor 15:34 — "some have no knowledge of God" — sustained suppression of the conscience and of God-knowledge reinforce each other, producing a settled epistemic blindness about God and self.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Sustained refusal to repent establishes: (1) *Inherited moral orientation received and kept*: 2Ki 15:9 — "as his fathers had done. He did not depart from the sins of Jeroboam" — the inherited sinful pattern is accepted and sustained, becoming one's own moral orientation through continued non-departure. (2) *Lifelong directional commitment*: 2Ki 15:18 — "all his days" — refusal to repent produces a whole-life orientation. (3) *Increasing entrenching of the will in the sinful direction*: 2Ki 3:3's "clung to" describes an active inner relationship with the sin — sustained refusal creates a bond between the will and the sinful course. (4) *Closed-off divine remedy*: Heb 10:26 — sustained deliberate sinning after knowing truth forecloses the sacrifice — the most severe consequence of refusal to repent.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Sustained habitual defection establishes: (1) *Moral identity as "the sinner"*: the Ecclesiastes person-type (Ecc 7:26; 9:2/18; Pro 11:31/13:22) describes someone whose moral identity has been constituted by the sinning pattern — the sinner is a type, a settled orientation, not merely an occasional actor. (2) *Vulnerability to entrapment*: Ecc 7:26 — "the sinner is taken by her" — the habitual sinner lacks the inner resource to escape the snare; the established sinning pattern has removed the dispositional capacity to resist. (3) *Destructive capacity*: Ecc 9:18 — "one sinner destroys much good" — the sustained sinning orientation gives the habitually sinning person a negative formative power disproportionate to their number: one established sinner can undo much accumulated good.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Sustained contagious sin establishes: (1) *Institutional structures that become self-perpetuating*: 2Ki 23:15 — Jeroboam's altar at Bethel is still standing generations after Jeroboam's death, still transmitting the sinning orientation; (2) *Communal identity shaped around the sinning direction*: 2Ki 21:11 — Manasseh's abominations have shaped Judah's communal moral identity — "has made Judah also to sin with his idols"; (3) *Generational transmission*: 1Ki 22:52 — Ahaziah follows "the way of his father and... his mother and... Jeroboam the son of Nebat, who made Israel to sin" — three generations of transmitted sinning orientation each contributing to the received pattern.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Sustained political revolt establishes: (1) *Settled political independence*: 2Ki 8:20 — "set up a king of their own" — the revolting community establishes its own governing structure as an ongoing reality; (2) *Permanent relational fracture*: the "to this day" markers (1Ki 12:19; 2Ki 8:22) name a fracture that has become the permanent state of the relationship; (3) *In 2Ch 21:10's causal context*: the fracture is embedded in a spiritual-moral framework — the ruler's forsaking of God has produced a political environment in which loyalty structures break down.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Sustained sinful speech establishes: (1) *Diseased inner craving and conceit*: 1Ti 6:4 — sustained slander from conceit entrenches the conceit; the speaking reinforces the pride that generated it; (2) *Constitutive anti-God identity*: VCG-03 — the beast's sustained blasphemy (Rev 13:5 — "for forty-two months") establishes the creature's total identity around defiance of God; (3) *2Ti 3:2's end-times character*: the blasphemous disposition is the settled character of persons who have given themselves to self-love — the speech-pattern is the established character-type.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — (1) *Enticement*: 2Pe 2:14 — "insatiable for sin" and "hearts trained in greed" — sustained enticement establishes a state of insatiability (desire that cannot be satisfied) and a trained inner character oriented toward sinful appetite; (2) *Collective hypocrisy*: sustained participation in collective hypocrisy establishes community-level inauthenticity — Gal 2:13's "led astray" implies that the authentic communal identity has been replaced by the performed one as the operating norm; (3) *Apostasy*: sustained departure from covenantal identity establishes a new identity defined by the departure — the person who has forsaken Moses is now in a position of non-covenantal standing.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The condition establishes: (1) *Spiritual deadness*: Eph 2:1 — "dead in trespasses and sins" — the condition as a settled state of inner spiritual non-life; (2) *Total enslavement*: Rom 6:20 — "when you were slaves of sin, you were free in regard to righteousness" — the condition's total orientation away from righteousness; (3) *The law of sin*: Rom 7:23 — "the law of sin that dwells in my members" — the condition as an established counter-authority within the person; (4) *Separation from the glory of God*: Rom 3:23 — "fall short of the glory of God" — the condition as a settled deficiency from the person's intended end.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Three sustained orientations. (1) *Slave-identity*: Joh 8:34 — the enslaved person's identity is now constituted around the master-slave relationship with sin; (2) *Devil-allegiance*: 1Jo 3:8 — "of the devil" — the identity-marker declares the person's deepest belonging; (3) *Death-trajectory*: 1Jo 5:16 — "sin that leads to death" — the most severe form of sin-enslavement establishes a trajectory toward eschatological death; the sustained enslavement moves the person toward the condition where intercessory prayer is unavailing.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Three established states. (1) *Accuser-testimony state*: Isa 59:12 — "our sins testify against us" — the accumulated record becomes a self-generating accusation that cannot be silenced; (2) *Hardened-face state*: Isa 3:9 — "they proclaim their sin like Sodom; they do not hide it" — when the record has grown extensive enough, conscience no longer restrains its display; the face itself bears witness to the interior record; (3) *Divine-memory vigilance state*: Jer 14:10 — "he will remember their iniquity and punish their sins" — the sustained record places the person in a state of pending divine reckoning; the record awaits its appointed day of visitation (Exo 32:34).

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — (1) *Cleanness before God*: Lev 16:30 — "clean before the Lord from all your sins" — the established condition of ritual-relational purity; (2) *Love-orientation*: Luk 7:47 — love as the sustained inner disposition of the forgiven person; (3) *Life-orientation*: Col 2:13 — made alive as the constitutional orientation replacing the death-in-trespasses state; (4) *Redemption-identity*: Col 1:14 — "in whom we have redemption, the forgiveness of sins" — redemption as the established identity of the forgiven person; Eph 1:7 — "in him we have redemption through his blood, the forgiveness of our trespasses, according to the riches of his grace."

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Three established states. (1) *Prolonged sin-conditionedness*: Isa 64:5 — "a long time in our sins" — the settled inner state of being-in-sin across generations; (2) *Rebellion-oriented inner disposition*: Psa 78:17 — "rebelling against the Most High" — the sustained sinning establishes a rebellious inner orientation toward God rather than trust; (3) *Defilement*: Eze 37:23 — "they shall not defile themselves anymore" — the sustained backslidings have produced a state of inner defilement that requires divine cleansing before it can be reversed.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Three established states. (1) *Constituted social exclusion*: Psa 1:5 — "sinners will not stand in the congregation of the righteous" — the sustained identity produces structural exclusion from the covenant community; (2) *Transactional inner orientation*: Luk 6:32/33/34 — sinners love only those who love them, do good only to those who do good, lend only expecting return — the sustained identity establishes a calculating, self-centred inner orientation; (3) *Divine-hearing cut-off*: Joh 9:31 — "God does not listen to sinners" — the sustained identity severs the communication channel with God.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Three established states. (1) *Shame-posture*: Ezr 9:6 — "I am ashamed and blush to lift my face to you, my God" — sustained guilt establishes a bodily-inner posture of shame and face-hiding before God; (2) *Inability to stand*: Ezr 9:15 — "none can stand before you because of this" — sustained guilt establishes a standing-disability before God; (3) *Punitive expectation*: 2Ki 7:9 — "punishment will overtake us" — sustained guilt-consciousness establishes an inner orientation of expecting punishment; the conscience is attuned to the punitive consequences of the guilt-burden.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Three established states. (1) *Separation from God*: Isa 59:2 — "your iniquities have made a separation between you and your God, and your sins have hidden his face from you so that he does not hear" — sustained iniquity establishes structural relational distance from God; (2) *Moral self-deception*: Psa 36:2 — "he flatters himself in his own eyes that his iniquity cannot be found out and hated" — sustained iniquity establishes a false inner self-assessment; Hos 12:8 — the wealthy Ephraim's claim of clean hands alongside real iniquity; (3) *Ruinous self-destruction*: Eze 18:30 — "lest iniquity be your ruin" — the sustained iniquity establishes the ruin-trajectory as the person's inner direction.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Three established states. (1) *Settled inner rebellion as orientation*: Eze 2:3 — "nations of rebels who have transgressed against me... from their fathers to this very day" — sustained transgression establishes multigenerational rebellion as the default orientation; (2) *Self-justifying posture*: Jer 2:29 — "why do you contend with me?" — the sustained transgressor adopts a self-justifying inner stance toward God; Pro 28:24 — "that is no transgression" — the sustained sinner develops an inner narrative that suppresses conscience; (3) *Separation from God's ways*: Hos 14:9 — "transgressors stumble in them" — sustained transgression establishes a constitutive incompatibility with God's right ways.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Three established states. (1) *Crookedness of character*: Pro 11:3 — "the crookedness of the treacherous" — sustained faithlessness establishes a constitutive inner moral distortion; (2) *Capture by lust*: Pro 11:6 — "the treacherous are taken captive by their lust" — sustained treachery establishes an inner captivity to craving as the driving force of the will; (3) *Desire for violence*: Pro 13:2 — "the desire of the treacherous is for violence" — the sustained faithless orientation establishes appetite for harm as the settled inner drive.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Three established states. (1) *Delight in perversity*: Pro 2:14 — "who rejoice in doing evil and delight in the perverseness of evil" — sustained perversion establishes an affective orientation of joy-in-wrongdoing; (2) *Continual evil-devising*: Pro 6:14 — "continually sowing discord" — sustained perversity produces unceasing destructive scheming; (3) *Bondage to corruption*: Rom 8:21 — "bondage to corruption" — the created order itself is in sustained enslaved-corruption as a structural condition.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Three established states. (1) *The unjust as fixed character-type*: Luk 16:10 — dishonest in very little and in much — a stable inner character that does not vary with scale or circumstance; (2) *God-ignorance*: Job 18:21 — "the place of him who knows not God" defines the unjust person's constitutive spiritual blindness; Psa 53:1 — "the fool says in his heart, 'There is no God'... doing abominable iniquity" — godlessness and injustice as mutually constituting states; (3) *Standing under divine custody*: 2Pe 2:9 — "keep the unrighteous under punishment until the day of judgment" — the sustained unjust character produces sustained divine custody.

---

### T1.6.3

**Question:** Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The sustained effect differs markedly from the immediate response. The immediate response (T1.5.1) is moral recognition — conscience registering the act. The sustained effect is compound: escalating compulsion (Hos 4:7; 13:2), estrangement (Isa 1:4), and consequence-accumulation (1Ki 8:33–50). The critical difference is directional: the immediate response includes conscience-active elements that resist or protest sinning, whereas the sustained effect shows conscience being progressively overridden — the will habituates to sinning and the moral recognition becomes less operative. This difference is the evidence base for the programme's distinction between CHAR-1 (wilful sinning as act) and CHAR-5 (refusal to repent) / CHAR-6 (habitual defection) — sustained wilful sinning without repentance migrates toward the habitual-defection register.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Within the evidenced material: the immediate response (realisation → confession → remedy) operates at the level of specific episodes. The standing cultic-remedy institutions (Exo 29:36 daily offering; Eze 45:18 annual sanctuary purification) operate at the sustained level — they address the ongoing accumulation of inadvertent defilement that episodic confession alone cannot clear. This suggests that even the act-by-act immediate response is insufficient as a complete remedy for the sustained effect of unintentional sinning in a community; the institutional purification system addresses what the episodic response leaves unremediated.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Yes. The immediate response of confession (heart-struck conscience, verbal naming, plea) is episodic. The sustained effect is formative: a person who habitually confesses sin promptly (2Sa 24:10 shows David's pattern — "heart struck him" → immediate confession to God) develops a conscience that fires readily and a will that responds to it without long delay. The sustained effect thus shapes the inner person's moral responsiveness — confession practiced over time forms a more sensitive conscience and a more ready will. The immediate response is a single moral event; the sustained effect is character formation in moral transparency.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The distinction is significant. There is effectively no immediate internal response within the conscience-suppressed person (the conscience is not producing the alerting signal). The sustained effect, by contrast, is substantial: accumulated judgment (Jer 2:35), constitutional warping (Tit 3:11), spiritual stupor (1Cor 15:34), and the progressive loss of moral self-knowledge (Jer 16:10 — a condition apparently reached over generational time). The sustained effect is what conscience suppression *does to the person* from the outside-in (judgment accumulates) and from the inside-out (the person is progressively deformed).

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The immediate response is continued non-departure (the same refusal maintained). The sustained effect adds to this: the will becomes increasingly entrenched (from "did not depart" → "clung to" → "stubborn shoulder"), and the external consequences accumulate (loss of standing — Eze 18:24; foreclosure of remedy — Heb 10:26). The sustained effect thus shows a *directional deepening*: not only does the will continue in its refusal, but the refusal becomes more entrenched, the will more captured, and the consequences more severe. What begins as non-departure can deepen into active clinging and constitutional hardening.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Yes. The immediate response to confrontation is continued non-departure (the sinning continues — Exo 9:34; 1Sa 2:25). The sustained effect is more structural: moral identity formation as "the sinner" (Ecc 7:26; 9:2; Pro 11:31); progressive loss of the capacity to resist moral entrapment (Ecc 7:26 — taken); and the total relational-epistemic consequence (1Jo 3:6 — never seen or known Christ). The sustained effect thus moves from the behavioural level (continuing to sin) to the constitutional and relational-epistemic level (formed as the sinner-type; unable to perceive God).

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Yes. The immediate response is compliance or escalation (walking in the transmitted sinning path). The sustained effect is structural: the sinning orientation becomes embedded in institutions (Jeroboam's altar — 2Ki 23:15) that outlast any individual leader and continue to transmit the sinning direction without requiring a new leader's active causative intent. The sustained effect transforms contagious sin from a leader-driven transmission event into a self-perpetuating structural reality. This structural persistence is why Josiah must physically demolish the altar (2Ki 23:15) rather than merely counter the leader's personal sinning — the structure has become the ongoing transmission mechanism.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Yes. The immediate response may include military engagement (2Ki 3:7 — seeking alliance against Moab). The sustained effect is the permanent fracture — the "to this day" condition. What begins as a decisive act of revolt becomes a settled political reality: Edom is no longer under Judah's rule; Israel is no longer under the Davidic house. The immediate action produces a permanent condition; the sustained effect is the institutionalisation of the break.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Yes. The immediate response is: judicial condemnation (VCG-02), community correction call (VCG-01). The sustained effect is: deepened inner corruption (1Ti 6:4 — conceit feeds on slander), constituted identity around the sinful speech pattern (VCG-03 — the beast's character), and the permanent foreclosure of forgiveness in the Spirit-blasphemy case (Mat 12:31). The sustained effect moves from the relational-consequential level (what others do in response) to the constitutional level (what the person becomes through sustained sinful speech).

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Yes. The immediate response is being drawn/lured (enticement), being led astray (hypocrisy), or departing (apostasy). The sustained effect is the formed character of 2Pe 2:14 ("hearts trained in greed"), the community's distorted integrity (Gal 2:13), or the established covenantal absence (Act 21:21). The sustained effect moves from the episodic (each act of enticement/hypocrisy/departure) to the constitutional (trained heart, corrupted community, absent covenantal standing).

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Yes. The immediate response to encountering the condition (wonder at Jesus — Luk 7:49; inner death-experience — Rom 7:9; divine judgment against the wicked — Mal 4:1) produces discrete events. The sustained effect is constitutional: the progressive hardening (Heb 3:13), the accumulating measure (1Th 2:16), the established deadness (Eph 2:1), the total enslavement (Rom 6:20) — these are the long-term constitutional outcomes of the condition's sustained operation. The immediate response is event-like; the sustained effect is structural.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Yes. The immediate response (continued sinning — Rom 6:1/2; the practice that produces the slavery — Joh 8:34) is the act-level. The sustained effect is constitutional: the person who has continued sinning is now a slave (a constituted identity), the allegiance is now to the devil (a deepened identity-marker), and the trajectory is toward death-through-sin (an eschatological consequence). The sustained effect moves from the behavioural to the constitutional and eschatological levels.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Yes. The immediate response is often confessional or grief-oriented (Num 5:7; Psa 38:18) — an acute response to the moment of recognition. The sustained effect is the gradual accumulation of separation from God (Isa 59:2), physical deterioration (Psa 38:3), and moral rotting (Eze 33:10). The sustained effect also involves the hardening of the face (Isa 3:9 — openly proclaimed without shame), suggesting that immediate conscience-engagement (acute response) gives way to diminished conscience over time if the record is not addressed.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Yes. The immediate response is the declaration or initial condition change (Lev 16:30 — clean; Luk 7:48 — sins forgiven; Col 2:13 — made alive). The sustained effect is the ongoing inner orientation that forgiveness produces over time: love (Luk 7:47 — the "much-love" that flows from much-forgiveness), Spirit indwelling (Act 2:38 — the permanent gift), and redemption-identity (Col 1:14; Eph 1:7 — the "we have redemption" that is a present permanent possession). The sustained effect deepens and extends what the immediate response initiates.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Yes. The immediate response (corporate confession in exile — 1Ki 8:47; Jer 8:14) is an episodic event. The sustained effects (prolonged sinning — Isa 64:5; hardened unbelief — Psa 78:32; defilement — Eze 37:23) are constitutional conditions that develop over the entire generational span. The immediate confession (acute) gives way to — or coexists with — the sustained condition that requires divine redemption to address (Eze 37:23).

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Yes. The immediate response (prostration — Luk 5:8; dread — Isa 33:14; defiant denial — Amo 9:10) is episodic.
