The sustained effects (moral totality — Gen 13:13; social exclusion — Psa 1:5; wandering — Jam 5:20; divine-hearing cut-off — Joh 9:31) are constitutional outcomes of the sustained sinner-identity over time. The immediate dread (episodic) gives way to either the soul-conversion of repentance (Luk 15:7 — joy over one sinner who repents) or the deepened presumption of the habitual extreme sinner (Amo 9:10 — denying disaster will come).

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Yes. The immediate response (shame — Ezr 9:6; despair — Gen 4:13; interpretive retrospection — Gen 42:21) is episodic. The sustained effects (accumulation — 2Ch 33:23; shame-posture — Ezr 9:6; inability to stand — Ezr 9:15; stumbling — Hos 5:5) are constitutional conditions that develop as the guilt-state persists without resolution. The sustained condition is more debilitating than the initial response: Ezr 9:6's shame produces Ezr 9:15's standing-disability, which is the accumulated inner effect of guilt that has been borne for generations (Ezr 9:7 — "from the days of our fathers").

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Yes. The immediate response (shame — Ezr 9:6; conscience-strike — 2Sa 24:10; despair — Psa 40:12) is episodic. The sustained effects (bodily decay — Psa 31:10; separation from God — Isa 59:2; moral self-deception — Psa 36:2; entrapment — Pro 5:22) are constitutional states established over time by unaddressed iniquity. The progression is: immediate shock of recognition → sustained accumulated weight → constitutional corruption of the inner person → ruination.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Yes. The immediate response (shame — Lam 1:22; awareness — Psa 51:3; defiance — Isa 1:5) is episodic. The sustained effects (inner collapse — Isa 1:5; enslaving bondage — Lam 1:14; identity-characterisation — Isa 48:8; moral blindness — Jer 2:29) are constitutional developments of the will over time. The progression is: wilful act → repeated acts → habit → constitutive inner orientation of rebellion → identity-level rebel label (Isa 48:8) → stumbling in God's right ways as settled pattern (Hos 14:9).

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Yes. The immediate response (shame — Dan 9:7; grief — Ezr 9:4; hardening — 2Ch 28:22) is episodic. The sustained effects (crookedness — Pro 11:3; captivity to lust — Pro 11:6; desire for violence — Pro 13:2; exile and desolation — 1Ch 9:1) are constitutional states established over time by unaddressed faithlessness. The most significant sustained effect is the progressive hardening: 2Ch 28:22's Ahaz — distress produced more faithlessness rather than repentance — the will has become constitutively set in the faithless direction and no longer responds to corrective pressure.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Yes. The immediate response (confession — 1Ki 8:47; self-indictment — Dan 9:5) is episodic. The sustained effects (active corruption through deceitful desires — Eph 4:22; enslavement — 2Pe 2:19; self-destruction by instinct — Jude 10; deprivation of truth — 1Ti 6:5) are constitutional states established over time. The most significant sustained effect is the transformation from agent-of-perversion to captive-of-corruption: 2Pe 2:19 — whatever overcomes a person enslaves them. The initial active perversion (the agent twisting) becomes passive enslavement (the corruption mastering the agent).

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Yes. The immediate response (victim's urgent plea — Job 6:29; Psa 43:1) is episodic. The sustained effects (water-drinking internalization — Job 15:16; shamelessness — Zep 3:5; fixed character-scale — Luk 16:10; divine custody — 2Pe 2:9) are constitutional states established through persistent injustice. The most significant shift: from the person who commits an act of injustice (Eze 18:24 — a righteous person who turns and commits injustice) to the person who IS the unjust (Luk 16:10 — the character-type whose dishonesty scales). The act-to-character trajectory is the defining sustained development of CHAR-22.

---

## T1.7 — Conditions of Reception

### T1.7.1

**Question:** What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — "Reception" requires clarification for this characteristic: wilful sinning is not received from outside in the way a gift or grace is received; it is generated by the person's own will. The inner conditions that enable its occurrence (rather than reception) are evidenced as: (1) *Absence of divine restraint*: Gen 20:6 — Abimelech sinned only in ignorance; God's external intervention prevented him. The absence of that restraint enables the will to proceed. (2) *Social pressure overriding conscience*: 1Sa 15:24 — Saul sinned because "I feared the people and obeyed their voice" — social pressure as the enabling condition that overrode the will's alignment with God's command. (3) *Vulnerability through exposure*: Neh 13:26 — foreign women as the corrupting influence that enabled Solomon's sinning. (4) *Temptation presenting the opportunity*: Neh 6:13 — enemies constructed a trap designed to produce sinning. These are conditions that the will then responds to by sinning.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The enabling conditions for unintentional sinning are primarily *epistemic* — lack of knowledge or awareness of the moral status of the act. Lev 4:2 ("sins unintentionally in any of the Lord's commandments about things not to be done") — the enabling condition is not knowing that the specific act was prohibited. Num 22:34 (Balaam — "I did not know that you stood in the road against me") — lack of perception of the morally relevant fact. The 1Sa 14:33/34 context (people eating meat with blood in the urgency of battle) suggests situational pressure or distraction as an enabling condition — the full remedy was rushed and the prohibition bypassed in the urgency. The enabling conditions are thus: limited knowledge, limited perception, situational distraction, and the finitude of creaturely awareness.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The corpus evidences four enabling conditions. (1) *Active conscience*: 2Sa 24:10 — "David's heart struck him" — the conscience must fire for confession to arise from within. Shimei (2Sa 19:20) — "your servant knows that I have sinned" — explicit inner knowledge driving the confession. (2) *Will's agreement to name the act as wrong*: 1Ch 21:17 — "It is I who have sinned and done great evil" — the will accepts responsibility without deflection. (3) *Awareness of a relational recipient*: confession is directional — the person must be oriented toward a recipient (God or person) to whom the naming is addressed (Luk 15:18 — the prodigal's first inner movement is toward his father). (4) *The absence of self-protective concern outweighing truthfulness*: genuine confession is distinguished from Saul's (1Sa 15:30) by the absence of self-interest driving the naming — David confesses without condition (2Sa 24:10/17).

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Three evidenced enabling conditions. (1) *Absence of the fear of God*: Ecc 8:12 — the sinner does evil a hundred times without the fear of God within — the fear of God's absence is the primary enabling condition for conscience-absent sinning. (2) *Self-interest in innocence*: Jer 2:35 — the person claims "I am innocent; surely his anger has turned from me" — the desire to believe oneself innocent (and free from divine anger) is an enabling condition for the active denial. (3) *Ignorance of God*: 1Cor 15:34 — "some have no knowledge of God" — the cognitive-spiritual absence of God-knowledge enables and sustains the stupor of continued sinning. These three (absence of fear of God, self-interested innocence-claim, ignorance of God) are the inner conditions that produce or sustain conscience suppression.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Three enabling conditions are evidenced. (1) *Inherited sinful orientation already in place*: the Kings pattern shows that each king "followed the sins of Jeroboam" — the inherited orientation is already established, and refusal to repent is simply its continuation. 2Ki 15:9 — "as his fathers had done" — the enabling condition is an inherited moral legacy that has been received and not rejected. (2) *Minimisation of established wickedness*: 1Ki 16:31 — "as if it had been a light thing for him to walk in the sins of Jeroboam" — moral minimisation of the gravity of the sinful course is the enabling condition for not departing from it. (3) *Partial obedience as substitute for turning*: 2Ki 10:29/31 — Jehu reformed in some areas but "did not turn from" in others — partial obedience enables continued refusal by providing the inner sense of having done enough.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Three enabling conditions. (1) *Pressure-relief cycles without inner reorientation*: Exo 9:34 — the plague ceasing is the enabling condition for Pharaoh's resumed sinning; the removal of external pressure allows the inner sinning disposition to re-express. The enabling condition is: no inner change during the relief period. (2) *Absence of the God-pleasing disposition*: Ecc 7:26 — the sinner "is taken" because he lacks what the God-pleaser has; the enabling condition is the absence of the God-oriented inner disposition that would enable escape. (3) *Fear of other gods / transferred allegiance*: 2Ki 17:7 — "sinned against the Lord their God... and had feared other gods" — the inner transfer of fear/allegiance from God to other objects enables the sustained pattern of defection.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Three evidenced enabling conditions in the leader. (1) *Personal inner commitment to the sinful course*: 1Ki 16:26 — "walked in all the way of Jeroboam" — the leader must be internally committed to the sinning direction; they cannot transmit what they do not themselves hold. (2) *Occupation of the authority position*: 1Ki 16:2 — "I exalted you out of the dust and made you leader over my people Israel" — the authority position is what makes the inner commitment's transmission effective. The same inner sinning commitment in a non-leader produces personal sinning (CHAR-1/5/6) rather than contagious sin. (3) *Active exercise of leadership toward the sinning direction*: 2Ki 17:21 — "Jeroboam drove Israel from following the Lord" — the active exercise of leadership energy in the sinning direction is the causative mechanism. Passive personal sinning without leadership-directed transmission does not produce CHAR-7.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Two evidenced enabling conditions. (1) *Perceived weakness of governing authority*: 2Ki 1:1 and 3:5 — both Moab revolts occur "after the death of Ahab" — the death of the strong authority figure creates the enabling condition for revolt; the perceived weakness of the successor authority makes revolt viable. (2) *Spiritual-authority vacuum in the governing authority*: 2Ch 21:10 — "because he had forsaken the Lord" — Jehoram's forsaking of God creates a spiritual-moral vacancy that enables the revolts of Edom and Libnah; when the governing authority has abandoned the spiritual foundation of legitimate rule, the subject peoples revolt.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Three enabling conditions. (1) *Corrupt heart*: Mat 15:19 — "out of the heart come evil thoughts... slander" — the corrupted heart is the primary enabling condition; (2) *Conceit and diseased craving*: 1Ti 6:4 — "puffed up with conceit... unhealthy craving for controversy" — pride and the appetite for controversy enable slander; (3) *Unbelief*: 1Ti 1:13 — Paul's former blasphemy arose from "ignorant unbelief" — the absence of saving knowledge of God removes the constraint against blasphemy. VCG-03's beast is the extreme form: total anti-God orientation as the constitutive enabling condition for constitutive blasphemy.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — (1) *Enticement*: Jam 1:14 — the enabling condition is the desire-faculty itself — "his own desire" is both the hook and the enabling condition; everyone has desire, making everyone susceptible; 2Pe 2:18 — "barely escaping from those who live in error" — residual vulnerability in those not yet firmly established is the specific enabling condition. (2) *Collective hypocrisy*: Gal 2:13 — the enabling condition is the social pressure of peer conformity combined with the presence of a prominent figure (Peter) modelling the hypocrisy; the social weight of the collective makes individual resistance difficult. (3) *Apostasy*: Act 21:21 — the enabling condition is the existence of a covenantal identity that can be abandoned; the mechanism requires a prior covenantal standing from which departure is possible.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — By definition, no inner enabling condition is required — the condition is universal and structural, not conditional: Rom 3:9 — "all, both Jews and Greeks, are under sin" — no pre-qualifying condition is named. However, two enabling pathways through which the condition becomes active are evidenced. (1) *Unbelief*: Joh 16:9 — "concerning sin, because they do not believe in me" — unbelief is the specific activating condition for the form of sin that the Spirit convicts of; (2) *The law*: Rom 7:8/9 — "when the commandment came, sin came alive" — the law's arrival activates the condition's full force within the one who has the law; Joh 15:22/24 — Jesus's coming and speaking removes excuse, making the condition's accountability operative.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Two enabling conditions. (1) *The practice of sinning*: Joh 8:34 — "everyone who practices sin" — the act of sinning habitually is the enabling condition that generates the enslaved state; the practice is both the mechanism and the enabling condition. (2) *The absence of God's seed / new birth*: 1Jo 3:9 — "no one born of God makes a practice of sinning, for God's seed abides in him" — the absence of the new-birth/God's-seed condition is the enabling condition for sin's enslaving power to hold; the person who lacks the new birth lacks the constitutional resistance to sin's mastery.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Four enabling conditions. (1) *Awareness when sin is made known*: Lev 4:23 — "the sin which he has committed is made known to him" — the conscience's ability to receive the disclosure of the record is the primary enabling condition; (2) *Conscience engagement*: Num 5:6 — "that person realizes his guilt" — the internal realization triggers the response mechanism; (3) *Humility before God*: Psa 32:5 — "I acknowledged my sin... I did not cover my iniquity" — the person's willingness not to cover their sin enables reception; (4) *Memory of prior failure*: Gen 41:9 — "I remember my offenses today" — the cupbearer's memory of past failure enables current acknowledgment.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Three enabling conditions. (1) *Recognition that sin has been committed*: Lev 4:14 — "when the sin which they have committed becomes known" — the recognition moment is the prerequisite; (2) *Repentance*: Act 2:38 — "repent... for the forgiveness of your sins" — the inner volitional turn is the explicit enabling condition in the NT; (3) *Faith*: Act 10:43 — "everyone who believes in him receives forgiveness of sins" — belief/faith is the specific inner condition through which forgiveness is received in the NT. Additionally: Lev 23:27 — self-affliction as the inner-posture of seeking on the Day of Atonement — the humbling of the self is an enabling condition for the ritual's efficacy.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Two enabling conditions. (1) *Corporate-community belonging*: membership in the lineage, family, or nation is the enabling condition for receiving the generational liability; Isa 43:27 — "your first father sinned" — the "your" addresses those who stand in the lineage of the first father; one cannot inherit what one is not lineally connected to; (2) *Inherited unbelief disposition*: Psa 78:32 — "they did not believe" — the unbelief that drives the generational pattern is itself enabled by the community's sustained failure to receive God's demonstrated faithfulness as a reason for trust.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Three enabling conditions. (1) *Proximity to holiness*: Luk 5:8 — Peter's recognition occurs specifically when Jesus demonstrates divine power over the fish; proximity to holiness triggers the conscience's recognition; (2) *Genuine humility*: Luk 18:13 — "would not even lift up his eyes to heaven" — the tax collector's self-abasement is the inner posture that enables honest self-recognition; (3) *Spiritual self-knowledge*: 1Ti 1:15 — Paul's "of whom I am the foremost" — the apostolic self-assessment is a considered inner knowledge of one's own worst state, not merely a moment of emotional distress.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Three enabling conditions. (1) *Knowledge of the violation*: Lev 5:2/3/4 — "when it is hidden from him... when he comes to know it" — guilt-recognition requires the relevant knowledge; the recognition is blocked when the violation is hidden; (2) *Honest conscience*: Gen 42:21 — "in truth we are guilty" — the word "in truth" (*ʾăbāl*) names honest acknowledgment as the enabling inner posture; (3) *Divine withdrawal provoking seeking*: Hos 5:15 — "until they acknowledge their guilt and seek my face" — God's strategic withdrawal creates the inner pressure that enables guilt-acknowledgment; the absence of God's presence is itself an enabling condition for guilt-recognition.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Three enabling conditions. (1) *Humbled heart*: Lev 26:41 — "if then their uncircumcised heart is humbled and they make amends for their iniquity" — heart-humiliation is the enabling precondition for iniquity-acknowledgment; (2) *Conscience-strike*: 2Sa 24:10 — "David's heart struck him" — the immediate conscience-event opens the path to acknowledgment; (3) *Divine discipline*: Hos 5:15 — "until they acknowledge their guilt and seek my face, and in their distress earnestly seek me" — God's strategic withdrawal and the resulting distress activate the inner pressure toward acknowledgment.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Three enabling conditions. (1) *Knowledge of the boundary*: Rom 4:15 — "where there is no law there is no transgression" — knowledge of the law is the prerequisite; transgression is definitionally impossible without prior awareness of the boundary being crossed; (2) *Inner absence of God-fear*: Psa 36:1 — "transgression speaks to the wicked deep in his heart; there is no fear of God before his eyes" — the absence of the fear of God is the enabling inner condition for transgression to take hold; (3) *Appetite of the will*: Pro 28:21 — "for a piece of bread a man will do wrong" — the will's desire is what transgression exploits; Pro 17:19 — "whoever loves transgression loves strife" — a positively-oriented inner affection toward transgression.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Three enabling conditions. (1) *Pride*: 2Ch 26:16 — "when he was strong, he grew proud, to his destruction. For he was unfaithful to the Lord his God" — pride is the inner condition that gives rise to faithlessness; Uzziah's strength produced pride, and pride produced the overstepping of God-given limits; (2) *Absence of spirit-vigilance*: Mal 2:15 — "guard yourselves in your spirit, and let none of you be faithless" — the command to guard implies that failure to guard is what enables faithlessness; the spirit is the inner domain where faithlessness originates and must be resisted; (3) *Divided or misplaced allegiance*: 1Ch 5:25 — "broke faith with the God of their fathers, and whored after the gods of the peoples" — allegiance transferred to false objects enables faithlessness to the true covenant-partner.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Three enabling conditions. (1) *Deceitful desires*: Eph 4:22 — "old self corrupt through deceitful desires" — desires that deceive (promising satisfaction while delivering corruption) are the enabling agent; (2) *Absence of wisdom/God-fear*: Pro 8:13 — "the fear of the Lord is hatred of evil... perverted speech I hate" — the absence of God-fear removes the resistance to perversion; Pro 2:12 — wisdom delivers from perverted speech — wisdom's absence enables it; (3) *Material inducement*: Exo 23:8; Deu 16:19 — bribery as the enabling mechanism for judgment-perversion; the monetary inducement corrupts the discernment faculty.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Three enabling conditions. (1) *Heart-denial of God*: Psa 53:1 — "the fool says in his heart, 'There is no God'... doing abominable iniquity" — the inner atheism of the heart produces the outer iniquity; Job 18:21 — "him who knows not God" — God-ignorance is the enabling inner condition; (2) *Self-trust rather than God-trust*: Hos 10:13 — "you have plowed iniquity; you have reaped injustice... because you have trusted in your own way and in the multitude of your warriors" — self-reliance displaces God-reliance and generates injustice; (3) *Material incentive*: 2Ch 19:7 — "partiality or taking bribes" — the external inducement that corrupts the inner orientation toward just conduct.

---

### T1.7.2

**Question:** What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The blocking conditions are explicitly evidenced. (1) *Stored word in the heart*: Psa 119:11 ("I have stored up your word in my heart, that I might not sin against you") — the word internalised is the inner bulwark against sinning. (2) *Fear of God before the eyes*: Exo 20:20 ("that the fear of him may be before you, that you may not sin") — the fear of God as an operative inner presence that restrains the will. (3) *Deliberate inner pondering*: Psa 4:4 ("ponder in your own hearts on your beds, and be silent") — reflective inwardness as a check on anger-driven sinning. (4) *Mouth-guarding*: Psa 39:1; Job 31:30 — disciplined restraint of speech as a specific block against speech-mode sinning. (5) *Divine external restraint*: Gen 20:6 — God's intervention preventing the sinning Abimelech would otherwise have committed. The blocking conditions span the external (divine restraint) and the internal (word, fear, pondering, speech-discipline).

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The conditions that prevent unintentional sinning are primarily *instructional and ritual*: Lev 4:2's entire Levitical-law context presupposes that teaching the commandments reduces unintentional violations — knowing "things not to be done" means the violation is less likely to occur unintentionally. The Lev 5:1 borderline verse (witness who "knows the matter" but doesn't testify) shows that *knowledge* is the primary preventive factor: once knowledge is present, the person can no longer sin "unintentionally" in the pure sense. The prescribed cultic remediation (Exo 29:36 daily; Eze 45:18 annual) is not preventive but restorative — it does not prevent unintentional sinning but addresses it after the fact.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Three evidenced blocking conditions. (1) *Self-interest overriding conscience*: 1Sa 15:30 — Saul's confession is immediately followed by "yet honor me now before the elders" — the need for social standing distorts the confession into a tool for self-preservation rather than genuine moral naming. (2) *External pressure as the sole motivator*: Exo 9:27/10:16 — Pharaoh's confessions are plague-prompted; once the plague ceases, he hardens (Exo 10:20 implied by context). Externally motivated confession without inner conscience-engagement is the hollow form. (3) *Will proceeding autonomously*: Deu 1:41 (VCG-03) — confession + immediate autonomous action = will not aligned with the confession's content. The blocking condition here is a will that remains self-directed despite the verbal acknowledgment.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The corpus evidences the preventive conditions by contrast. (1) *Fear of God*: Ecc 8:12 — those who "fear God, because they fear before him" — the fear of God as an operative inner orientation is the primary preventive against conscience-absent sinning. (2) *Knowledge of God*: 1Cor 15:34 — "some have no knowledge of God; I say this to your shame" — the call to "wake up" implies that knowledge of God, restored, is the preventive against the stupor. (3) *Responsive awakening to shame*: 1Cor 15:34 — Paul's appeal to shame as a corrective implies that the capacity for shame, if activated, can break the stupor. The blocking conditions are the positive counterparts: God-knowledge, fear of God, and moral shame-responsiveness.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The corpus names the blocking conditions through contrast. (1) *Walking in the law of the Lord with all the heart*: 2Ki 10:31 — "not careful to walk in the law of the Lord... with all his heart" — the positive blocking condition is whole-heart commitment to God's law. (2) *Fear of God*: 1Ti 5:20 — "so that the rest may stand in fear" — the fear of God (or fear of judgment) that public rebuke aims to produce in the community is the deterrent against persistent refusal. (3) *Receiving and acting on the knowledge of truth*: Heb 10:26 — the person who has received knowledge of truth and acts on it rather than continuing to sin.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The blocking conditions from the corpus: (1) *Abiding in Christ*: 1Jo 3:6 — "no one who abides in him keeps on sinning" — the abiding relationship with Christ is the primary structural preventive against habitual defection. (2) *Pleasing God*: Ecc 7:26 — "he who pleases God escapes her" — the inner disposition of God-pleasing (God-orientation) enables escape from the entrapment that habitual defection produces. (3) *Responsive listening*: 1Sa 2:25 — the blocking condition opposite to "they would not listen" is responsive hearing of the corrective voice; hearing and responding to God and his representatives.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Reception-enabling conditions: (1) *Dependence on the authority figure*: the community's reception of the transmitted sin is enabled by their structural position under the leader's authority — they receive what the leader transmits because the leader is their authority; (2) *Absence of independent God-orientation strong enough to resist*: Exo 23:33 — the warning implies that without the protective boundary (removing foreign nations), the community will be vulnerable to sin-transmission through influence. Reception-blocking conditions: 2Ki 23:15 — Josiah's response shows that a leader whose inner commitment is to God can reverse the transmission by dismantling the structures. The blocking requires either a leader whose own inner commitment to God overrides the transmitted sinning pattern, or the community's own independent resistance.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — The blocking conditions appear by implication from the enabling conditions. (1) *Perceived strength and legitimacy of governing authority*: Moab's revolts occurring "after the death of Ahab" (2Ki 1:1; 3:5) imply that during Ahab's reign, Moab did not revolt — the strong authority blocked revolt. (2) *The ruler's faithfulness to God*: 2Ch 21:10's causal link implies the converse: a ruler who does not forsake the Lord maintains the spiritual ground of legitimate authority that prevents the subject peoples from revolting. Fidelity to God in the governing authority is the primary blocking condition.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The blocking conditions from the corpus: (1) *Creaturely humility and restraint*: Jude 9 — Michael "did not presume to pronounce a blasphemous judgment" — the inner condition of knowing one's creaturely limits restrains sinful speech; (2) *Renunciation and replacement*: Eph 4:31 — "let all... slander be put away from you" — the deliberate inner act of renunciation is the blocking condition; (3) *Knowledge of God (faith)*: 1Ti 1:13 — Paul's blasphemy was from "ignorant unbelief" — the converse is that knowing God in faith prevents blasphemous speech.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — (1) *Enticement blocking*: the opposite of being "unsteady" (2Pe 2:18 — susceptibility) is being firmly established — a stable inner constitution not vulnerable to desire-exploitation; (2) *Hypocrisy blocking*: Gal 2:13's converse — the capacity to maintain authentic identity under social pressure, modelled by Paul's confrontation of Peter (Gal 2:11 context) — the inner integrity that resists collective performance; (3) *Apostasy blocking*: covenantal faithfulness maintained against departure pressure — the inner commitment to the covenantal identity that resists abandonment.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Nothing within the fallen person can block the universal condition — it is by definition universal: Heb 4:15 — "tempted as we are, yet without sin" — Christ's sinlessness is the single exception and it is rooted in his divine nature, not in human achievement. Within the condition's ongoing operation, what blocks its dominion is: (1) *Forgiveness received* (VCG-02): the condition's debt-dimension is addressed by divine forgiveness — "your sins are forgiven" (Mat 9:2); (2) *Death to sin through Christ*: Rom 6:11 — "consider yourselves dead to sin and alive to God in Christ Jesus" — the condition's enslaving power is blocked within the believer by their co-death with Christ; (3) *The Spirit's law*: Rom 8:2 — "the law of the Spirit of life has set you free... from the law of sin and death" — the Spirit's operation blocks the law of sin.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Two blocking conditions. (1) *New birth and indwelling seed*: 1Jo 3:9 — "God's seed abides in him, and he cannot keep on sinning, because he has been born of God" — the new birth with its indwelling divine seed constitutionally prevents the enslaving power's hold; (2) *Christ's protective intervention*: 1Jo 5:18 — "he who was born of God protects him, and the evil one does not touch him" — the born-of-God person (Christ) actively protecting the believer is the external-divine blocking condition. Both conditions are God-given; neither is achievable through human effort against the enslaving power.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Three blocking conditions. (1) *Self-deception through prosperity*: Hos 12:8 — "in all my labors they cannot find in me iniquity or sin" — material success produces a false sense of moral clearance; (2) *Suppression of the record*: Psa 32:5 — "I did not cover my iniquity" (the positive) implies that covering is the blocking condition; Jer 16:10 — the people's inability to identify their sin shows a suppression that blocks reception; (3) *Hardened face*: Isa 3:9 — "they proclaim their sin like Sodom; they do not hide it" — conscience has been so thoroughly suppressed that the record no longer produces shame; the blocking condition has become permanent display without awareness of its gravity.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Two blocking conditions. (1) *The unrecognised sin*: Lev 4:14 — sin "becomes known" only when it is recognised; while unrecognised, the seeking cannot begin (the sin must first be "made known" — T1.7.1); (2) *The eternal-sin condition*: Mar 3:29 — "whoever blasphemes against the Holy Spirit never has forgiveness, but is guilty of an eternal sin" — the eternal-sin condition is the one inner condition in the corpus that permanently forecloses forgiveness-reception. Lev 10:19 — Aaron's question about whether eating the sin offering while personally stricken with grief "would the Lord have approved" implies that a wrong inner state in the officiant can block the ritual's efficacy.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — The opposite of the generational pattern's unbelief: Isa 64:5 — "you meet him who joyfully works righteousness, those who remember you in your ways" — joyful righteousness-working and remembering God's ways are the inner conditions that resist the generational sinning pattern. These are the alternative inner orientations that break the cycle within a generation. Eze 37:23 — God's cleansing and saving — names the divine intervention that is ultimately what blocks the pattern when human inner conditions alone cannot.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Two blocking conditions. (1) *Self-righteousness*: Mat 9:13 — "I came not to call the righteous, but sinners" — those who perceive themselves as righteous cannot receive the sinner-identity they bear; the Pharisees (implied) block recognition through self-evaluation as righteous; (2) *Presumptuous self-confidence*: Amo 9:10 — "who say, 'Disaster shall not overtake or meet us'" — the habitual extreme sinner's inner conviction of security from consequence blocks the recognition of the sinner-identity's implications.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Three blocking conditions. (1) *Hardened false heart*: Hos 10:2 — "their heart is false; now they must bear their guilt" — the false heart does not accurately register guilt even while bearing it; (2) *Pride*: Eze 16:49 — "this was the guilt of your sister Sodom: she and her daughters had pride" — pride is the inner disposition that prevents guilt-recognition by generating a false sense of self-sufficiency; (3) *Self-generated concealment*: Jer 2:22 — the attempt to wash away guilt with lye and soap is itself a blocking mechanism — the effort at self-cleansing is a form of guilt-avoidance rather than guilt-recognition.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Three blocking conditions. (1) *Pride and self-flattery*: Psa 36:2 — "he flatters himself in his own eyes that his iniquity cannot be found out and hated" — pride generates a self-protective cognitive distortion; (2) *Wealth-induced false security*: Hos 12:8 — "I am rich; I have found wealth for myself; in all my labors they cannot find in me iniquity or sin" — material prosperity generates the illusion of moral cleanness; (3) *Stiff-necked will*: Exo 34:9 — Moses names Israel as "a stiff-necked people" requiring pardon precisely because the will is set against acknowledgment.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Three blocking conditions. (1) *Self-flattery and pride*: Pro 28:24 — "that is no transgression" — the wilful verbal denial; Jer 2:29 — "why do you contend with me?" — the self-justifying contention against God; (2) *Love of transgression itself*: Pro 17:19 — "whoever loves transgression loves strife" — the positive inner affection toward transgression blocks recognition of it as wrongdoing; (3) *Deception*: 1Ti 2:14 — "the woman was deceived and became a transgressor" — external deception can partially diminish the deliberate dimension by distorting perception of the boundary.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Three blocking conditions. (1) *Spirit-vigilance*: Mal 2:15/16 — "guard yourselves in your spirit, and do not be faithless" — the active inner guarding of the spirit is the most explicit faithlessness-prevention command in the corpus; it targets the exact origin-level of the characteristic; (2) *Fear of God*: 2Ch 30:7 — the fathers who were faithless are the negative example; their negative example presupposes the positive alternative of God-fearing loyalty; Ezr 9:4 — "all who trembled at the words of the God of Israel" — God-fear produces the response to faithlessness rather than the faithlessness itself; (3) *Honest awareness of covenant obligations*: Mal 2:14 — "the Lord was witness between you" — awareness that God witnesses the covenant prevents its casual breaking.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Three blocking conditions. (1) *Wisdom and God-fear*: Pro 8:13 — the fear of the Lord as hatred of evil including perverted speech; Pro 2:12 — wisdom delivering from perverted-speech people; (2) *Participation in the divine nature*: 2Pe 1:4 — "having escaped from the corruption that is in the world because of sinful desire" — participation in divine nature is the escape-mechanism from corruption; (3) *Putting off the old self*: Eph 4:22-24 — the deliberate act of putting off the corrupt old self; the actively renewed mind (Eph 4:23) is the blocking mechanism against deceitful-desire corruption.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Three blocking conditions. (1) *Fear of the Lord*: 2Ch 19:7 — "let the fear of the Lord be upon you. Be careful what you do, for there is no injustice with the Lord our God" — the fear of the Lord is the primary blocking condition that prevents judicial injustice; (2) *Active hand-withdrawal*: Eze 18:8 — "withholds his hand from injustice" — the deliberate volitional restraint; (3) *Walking in God's ways*: Psa 119:3 — "who also do no wrong, but walk in his ways" — covenant faithfulness as the structural disposition that forecloses injustice.

---

### T1.7.3

**Question:** What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The person who encounters the temptation to sin but does not — the character of the sinning-resisted state — is evidenced in several portraits. Joseph in Gen 39:9: the temptation is present; the inner state is one of named moral clarity ("How then can I do this great wickedness?") and upward reference (God's claim). Job in Job 1:22 and 2:10: under devastating suffering, Job's inner state is one of sustained moral restraint — conscience-active control even under pressure. Nehemiah in Neh 6:13: the trap is set; his inner state involves recognising the mechanism ("for this purpose he was hired") and refusing to yield. The common feature is that the non-sinning person retains full moral agency, with the will actively engaged in the decision not to sin rather than simply being unaware of the choice. The inner-being state is one of conscious, conscience-engaged refusal.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The question requires reframing for CHAR-2: unintentional sinning is not "received" from outside but committed. The more relevant question for this characteristic is: what is the inner-being state of the person who *fails to respond* when unintentional sinning surfaces to awareness — who does not confess or seek remedy? The corpus does not directly evidence this failure mode within CHAR-2's 18 verses. By implication, the person who suppresses awareness after the sin surfaces moves from CHAR-2 into CHAR-4 (Conscience suppression) territory. The CHAR-2 corpus presupposes a response; the absence of response is not evidenced here but is implicitly the boundary marker beyond which CHAR-2 ends.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The corpus does not directly evidence the non-confessing person's inner state within CHAR-3's 34 verses (this belongs primarily to CHAR-4 — Conscience suppression). However, VCG-03 (Deu 1:41) and the Pharaoh pattern (Exo 9:27/10:16 — confesses under pressure, hardens when pressure lifts) evidence the *partial* version: the person who produces the verbal form but whose inner state remains unchanged. This partial state is characterised by: the conscience may have registered (enough to produce the words) but the will has not been reoriented. The full non-confessing person (who would not even produce the words) is outside this corpus's scope — their state belongs to CHAR-4.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The 8-verse corpus does not directly evidence this scenario — the persons exhibiting conscience suppression in the corpus are not described as encountering and then refusing to resolve it (that would be closer to CHAR-5 — Refusal to repent). The corpus describes conscience suppression as an *already-settled* inner condition: Jer 2:35 (already claiming innocence), Jer 16:10 (already failing to recognise), Ecc 8:12 (already sinning a hundred times), Tit 3:11 (already warped). The inner-being state of the person within conscience suppression is: moral self-perception that does not accurately register one's own sinfulness — a state characterised by false peace (Jer 2:35 — "his anger has turned from me") or genuine puzzlement (Jer 16:10 — "what sin?").

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The corpus evidences the turning person most directly through Eze 33:12 — "the wickedness of the wicked, he shall not fall by it when he turns from his wickedness" — the turning person is the one whose prior wickedness does not condemn them because the will has moved. The turning person's inner state is the opposite of "did not depart" — it is active departure, movement, change of direction. The corpus (18 verses all describing refusal) does not portrait the inner state of the turning person extensively, but Eze 33:12's "turns from his wickedness" is the positive counter-portrait: the will that moves in the direction of departure.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — 1Jo 3:6 provides the clearest evidence: the person who "abides in him" is the one who does not keep on sinning — the inner-being state is one of *sustained relational union with Christ* that structurally prevents the habitual pattern. Ecc 7:26 — "he who pleases God escapes her" — the inner-being state is one of active God-pleasing orientation, which provides the dispositional resource for escaping the snare that traps the sinner. The positive inner-being state is thus: abiding in Christ (1Jo 3:6), pleasing God (Ecc 7:26), and responsive hearing (the opposite of 1Sa 2:25) — all of which represent an active God-oriented inner constitution that prevents the sinning pattern from becoming habitual.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-7]** S — The corpus does not evidence the inner-being state of a community member who resists the leader's transmitted sinning direction. The corpus shows compliance (dominant Kings pattern) and structural reversal (Josiah). The individual community member who privately maintains their God-orientation while the leader transmits the sinning direction is not addressed in the 19-verse corpus. This is a gap in the evidence.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(S)*

**[CHAR-8]** S — The corpus does not describe the inner-being state of communities that maintain submission to governing authority. The corpus is entirely focused on the revolting parties; the non-revolting community's inner state is not addressed.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Jude 9 and 2Pe 2:11 provide the clearest evidence: Michael and the angels do not pronounce blasphemous judgments even in contexts where they might seem warranted. The inner-being state of the non-blasphemer is: creaturely deference — "The Lord rebuke you" (Jude 9) — acknowledging that some pronouncements exceed creaturely authority and belong to God alone. The non-blasphemer's inner state is defined by the recognition of their own creaturely limits in speech.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(S)*

**[CHAR-10]** S — The corpus does not directly evidence the inner-being state of the person who resists enticement, hypocrisy, or apostasy. Gal 2:11's Paul (confronting Peter rather than joining the hypocrisy) is the implicit positive exemplar, but his inner state during the confrontation is not described in the 5-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Rom 6:22 — "you have been set free from sin and have become slaves of God, the fruit you get leads to sanctification and its end, eternal life" — the freed person is: no longer under sin's dominion, now under God's authority (slave of God), producing the fruit of sanctification, and oriented toward eternal life. Rom 6:18 — "having been set free from sin, have become slaves of righteousness" — the freed person's inner allegiance has been relocated from sin to righteousness. The inner state is not the absence of sin's presence but the absence of sin's dominion: Rom 6:11 — "dead to sin and alive to God" — the condition persists as a reality to reckon oneself dead to, not as a master with living authority over the person.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — 1Jo 3:9 and 1Jo 5:18 together describe the liberated inner-being state. (1) *Born of God*: a constitutional state of divine birth that has transformed the inner person's relationship to sin; (2) *God's seed abiding*: an indwelling divine principle that constitutionally prevents habitual sinning from taking hold; (3) *Protected by Christ*: an external protective guardianship that bars the evil one's touch. The liberated state is thus: constitutionally new (born of God), internally reinforced (God's seed abiding), and externally protected (Christ's guardianship). This is not a self-generated freedom but a God-given, Christ-protected liberation.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Jer 16:10 — the people under judgment ask "What is our iniquity? What is the sin that we have committed against the Lord our God?" — the non-receiving state is incomprehension: the record is there (God sees it; judgment has come) but the person cannot identify it in themselves. Isa 3:9 — "they proclaim their sin like Sodom; they do not hide it" — the alternative non-receiving state: the record has produced such conscience-deadness that the person exhibits their sin publicly without awareness of its gravity. Both states involve a failure of the inner conscience to correctly interpret the moral reality of the record before God.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Mar 3:29 — "guilty of an eternal sin" — the person guilty of the eternal sin is in a state of permanent unresolved guilt before God; the seeking cannot break through the condition. For the broader case (seeking without receiving), the corpus is largely silent: the pattern evidenced is that genuine seeking (repentance + faith — Act 2:38/10:43) produces reception. The case of seeking without receiving is not directly evidenced beyond the eternal-sin exception of Mar 3:29.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-15]** S — The corpus does not describe the inner-being state of the individual within the community who recognises the generational sin-pattern but stands apart from it. Isa 43:27 names the first father's sin; Eze 37:23 names the promise to cleanse; neither describes the inner experience of the individual who breaks the pattern within their generation.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Amo 9:10 names the resistant state: "who say, 'Disaster shall not overtake or meet us'" — the inner state is confident self-deception about the consequences of the sinner-identity. Joh 9:24/25 — the Pharisees who declare Jesus "a sinner" with certainty while the healed man refuses the label — the resisters are in a state of inverted moral judgement: applying the sinner-label to the holy and denying it to themselves. The inner state of resistance is thus characterised by moral inversion: others are sinners; the self is not.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Eze 21:23/24 — "they have sworn solemn oaths, but he brings their guilt to remembrance" — the person who suppresses guilt-acknowledgment exists in a state of false oath-confidence that is overridden by God's recall of the guilt-record; Amo 9:10 (CHAR-16 context) — "disaster shall not overtake or meet us" — the guilt-denier's inner state is presumptuous self-assurance. Jer 2:22 names the guilt-denier's activity: attempting self-cleansing while the stain remains before God. The inner state of guilt-refusal is thus false confidence sustained against an objective guilt-reality that God sees and will eventually expose.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Hos 12:8 names it: "I am rich... they cannot find in me iniquity" — the inner state is wealthy self-sufficiency generating false moral confidence. Psa 36:2 — "flatters himself in his own eyes" — the inner state is proud self-deception. Job 31:33 — "if I have concealed my transgressions... by hiding my iniquity in my heart" — the alternative to honest disclosure is conscious inner concealment; the person knows the iniquity but buries it deliberately. The denier's inner state thus has two forms: unconscious self-deception (Psa 36:2 — cannot see or hate the iniquity) and conscious concealment (Job 31:33 — hiding it in the heart).

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Isa 1:5 names it comprehensively: "why will you still be struck down? Why will you continue to rebel? The whole head is sick, and the whole heart faint" — the persistent transgressor's inner state is one of comprehensive moral-spiritual illness in both cognitive (head) and volitional (heart) faculties. Jer 2:29 — "why do you contend with me? You have all transgressed against me" — the inner state is self-righteous contention against God despite guilt. The persistent transgressor's inner state is thus a combination of structural inner deterioration (Isa 1:5 — head and heart incapacitated) and self-justifying posture (Jer 2:29) that produces inability to stand in God's right ways (Hos 14:9 — stumbling).

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — 2Ch 28:22 names it most precisely: "in the time of his distress he became yet more faithless to the Lord — this same King Ahaz" — the inner state is a will that has become constitutively oriented away from God such that the very pressure that would normally drive a person toward God drives this person further from him. Pro 11:6 — "the treacherous are taken captive by their lust" — the inner state under sustained faithlessness is captivity to the will's own craving; the person is not free to turn toward God because the lust has assumed agentive control. The hardened-under-distress state of 2Ch 28:22 is CHAR-20's most extreme dispositional portrait.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — 2Pe 2:12 names it most vividly: "like irrational animals, creatures of instinct, born to be caught and destroyed... will also be destroyed in their destruction" — the inner state is animal-instinctual operating without reason, heading toward destruction that matches their nature. 1Ti 6:5 — "depraved in mind and deprived of the truth" — the inner state lacks the basic cognitive capacity to access truth. Jude 10 — destroyed by what they understand instinctively — the instinct has replaced moral reasoning as the inner governing faculty. The characterised inner state is: reason and moral faculty replaced by unreflective instinct, enslaved to the corruption that will ultimately destroy the self.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Zep 3:5 names it with the greatest diagnostic precision: "the unjust knows no shame" — the inner-being state is one of complete insensibility to the moral wrongness of their own conduct. Job 15:16 fills out the appetite-dimension: "a man who drinks injustice like water" — the person's deepest craving is for what wrongs others; the inner orientation is appetitive toward harm. Psa 53:1 names the cognitive-theological foundation: "There is no God" in the heart — the inner denial of divine accountability is the cognitive substructure of the shameless, water-drinking injustice.

---

## T1.8 — Dimension Classification

### T1.8.1

**Question:** What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The primary inner-being dimension of wilful sinning is **volition / will** — the capacity to choose and to act. This is established by the definitional criterion ("the will committing a known wrong") and confirmed throughout the corpus: the acts of sinning in VCG-01 (Gen 39:9 refusal, Eze 18:4/20 personal accountability), VCG-02 (1Ki 8:31 sin against neighbor), and VCG-05 (1Jo 2:1 — "so that you may not sin") all presuppose a will that chooses. The term cha.ta as a verb further confirms this: the act of sinning is volitional, not merely circumstantial. The will is the seat of the characteristic; sinning is what the will does when it turns against the moral order it was designed to uphold.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The primary inner-being dimension of unintentional sinning is **moral accountability / conscience** — specifically conscience in its post-act engagement mode. The definitional distinction from CHAR-1 is that conscience does not engage at the moment of the act (because knowledge is absent) but engages upon realisation. Lev 5:5 ("when he realizes his guilt... and confesses") and Num 22:34 (Balaam's immediate confession upon disclosure) show conscience as the faculty that fires when the morally relevant information arrives. The conscience is thus the primary inner faculty that processes unintentional sinning — not the will (which did not knowingly choose the wrong) but the conscience (which responds to the moral reality once it becomes available).

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The primary inner-being dimension of confession is **conscience** — conscience in its confessional mode, as the brief's definition states. 2Sa 24:10 establishes this most clearly: "David's heart struck him" — the heart/conscience is the initiating faculty; the verbal confession follows. The conscience here functions not as a deterrent (as in CHAR-1's VCG-03) but as a *retrospective witness that drives speech*. It is the faculty that fires post-act, identifies the wrong, and refuses to remain silent — driving the will and mouth toward naming. Neh 1:6 ("confessing the sins... day and night") shows conscience in sustained confessional mode rather than as a single episode.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The primary inner-being dimension is **conscience** — specifically conscience in its *malfunctioning, absent, or refused mode*. The characteristic is constitutively a conscience-failure: the moral-witness faculty (conscience) that should register sin, produce guilt, and drive confession either does not register (Jer 16:10; Ecc 8:12; 1Cor 15:34) or is explicitly refused/denied (Jer 2:35; Tit 3:11 implicit). The characteristic is named for this faculty precisely because conscience is what is suppressed.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The primary inner-being dimension is **volition / will** — the characteristic is constitutively a will-act (refusal) sustained over time. The definitional language throughout is volitional: "did not depart," "clung to," "would not obey," "sinning deliberately" (Heb 10:26 — *hekousiōs* = willingly/voluntarily). The will is both the faculty that could turn and the faculty that is refusing the turn. The characteristic cannot exist without an operative will — there must be a will that is capable of turning for there to be a refusal to turn.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The primary inner-being dimension is **will/volition** — specifically the will in its *dispositional/formational* mode rather than its moment-of-decision mode. The will that has been habituated to sinning is the primary faculty: Exo 9:34 — "sinned yet again and hardened his heart" — the will expressed through the hardened heart drives the repetition. 1Jo 3:6's "keeps on sinning" names the will's continuous operational state. The will here is not making a fresh choice at each moment (that would be CHAR-1) but has been formed into a direction that produces sinning as its default output.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The primary inner-being dimension is **will/volition** — specifically the leader's will operating in its *causative* mode. The Hiphil causative of cha.ta — the grammatical marker that distinguishes CHAR-7 from all other sinning characteristics — is precisely the form that names the will acting to cause another's sinning, not merely one's own. 1Ki 16:2 — "you have walked in the way of Jeroboam and have made my people Israel to sin" — the will is the agent ("walked") and the causative force ("made... to sin"). The will is primary at both ends: the leader's will is committed to the sinning direction and exercises its authority to transmit it; the community's will is redirected by the transmitted influence.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — The primary inner-being dimension is **will/volition** — the decisive act of breaking submission requires a will that chooses the break. The pa.sha root itself names a deliberate wilful transgression-breaking: 2Ki 8:20 — "Edom revolted... and set up a king of their own" — the constructive act of setting up their own king is a volitional assertion of independence. 2Ch 21:10's causal ground — "because he had forsaken the Lord" — shows that forsaking (a volitional act) is the inner precondition for the political revolt. The characteristic is constitutively volitional: revolt requires a will that decides to break submission.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The primary inner-being dimension is **conscience/moral evaluation** in the sense that sinful speech is the external externalisation of the inner moral condition — but more precisely, the primary faculty engaged is the **heart as the moral-generating centre**. Mat 15:19 — "out of the heart come evil thoughts... slander" — the heart is the origin; the speech is the product. The heart's moral-generating capacity is the primary inner-being dimension: sinful speech is what the corrupted heart produces when it speaks.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Given the composite nature of the characteristic, different mechanisms engage different primary dimensions. (1) *Enticement (deleazō)*: the primary dimension is **desire/appetite** — the desire-faculty (epithumia) is constitutively engaged as the mechanism's entry point (Jam 1:14 — "his own desire"). (2) *Collective hypocrisy (sunupokrinomai)*: the primary dimension is **will and social identity** — the volitional act of adopting a performed identity alongside others (Gal 2:13). (3) *Apostasy (apostasia)*: the primary dimension is **will and covenantal identity** — the volitional departure from the covenantal standing (Act 21:21 — "forsake Moses"). Across the characteristic, **will/volition** is the common faculty: each mechanism operates through the will's response to (or capture by) the specific mechanism.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The primary dimension is **the person as constituted moral subject under a power** — what the programme would call the will/volition level but more precisely the *person's inner constitutional standing* relative to sin as a power. The three VCG registers each engage a different inner dimension: (1) VCG-01 — *moral character/identity* dimension (rish.ah as settled inner quality); (2) VCG-02 — *conscience/guilt/relational-standing* dimension (debt before God requiring forgiveness); (3) VCG-03 — *will-under-power* dimension (enslaved will, indwelling sin-force). At characteristic scope, the primary dimension is the person's entire constitutional inner standing before God: Rom 3:23 — "all have sinned and fall short" — is a total-person statement engaging every inner-being dimension simultaneously.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — The primary inner-being dimension is **will/volition in its captive mode** — the will whose freedom toward God has been taken over by sin as master. Joh 8:34 — "a slave to sin" — the slave's will is the will that cannot freely choose otherwise; the enslaving power specifically targets and captures the will's directional freedom. The definition confirms this: "governing the will so it cannot freely choose otherwise" — the will is explicitly named as the faculty the enslavement targets. The other inner-being dimensions (conscience, moral evaluation) are secondary consequences of the will's captivity.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — The primary dimension is **moral-accountability standing before God** — not a specific faculty but the person's total relational-moral position. The characteristic is defined by its standing before God, not by its engagement of a specific inner faculty. Amo 5:12 — "for I know how many are your transgressions and how great are your sins" — God's knowledge of the record is the defining dimension; the record exists before divine omniscience. Hos 13:12 — "his sin is kept in store" — the storage is in the divine memory. The primary dimension is thus the person's standing in God's moral memory.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — The primary dimension is **will/volition in its God-directed turning mode** — the will's movement toward God in seeking forgiveness. Act 2:38 — "repent" (metanoeō — change of mind + direction); Exo 32:30 — "I will go up to the Lord" — the volitional ascent; Act 10:43 — "everyone who believes in him receives" — faith as the will's trust-act directed toward Christ. The seeking dimension is constitutively volitional; the receiving dimension is relational-condition change that follows the volitional seeking. The will's God-directed movement is the primary inner-being faculty engaged.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — The primary dimension is **corporate moral identity** — the person's constitutive belonging to a community whose accumulated sinning history shapes their inner moral condition. Isa 43:27 — "your first father sinned, and your mediators transgressed against me" — the present-tense "your" makes the ancestral sinning part of the current person's moral identity through their lineage. 1Ki 8:47 — "we have sinned" — the "we" is not merely a grammatical convenience but names the corporate moral subject as the primary dimension.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — The primary dimension is **constituted moral identity** — the person's moral character as a whole, not a specific faculty. Rom 5:19 — "were made sinners" — the making is a total-person status; Luk 18:13 — "be merciful to me, a sinner" — the sinner-identity is a whole-person self-designation. The characteristic does not primarily engage a specific inner faculty (will, conscience, affect) but constitutes the person's *moral self as a whole* as a sinner.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — The primary dimension is **conscience in its guilt-awareness mode** — the definition's own identification. The conscience is the faculty that registers guilt (Lev 4:13/22/27 — "realizes his guilt"), experiences its weight (Ezr 9:6 — "I am ashamed"), staggered by it (1Sa 25:31 — pu.qah — pangs of conscience), and initiates the remedial movement (Lev 6:4 — "realized his guilt and will restore"). Guilt-as-inner-state is constitutively a conscience-phenomenon; it cannot exist without conscience engagement.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — The primary dimension is **the objective moral-crime account before God** — the person's standing in God's moral ledger as the one who has accumulated wrongdoing against him. This is the definition's "crime in its moral-spiritual sense." The characteristic is not primarily experiential (CHAR-17 is the experiential register) but constitutional: it subsists before God whether the person feels it or not (Hos 12:8 — Ephraim denies it; Hos 13:12 — God has it bound up and stored). The constitutional moral-crime account is the primary dimension; the felt-weight is secondary.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — The primary dimension is **the will's volitional act of knowing defiance** — the definition's "wilful defiance of known moral or covenantal order." The will is the primary faculty: it knows the boundary (Rom 4:15 — law required), it chooses to cross (Isa 1:2 — "they have rebelled"), it sustains the direction (Eze 2:3 — "to this very day"). Every other dimension (cognitive distortion, affective collapse, conscience suppression) is secondary to the will's primary volitional choice.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — The primary dimension is **the will's covenantal orientation — the inner disposition of loyalty or betrayal within a known relational bond**. Mal 2:15/16 — "guard yourselves in your spirit, and do not be faithless" — the spirit is named as the inner locus requiring guarding; Isa 48:8 — the foreknown constitutional bent of the will toward treachery — the will's settled inner orientation is the characteristic's primary faculty. The characteristic is constitutively volitional and dispositional rather than cognitive or affective at the primary level.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — The primary dimension is **the moral faculty in its distorted/corrupted condition** — specifically the heart, mind, will, and desire as twisted from their designed moral orientation. Pro 6:14 — "perverted heart devises evil" — the heart as origin; 1Ti 6:5 — "depraved in mind" — the mind as primary corrupted faculty; Eph 4:22 — "corrupt through deceitful desires" — desire as corruption-agent. The characteristic operates at the level of the person's inner moral constitution rather than discrete acts or record-entries.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — The primary dimension is **the moral-conduct faculty oriented toward wrong in dealings with others** — the will's deployment of the capacity for just conduct in the wrong direction. Psa 58:2 — "in your hearts you devise wrongs" — heart as the origin; Eze 18:8 — "withholds his hand from injustice" — the will restraining the hand confirms the will as the governing faculty; Luk 16:10 — the fixed-character dishonesty confirms the dispositional-volitional level as primary.

---

### T1.8.2

**Question:** What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Multiple lines of evidence support the will-dimension classification. (1) Accountability: Eze 18:20 ("the soul who sins alone shall die; the son shall not suffer for the iniquity of the father") — personal accountability presupposes a personal will. (2) Resistance possible: VCG-03's entire evidence base (Gen 39:9, Exo 20:20, Job 1:22, Psa 4:4, Psa 39:1, 1Jo 2:1) shows that sinning can be resisted, which only makes sense if the will is the operative faculty. (3) Social pressure overriding it: 1Sa 15:24 ("I feared the people and obeyed their voice") shows the will being deflected by pressure — volitional language throughout. (4) The deterrence formula: Exo 20:20 ("that you may not sin") and Eze 3:21 ("if you warn the righteous person not to sin, and he does not sin") both treat not-sinning as a decision that warning and moral instruction can produce — confirming the will's centrality.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The conscience-as-primary-dimension is supported by: (1) Lev 5:5 — the transition from "realizes his guilt" to "confesses" is a conscience-activation event; (2) Num 22:34 — Balaam's immediate moral response ("I have sinned") upon seeing the angel demonstrates conscience engaging on new information; (3) The entire Lev 4/Num 15 framework presupposes that once the sin surfaces to awareness, the person is morally obligated to respond — this obligation is the conscience's claim. The will is involved in the remedy (bringing the offering, confessing) but not in the original sinning act. Conscience is the faculty that bridges the gap between the uninformed act and the informed response.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The conscience-primary classification is supported by: (1) The direct heart-conscience language in the paradigm case: 2Sa 24:10 — "David's heart struck him" — heart as the conscience-organ initiating confession; (2) Shimei's confession: 2Sa 19:20 — "your servant *knows* that I have sinned" — knowledge as the conscience-basis for the confession; (3) The hollow-confession contrast: Deu 1:41 — words spoken but conscience not fully engaged (will proceeds independently) — confirming that genuine conscience-engagement is the distinguishing feature; (4) The extended confession: Dan 9:5 — multiple named dimensions of failure show conscience operating with high articulation, naming specific aspects of what went wrong.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The conscience-primary classification is supported by: (1) Jer 2:35 — the explicit denial of sin is an anti-confessional conscience-act: the conscience that should say "I have sinned" is made to say "I have not sinned"; (2) Jer 16:10 — "what sin have we committed?" — the question reveals a conscience that is not firing its sin-recognition signal; (3) Ecc 8:12 — sinning "a hundred times" without the fear of God reveals conscience-absent or conscience-numbed habituation; (4) 1Cor 15:34 — the "drunken stupor" is explicitly a conscience-alertness failure; (5) Tit 3:11 — "self-condemned" — the person's own conscience implicitly witnesses against them (the self-condemnation is a conscience-verdict they do not consciously receive).

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — (1) 2Ki 10:31 — "not careful to walk... with all his heart" — the heart as the integrating volitional centre is the faculty engaged; "all his heart" = complete volitional alignment; its absence = volitional partial-refusal. (2) Neh 9:29 — "would not obey" — the "would not" is a volitional statement. (3) Heb 10:26 — "sinning deliberately" (*hekousiōs*) — the adverb of willing/deliberateness names the will directly. (4) 2Ki 3:3 — "clung to" (*davaq*) — a volitional attachment. (5) Rom 6:15 — the hypothetical of sinning "because" of grace — the "because" implies a reasoned volitional choice about whether to sin.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — (1) Exo 9:34 — "hardened his heart" — the heart (as the volitional centre) is the faculty that is hardened; (2) 1Sa 2:25 — "they would not listen" — the "would not" is volitional; (3) Hos 10:9 — "you have sinned... there they have continued" — the continuation is volitional persistence; (4) 1Jo 3:6's "abides in him" as the structural opposite — abiding is a volitional-dispositional state; (5) 2Ki 17:7 — "feared other gods" — the fear/allegiance is a dispositional volitional commitment. All evidence confirms the will/disposition as the operative faculty.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — (1) 1Ki 16:19 — "walking in the way of Jeroboam, and for his sin which he committed, making Israel to sin" — the will expressed through walking (personal commitment) and the Hiphil causative (transmitted to others); (2) 2Ki 17:21 — "Jeroboam drove Israel from following the Lord" — drove (*niddah* — to push away, banish) names the causative volitional force; (3) 1Ki 16:2 — God holds the leader accountable for "making my people... to sin" — the accountability is volitional (you chose to walk, you chose to make); (4) Jer 32:35 — "they built the high places... to cause Judah to sin" — the building is an agentive volitional act with causative intent.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — (1) Pa.sha root meaning — deliberate transgressive breaking-away (not accidental); (2) 2Ki 8:20 — "set up a king of their own" — positive volitional assertion of independence alongside the breaking; (3) 2Ch 21:10 — "because he had forsaken the Lord" — *forsook* (*azav*) is a volitional act of abandonment; the political revolt follows from the volitional inner spiritual forsaking; (4) 2Ki 1:1 / 3:5 — "after the death of Ahab, Moab rebelled" — the temporal marker implies a decision taken at a specific moment.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — (1) Mat 15:19 — the heart named as the source; (2) 1Ti 6:4 — slander traced to the inner conditions of conceit and diseased craving (not to external triggers); (3) 2Ti 3:2 — the abusive/blasphemous disposition as a character trait (inner formation, not external act); (4) VCG-03 — the beast's blasphemy as constitutive identity rather than isolated act — the deepest level of the heart's orientation expressed in constitutive speech. All evidence supports: the inner moral-generative capacity of the heart is the primary faculty; speech is its expression.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — (1) Jam 1:14 — "lured and enticed by his own desire" — the desire is the mechanism but the luring requires the will's yielding to the desire's pull; (2) Gal 2:13 — "acted hypocritically along with him" — the acting-alongside is a volitional adoption; (3) Act 21:21 — "forsake Moses" — forsaking (*apostasia*) is a volitional departure; (4) 2Pe 2:14 — "hearts trained in greed" — the training involves the volitional sustaining of the desire-appetite over time.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — (1) Rom 3:9 — "under sin" — the preposition "under" names a positional relationship of the whole person relative to sin; (2) Eph 2:1 — "dead in trespasses and sins" — the deadness is total-person; (3) Rom 7:14 — "sold under sin" — sold as a whole person to a master; (4) Rom 6:6 — "the body of sin might be brought to nothing" — the "body" as the whole embodied person under sin's ownership; (5) Gen 4:7 — "its desire is for you" — the predatory desire is for the whole person as its target; the will is named only as the faculty that must resist ("you must rule over it") but sin desires the whole person.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — (1) Joh 8:34 — "slave to sin" — slavery directly names the will's captivity; a slave's will is governed by the master; (2) Rom 6:1/2 — "continue in sin... live in it" — the continued living-in presupposes a will that cannot or does not freely choose to exit; (3) 1Jo 3:9 — "he cannot keep on sinning" — the "cannot" names a constitutional volitional impossibility that the new birth produces; (4) Gal 3:22 — "imprisoned everything" — the imprisonment targets the will's freedom to obtain the promise through human effort; the prison metaphor specifically names the restriction of free movement.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — (1) Exo 32:33 — "whoever has sinned against me, I will blot out of my book" — the person's standing in the divine book is the operative moral reality; (2) Jer 31:34 — "I will remember their sin no more" — the erasure of divine memory is the defining liberation; (3) Job 10:6 — "seek out my iniquity and search for my sin" — divine scrutiny of the person's standing is the characteristic's primary mode; (4) Gen 18:20 — "their sin is very grave" — the gravity is measured by what has reached God as an objective reality, not by the person's own internal assessment.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — (1) Act 2:38 — "repent" — repentance is a volitional act named first in the seeking-sequence; (2) Exo 32:30 — "I will go up to the Lord" — the first-person future volitional statement; (3) Act 10:43 — "everyone who believes in him receives" — belief as the volitional trust-act; (4) Lev 23:27 — "you shall afflict yourselves" — the deliberate inner self-affliction is a volitional posture of seeking; (5) 2Ch 29:23 — "they laid their hands on them" — the hand-laying is the volitional act of identification with the offering's purpose.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — (1) Isa 43:27 — "your first father sinned" — the ancestral sin is addressed to the present community as their inherited condition; (2) 1Ki 8:47 — "we have sinned" — the corporate "we" is the locus of the characteristic; (3) Isa 64:5 — "in our sins we have been a long time" — the possessive "our" names the shared corporate condition; (4) Jer 8:14 — "we have sinned against the Lord" — the corporate acknowledgment. All uses are corporate rather than individually-bounded.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — (1) Rom 5:19 — "made sinners" — the passive voice confirms the total-person constitution; (2) Gen 13:13 — "great sinners against the Lord" — the identity is the totality of the Sodomites' moral character; (3) Luk 5:8 — "I am a sinful man" — the whole-person self-declaration; (4) 1Ti 1:15 — "Christ Jesus came into the world to save sinners" — the salvific mission targets the whole person, not a specific faculty; (5) Heb 7:26 — "separated from sinners" — the separation is total-person, not faculty-specific.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — (1) Lev 4:13/22/27 — "they realize their guilt" — the realisation is conscience's act; (2) Lev 5:5 — "when he realizes his guilt in any of these and confesses" — conscience-realisation produces confession; (3) Gen 42:21 — the brothers' conscience connects their past cruelty to their present distress; (4) 1Sa 25:31 — pu.qah (staggering of conscience) names the conscience-specific faculty directly; (5) Hos 5:15 — "until they acknowledge their guilt" — the acknowledgment is a conscience act.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — (1) Gen 15:16 — "the iniquity of the Amorites is not yet complete" — the Amorites are not described as feeling their iniquity; it exists as a measured moral reality before God regardless of their inner awareness; (2) Hos 13:12 — "bound up; his sin is kept in store" — the bound-up condition is God's action, not Ephraim's subjective experience; (3) Hos 12:8 — Ephraim claims no iniquity while God knows it is real — the objective and subjective are explicitly divergent; (4) Eze 18:20 — "the wickedness of the wicked shall be upon himself" — the "upon himself" is an objective moral-legal attachment.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*
