**[CHAR-19]** E — (1) Rom 4:15 — transgression requires knowledge of the law → will can only transgress what it knows; (2) Isa 1:2 — "children have I reared... but they have rebelled" — the rebellion is wilful choice against received care; (3) Eze 18:30 — "repent and turn from all your transgressions" — the remedial call is to the will to turn; (4) Isa 31:6 — "turn to him from whom people have deeply revolted" — the revolt and its reversal are both volitional movements; (5) Pro 28:13 — "he who confesses and forsakes them" — the forsaking is a volitional act confirming that the committing was volitional.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — (1) Mal 2:15 — "guard yourselves in your spirit" — the spirit as the named locus of faithlessness-danger; (2) 2Ch 28:22 — Ahaz becoming "yet more faithless" under distress — the will's sustained dispositional hardening; (3) Isa 48:8 — "I knew you would surely deal treacherously" — the foreknown constitutional inner bent; (4) 1Ch 5:25 — "broke faith with the God of their fathers, and whored after the gods" — the will's active allegiance-transfer; (5) Pro 11:6 — "the treacherous are taken captive by their lust" — the will enslaved by its own faithless orientation.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — (1) Pro 6:14 — heart as the perverted origin of continual evil-devising; (2) 1Ti 6:5 — mind as the named perverted faculty; (3) Eph 4:22 — desire as the active corruption-agent within the inner person; (4) Pro 12:8 — "twisted mind" as the characterising inner trait; (5) Isa 29:16 — the mind's cognitive-relational inversion as perversion; (6) 2Cor 11:3 — "your thoughts will be led astray" — the thoughts as the corruption-target.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — (1) Psa 58:2 — heart-devising is the named origin; (2) Eze 18:8 — hand-withholding confirms volitional control; (3) Job 34:32 — "if I have done iniquity, I will do it no more" — the will's capacity to cease confirms it governs; (4) Luk 16:10 — fixed character confirmed by scaling from small to much; (5) Eze 3:20 — "a righteous person turns from his righteousness and commits injustice" — the turn is volitional.

---

### T1.8.3

**Question:** Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Secondary dimensions are evidenced without competing with the primary will-classification. (1) *Conscience*: VCG-03's deterrence register engages conscience as the faculty that recognises the moral quality of the act (Gen 39:9 — "great wickedness"; Job 1:22 — restraint of charge against God). Conscience operates as the inner witness to the will's decision but is not itself the seat of the sinning. (2) *Moral evaluation*: the entire corpus presupposes a moral standard against which the act is measured as wrong — the law (Deu 19:15; 24:4), God's command (Eze 14:13), the relational claim of the neighbour (Mat 18:15). Moral evaluation is engaged but functions as the background standard, not the active faculty producing the act. (3) *Body*: speech-mode sinning (Psa 39:1, Job 2:10, Ecc 5:6) and bodily sinning (1Cor 6:18) implicate the body as the expressive organ. These secondary dimensions do not compete with the primary will-classification; they describe what the will works through and against.

## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Secondary dimensions are present. (1) *Moral liability / guilt*: unintentional sinning immediately creates an objective state of guilt before God (Lev 4:2 — real sin; Num 15:28 — requires atonement). This guilt-state is the condition that conscience processes upon realisation; it is the objective counterpart to the conscience's subjective response. (2) *Communal accountability*: Lev 4:3 (priest's sin implicating the community) and Lev 9:15 (community sin offering) show that unintentional sinning carries a communal dimension — individual inadvertent violation can produce corporate moral liability. These secondary dimensions do not compete with the conscience-primary classification; they describe the objective moral landscape within which conscience operates.

## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Secondary dimensions: (1) *Will/volition*: confession requires the will's agreement to name the act as wrong — 1Ch 21:17 ("It is I who have sinned") is a volitional claim, not just a conscience-registration. The will must not be blocked by self-protection (1Sa 15:30 — Saul) for genuine confession to occur. (2) *Speech / communicative agency*: the verbal externalisation is not peripheral but constitutive of confession — without the naming spoken to a recipient, the inner recognition remains guilt (CHAR-17) rather than becoming confession. (3) *Moral evaluation*: Num 12:11 — "we have done foolishly and have sinned" — Aaron's confession involves a moral evaluation (foolishness as the character of the sin). These secondary dimensions do not compete with the conscience-primary classification; they describe what conscience works through and with to produce confession.

## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

(3) *Moral evaluation*: Ecc 8:12 — the sinner who evaluates his long life as evidence that all is well has a moral evaluation faculty producing incorrect assessments. These secondary dimensions do not compete with the conscience-primary classification; they describe the channels through which conscience suppression operates.

These secondary dimensions describe what the will works through and what shapes its continued refusal; they do not compete with the will-primary classification.

## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Yes — multiple, constituting the characteristic's three VCG registers. (1) *Moral-character dimension* (VCG-01): the condition as wickedness defining the person's moral identity (rish.ah); (2) *Relational-covenantal dimension* (VCG-02): the condition as a standing debt before God within the divine-human relationship — requiring the mediatorial work of forgiveness; (3) *Constitutional-power dimension* (VCG-03): the condition as an indwelling force governing the will, competing with the mind, and producing death. These secondary dimensions do not compete with the total-person primary classification; they each describe a different aspect of what it means for the whole person to be under sin's universal dominion.

## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Two secondary dimensions. (1) *Temporal/historical dimension*: the condition extends across time — "a long time in our sins" (Isa 64:5); the temporal reach backward (to the first father) and forward (to the present and potentially future generations) is a secondary dimension that distinguishes CHAR-15 from merely corporate sin; (2) *Will/unbelief dimension*: Psa 78:32 — "they did not believe" — the unbelief that drives the sustained sinning is a secondary will-level dimension; the generational pattern is not merely structural but is sustained by each generation's own volitional unbelief.

## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Yes — three secondary dimensions. (1) *Social-relational*: VCG-01 — the sinner-identity is expressed and maintained through social categorisation and exclusion (Psa 1:5; Mat 9:10/11; Luk 7:37); (2) *Volitional*: Luk 6:32/33/34 — the sinner's inner orientation is fundamentally transactional and self-directed; the will operates within a self-interest radius; (3) *Eschatological*: Isa 13:9; Psa 104:35; Jude 15 — the sinner-identity carries an eschatological judgment-destination; the person-type is oriented toward divine destruction.

## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Yes — three secondary dimensions. (1) *Subjective weight dimension*: Psa 38:4 — "too heavy for me" — the accumulation is felt; Psa 40:12 — "my heart fails me" — the weight has an experiential dimension secondary to the objective reality; (2) *Social-relational dimension*: Eze 18:20 — the moral crime is between the person and God but also affects the person's standing in the community (Lev 19:8 — "that person shall be cut off from his people"); (3) *Generational-corporate dimension*: VCG-02 (Exo 20:5; Deu 5:9) — the iniquity has a corporate reach across family lines that makes it more than individual.
